1 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs.


SC 19567


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


324 Conn. 292; 152 A.3d 488; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 409


October 13, 2016, Argued 
December 28, 2016*, Officially Released


* December 28, 2016, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Allen v. Conn. Comm'r of Revenue Servs., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 3670 (U.S., June 5, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the defendant denying the plaintiffs' request for the refund of certain income taxes, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, where the court, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon in its favor, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Allen v. Sullivan, 2015 Conn. Super. LEXIS 953 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 29, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Improper form of judgment; judgment directed in part; affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court properly granted summary judgment to the Commissioner of Revenue Services as to nonresident taxpayers' (TPs) request for a refund of certain income taxes in 2002, arising from their exercise of certain nonqualified stock options, as the TPs did not comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-732(a)(1) for purposes of invoking jurisdiction, which was a condition precedent to the limited statutory waiver of sovereign immunity provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-730; [2]-Income from stock options in later years was properly taxed under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 12-711(b)-18(a), as the regulation was properly interpreted to require taxation from a TP who performed services in Connecticut at any point during the taxable year in which the options were granted or exercised; [3]-There was no due process violation by the taxation based on satisfaction of the two-pronged test.


OUTCOME: Judgment directed in part to correct improper form of judgment; affirmed in part.

 

2 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Samuel M.


SC 19578


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


323 Conn. 785; 151 A.3d 815; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 385


October 17, 2016, Argued 
December 27, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Juvenile summons charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, Juvenile Matters at Willimantic, and transferred to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court, where the state filed a substitute information charging the defendant with fourteen counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and with one count of the crime of risk of injury to a child; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Seeley, J.; subsequently, the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to two counts of sexual assault in the first degree; verdict of guilty of risk of injury to a child and three counts of sexual assault in the first degree; thereafter, the court granted in part the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal, denied the defendant's motion to dismiss and to transfer, and rendered judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child and two counts of sexual assault in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Sheldon and Sullivan, Js., which vacated the judgment [***2] of conviction and remanded the matter to the trial court with direction to grant the defendant's motion to dismiss and to transfer the case back to the juvenile docket for further proceedings, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Samuel M., 159 Conn. App. 242, 123 A.3d 44, 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 300 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Once the juvenile defendant challenged the ability of the court to convict and sentence him as an adult based upon his age at the time of the underlying criminal conduct for which the jury returned a guilty verdict, the State bore the burden to prove defendant's age; [2]-In the absence of any testimony as to the order or the specific time period of the individual incidents, a finder of fact could not reasonably infer that the specific incidents occurred after defendant's fourteenth birthday for purposes of transfer to the adult docket under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127(a), which required that defendant's convictions be vacated and the case transferred to the juvenile docket.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the Appellate Court affirmed with respect to vacating defendant's conviction and remanding the case to the trial court with direction to grant defendant's motion to dismiss and to transfer the case to the juvenile docket for new trial.

 

3 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dattco, Inc. v. Comm'r of Transp.


SC 19558


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


324 Conn. 39; 151 A.3d 823; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 386


October 20, 2016, Argued 
December 27, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Actions, in four cases, for injunctive relief in connection with the defendant's condemnation of the plaintiffs' certificates of public convenience and necessity permitting them to operate bus services over certain routes, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Hon. Joseph M. Shortall, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgments in favor of the defendant, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Collins Bus Serv. v. Redeker, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3048 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 4, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Commissioner of Transportation's power to take "facilities" includes the power to take a government issued certificate permitting a bus company the right to operate over a given route. HOLDINGS: [1]-The Commissioner of Transportation's power to take "facilities" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13b-36, did not include the power to take a government issued certificate permitting a bus company the right to operate over a given route, as the certificates did not merely promote the ease of the businesses, but provided the fundamental authority to conduct service; [2]-The text of the provision at issue, § 13b-36, strongly suggested that the term "facilities" referred to tangible assets, not intangible operating rights, as the term was grouped with other nouns denoting tangible objects; [3]-The trial court improperly granted the Commissioner's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

4 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kono


SC 19613


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


324 Conn. 80; 152 A.3d 1; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 396


March 30, 2016, Argued 
December 22, 2016, Officially Released*


* December 22, 2016, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a controlled substance with intent to sell, operating a drug factory, illegal possession of an assault weapon and possession of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Alander, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the charges and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.
State v. Kono, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2867 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 18, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The suppression of evidence seized from defendant's condominium following a canine sniff was proper because the canine sniff violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 7; [2]-A canine sniff directed toward a home, whether freestanding or part of a multi-tenant structure, was a search under Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 and, as such, required a warrant issued upon a court's finding of probable cause; [3]-The assertion that defendant clearly prevailed under the under the federal constitution was rejected because the supreme court simply had no idea how a majority of the members of the United States Supreme Court would decide the issue.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment affirmed.

 

5 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Blakely v. Danbury Hosp.


SC 19461


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


323 Conn. 741; 150 A.3d 1109; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 380


December 9, 2015, Argued 
December 20, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Roraback, J., denied the defendant's motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, which, sua sponte, dismissed the appeal, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Blakely v. Danbury Hosp., 316 Conn. 905, 111 A.3d 471, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 117 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The intermediate appellate court properly dismissed for lack of a final judgment defendant's appeal of the trial court's denial of its motion to dismiss plaintiff's wrongful death suit as time-barred under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555; the trial court's decision that the savings statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-592, saved the otherwise untimely action could not be the subject of an interlocutory appeal under State v. Curcio, because the fact that the applicable statute of limitations was jurisdictional did not mean defendant was immune from suit once it had lapsed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

 

6 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Jayce O.


SC 19669


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


323 Conn. 690; 150 A.3d 640; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 370


September 15, 2016, Argued 
December 8, 2016*, Decided


* December 8, 2016, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition by the Commissioner of Children and Families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, Juvenile Matters at Middletown, and transferred to the Child Protection Session, where the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Barbara M. Quinn, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed.
In re Jayce O., 2015 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2980 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 5, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In terminating a mother's parental rights under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j), the trial court did not violate her procedural due process rights by considering her prior voluntary termination of her rights to another child, as she was provided with sufficient procedural safeguards to protect her fundamental right to parent and every effort was made to assist her in rehabilitating sufficiently in order to be reunified with her child; [2]-As the court found she was neither willing nor able to benefit from the Department's efforts toward reunification, it was not necessary for it to make findings as to whether the Department's efforts were reasonable; [3]-Evidence that she resisted treatment, failed to deal with mental health issues, and denied the effects of her drug use on her ability to parent was sufficient to support the court's finding that she failed to rehabilitate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

7 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bellamy


SC 19337


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


323 Conn. 400; 147 A.3d 655; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 291


December 7, 2015, Argued 
October 25, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and one count each of the crimes of assault in the first degree, criminal possession of a pistol and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Alexander, J.; thereafter, the court granted the state's motion to preclude certain evidence and denied in part the defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence; subsequently, verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Bear and Keller, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Bellamy, 149 Conn. App. 665, 89 A.3d 927, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 169 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant waived his claim that the trial court's identification instruction was erroneous because counsel, having been provided with a draft copy of the jury instructions and a meaningful opportunity to review them and to alert the court to any potential issues, declined to object, and affirmatively expressed his satisfaction with the content of the instructions; counsel explicitly conceded during the sentencing hearing that he had agreed with the substance of the jury instructions before they were given and that his only objection was to the speed with which they had been delivered by the court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

8 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edmonds


SC 19389


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


323 Conn. 34; 145 A.3d 861; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 251


September 10, 2015, Argued 
September 13, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court, Rodriguez, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Arnold, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Alvord and West, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Edmonds, 151 Conn. App. 763, 96 A.3d 607, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 339 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was seized under U.S. Const. amend. IV because defendant was standing alone on private property when two marked police cruisers converged on him from opposite directions, effectively blocking him from exiting the lot, as defendant turned to walk away, he was confronted by a second cruiser, appearing to thwart his passage, and, as a result of the officer's verbal command to stop, defendant stopped and submitted to police authority; [2]-Frisk was not supported by reasonable suspicion under U.S. Const. amend. IV because, although officers testified that they were concerned that defendant might have been carrying a weapon, the only fact they were able to articulate was that defendant moved his hands near his waistband; there was no testimony describing a gun-shaped bulge in the clothing, or an awkward gait or arm movement typical of those carrying concealed guns.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

9 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Newland v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 19381


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 664; 142 A.3d 1095; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 243


October 7, 2015, Argued 
 August 30, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Cobb, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Sheldon, Keller and Harper, Js., which affirmed the habeas court's judgment, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Newland v. Comm'r of Corr., 151 Conn. App. 134, 94 A.3d 676, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 285 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where petitioner claimed his right to counsel was violated because he mistakenly believed he did not qualify for a public defender and only represented himself because he could not afford private counsel, the habeas court erred in finding that his claim of public defender error was not procedurally defaulted, because he alleged error by the trial court, not by the public defender's office, in improperly canvassing petitioner about his waiver of counsel; accordingly, the intermediate appellate court erred in upholding the habeas court's determination; [2]-On remand, the habeas court was to consider whether petitioner's claims of trial court error were procedurally defaulted and, if they were not, it was to consider the claims on their merits.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

10 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gould


SC 19471


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 519; 142 A.3d 253; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 238


May 3, 2016, Argued 
August 16, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the jury before Alander, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Sheldon and Schaller, Js., with Prescott, J., concurring, which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Gould, 155 Conn. App. 392, 109 A.3d 968, 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 48 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant suffered no prejudice from the removal of a juror for cause under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-217 because the juror lacked sufficient proficiency in English; even assuming the English proficiency requirement excluded a cognizable group of nonnative English speakers from jury service, the state's interest in ensuring that jurors were capable of understanding the judicial proceedings was compelling, and the English proficiency requirement was narrowly tailored to serve that interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

11 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dickson


SC 19385


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 410; 141 A.3d 810; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 236


December 11, 2015, Argued 
 August 9, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Connecticut v. Dickson, 137 S. Ct. 2263, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 3883 (U.S., June 19, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of robbery in the first degree and with one count each of the crimes of attempt to commit murder, assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Thim, J., denied the defendant's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter the matter was tried to the jury before Thim, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Keller and Flynn, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Dickson, 150 Conn. App. 637, 91 A.3d 958, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 242 (June 3, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In-court identifications that were not preceded by a successful identification in a nonsuggestive identification procedure implicated due process principles under U.S. Const. amend. V and, therefore, must have been prescreened by the trial court; [2]-Because the victim's in-court identification of defendant was preceded by an unsuccessful attempt to identify defendant in a photographic array, it was a first time in-court identification, and the identification testimony should have been prescreened; [3]-The admission of the victim's in-court identification was harmless because there was no evidence that the accomplice made any material misrepresentations or misstatements during his testimony at trial, the record did not reveal any motive for the accomplice to have falsely identified defendant, and the victim testified that the accomplice was not the person who shot him.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

12 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Shannon v. Comm'r of Hous.


SC 19562


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 191; 140 A.3d 903; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 229


February 23, 2016, Argued 
August 2, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a decision by the defendant terminating the plaintiff's state rental assistance benefits, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Shannon v. Klein, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3213 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 29, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case wherein a tenant's benefits under a state rental assistance program were terminated due to his sex offender status, the Court held that the trial court improperly dismissed the tenant's administrative appeal by retroactively applying Conn. Agencies Regs. § 17b-812-13(9) by imposing a new obligation based on the tenant's sex offender status as nothing in the applicable statutes, regulations, or administrative policies supported the Commissioner of Housing's argument that the tenant's continued participation in the rental assistance program was a time-limited or otherwise tenuous expectation subject to the Commissioner's annual exercise of discretion.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court with direction to sustain the tenant's appeal.

Webb v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 18857


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 187; 140 A.3d 198; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 227


October 22, 2013, Argued 
July 26, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought tothe Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and triedto the court, White, J.; judgment denying the petition, fromwhich the petitioner, on the granting of certification,appealed.
State v. Webb, 252 Conn. 128, 750 A.2d 448, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 19 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court reversed the judgment denying defendant's writ of habeas corpus challenging his death sentence because new case law established that the imposition of the death penalty on defendants sentenced to death for capital felonies committed before the effective date of 2012 Conn. Acts 12-5 would be unconstitutional under the Connecticut constitution.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; judgment directed.

 

14 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saturno


SC 19602


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


322 Conn. 80; 139 A.3d 629; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 198


April 5, 2016, Argued 
July 19, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information in one case charging the defendant with the crime of manufacturing a bomb and substitute information in a second case charging the defendant with the crime of possession of child pornography in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Comerford, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, White, J., in both cases on conditional pleas of nolo contendere; judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress the fruits of an administrative search, which included a bomb and child pornography. HOLDINGS: [1]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-220 authorized the judge to issue an administrative search warrant allowing health officials to search for an illegal apartment in defendant's building after he had refused them entry into his apartment; [2]-The health department's warrant application established probable cause to believe the building was a "multiple dwelling" that violated a city ordinance; [3]-The search and seizure did not violate defendant's rights under Conn. Const. art. I, § 7; [4]-An officer acted reasonably and did not violate defendant's Fourth Amendment rights by breaking a lock to allow city officials to enter the basement, as this was only way they could determine whether there was an illegal apartment there.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

15 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sabato


SC 19406, SC 19407


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


321 Conn. 729; 138 A.3d 895; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 166


December 8, 2015, Argued 
June 28, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of larceny in the fifth degree, attempt to interfere with an officer, and intimidating a witness, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, and tried to the jury before Pavia, J.; verdict of guilty of attempt to interfere with an officer and intimidating a witness; subsequently, the court declared a mistrial as to the charge of larceny in the fifth degree and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Keller and West, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment with respect to the charge of attempt to interfere with an officer and remanded the case with direction to render a judgment of acquittal on that charge and to resentence the defendant on the remaining count, and the state and the defendant, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals with this court.
State v. Sabato, 152 Conn. App. 590, 98 A.3d 910, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 381 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The intermediate appellate court properly reversed defendant's conviction of attempt to interfere with an officer (Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-49(a), 53a-167a) because a text message he sent to a friend instructing him not to cooperate with officers investigating defendant's involvement in a crime did not contain fighting words, and the state did not proceed at trial in the theory that it constituted a threat; [2]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of intimidating a witness (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151a(a)(1)) because it allowed the jury to find he sent threatening messages to the friend after learning he had cooperated with the police; that defendant believed the friend would probably be summoned to testify at an official proceeding; and that defendant, in threatening the friend, intended to influence, delay, or prevent his testimony at a criminal trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

State v. Peeler


SC 18125


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


321 Conn. 375; 140 A.3d 811; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 134


January 7, 2016, Argued 
May 26, 2016, Officially Released*


* May 26, 2016, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.

This case originally was argued before the same panel of justices on July 10, 2014. This court granted the state's request for supplemental argument on November 30, 2015, which was heard on January 7, 2016.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of capital felony and one count each of the crimes of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the guilt phase of the proceedings was tried to the jury before Ford, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, during the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury could not reach a unanimous verdict with respect to either of the two capital felony counts; subsequently, the court, Ford, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and sentenced the defendant to a term of life imprisonment without the possibility of release, and the state and the defendant filed separate appeals with this court; thereafter, this court affirmed the defendant's convictions but reversed the sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of release and remanded the case to the trial court for a new penalty phase hearing; on remand, the jury found the existence of one or more aggravating factors and one or more nonstatutory mitigating factors, and that the aggravating factor or factors outweighed the mitigating factor or factors, and the court, Devlin, [***2] J., rendered judgment imposing two sentences of death, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Peeler, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1826 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 10, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.

 

17 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Connor


SC 19421


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


321 Conn. 350; 138 A.3d 265; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 120


January 26, 2016, Argued 
May 17, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, robbery involving an occupied motor vehicle, larceny in the third degree and stalking in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Espinosa, J., granted the defendant's motion to proceed by self-representation; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury; verdict and judgment of guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, robbery involving an occupied motor vehicle and larceny in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to this court, which remanded the case for further proceedings to determine if the court, Espinosa, J., would have denied the defendant's motion to proceed by self-representation due to mental illness or mental incapacity; thereafter, the court, Schuman, J., after a hearing, determined that the court, Espinosa, J., properly granted the defendant's motion to proceed by self-representation, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Sheldon and Schaller, Js., with Bear, J., concurring and dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment [***2] and remanded the case for a new trial, from which the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Connor, 152 Conn. App. 780, 100 A.3d 877, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 394 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An appellate court abused its discretion by deciding sua sponte defendant's appeal on the basis of an unpreserved issue that had not been raised by the parties without satisfying the requirements articulated in case law requiring the state with a meaningful opportunity to be heard on the dispositive issue and a remand hearing was ordered.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to lower appellate court for further proceedings.

 

18 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. King


SC 19339


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


321 Conn. 135; 136 A.3d 1210; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 99


November 10, 2015, Argued 
May 3, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Prescott, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion for a new trial and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Keller and Bishop, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. King, 149 Conn. App. 361, 87 A.3d 1193, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 143 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was convicted of both intentional and reckless first-degree assault (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1) and (3)), the intermediate appellate court improperly held that the verdict was legally inconsistent, as the jury could have found that defendant initially stabbed the victim while recklessly swinging a knife around and then intentionally stabbed her when she intervened in his conflict with a third party; [2]-Defendant's due process right to notice that he could be convicted of both charges was not violated, because the information charged both offenses, not one or the other; the manner in which the state prosecuted the case did not encourage him to craft his defense in a certain way or to forsake defending against evidence he believed the state would not present; and the trial court instructed the jury to reach a verdict on both charges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

19 of 1861 DOCUMENTS

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT

April 26, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Cobb, J.; judgment granting the petition in part, from which the respondent and the petitioner filed separate appeals to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Alvord and Bishop, Js., which affirmed the habeas court's opinion, and the respondent and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, a new trial was properly granted on a kidnapping charge under Conn. Gen. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Wright


SC 19233, SC 19234


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 781; 135 A.3d 1; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 75


February 10, 2015, Argued 
April 19, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of aggravated sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of conspiracy to commit aggravated sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree, conspiracy to commit kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the third degree, and conspiracy to commit assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Cremins, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of aggravated sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of conspiracy to commit aggravated sexual assault in the first degree, conspiracy to commit kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the third degree, and conspiracy to commit assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Beach, Bear and Sheldon, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to that court with direction to vacate the judgment with respect to two of the conspiracy counts and to resentence the defendant accordingly, and the state and the defendant, on the granting of certification, filed [***2] separate appeals with this court.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Although the evidence excluded was admissible under the rape shield statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86f(4), and the trial court abused its discretion by excluding such evidence, the error was harmless because the defense had available to it other means of directly testing the victim's credibility and the codefendant's testimony refuted the existence of an agreement on the part of the victim to engage in prostitution. OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Brundage


SC 19308


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 740; 135 A.3d 697; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 57


October 8, 2015, Argued 
March 22, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute informations, in two cases, charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the matter was tried to the jury before Crawford, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Robinson and Flynn, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgments and remanded the cases for a new trial; thereafter, the state filed a substitute information in one case charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree; subsequently, the trial court, Fasano, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the substitute information, and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Keller and Borden, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to reinstate the substitute information and for further proceedings, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Brundage, 148 Conn. App. 550, 87 A.3d 582, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 91 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the lower appellate court properly determined that the kidnapping charges in the state's substitute information were not barred by the doctrine of res judicata as res judicata did not apply since the state had filed a substitute information charging new offenses following defendant's successful appeal from judgments of conviction and a remand for a new trial; [2]-The Court noted that the judgments of conviction for sexual assault and risk of injury on which defendant relied in invoking the doctrine had been vacated and had no preclusive effect, and the only valid final judgment that remained was the judgment of the lower appellate Court, which reversed defendant's judgments of conviction, remanded the case to the trial court with direction to dismiss the time barred count of sexual assault, and expressly directed a new trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Maietta


SC 19524


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 678; 134 A.3d 572; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 53


December 16, 2015, Argued 
March 15, 2016, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Baldini, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Baldini, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Maietta, 2015 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1155 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 15, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the trial court properly admitted the handgun found during the search of defendant's garage and the statements he made during the searches of his apartment and the garage as the exclusionary rule was inapplicable to probation revocation proceedings and, contrary to the defendant's characterization of the searches as law enforcement searches, the searches were planned probationary searches to ensure his compliance with the terms of his probation; [2]-The Court further held that defendant could not prevail on his claim that the condition of his probation barring him from possessing firearms contravened his U.S. Const. amend. II right to bear arms as he waived his right when he voluntarily accepted the terms of his probation and, had he been fundamentally opposed to that particular condition, he was free to reject the offer of probation.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

MERSCORP Holdings, Inc. v. Malloy


SC 19376


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 448; 131 A.3d 220; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 25


October 14, 2015, Argued 
February 23, 2016, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Merscorp Holdings v. Malloy, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 6516 (U.S., Oct. 31, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for a judgment declaring the unconstitutionality of certain statutes governing fees charged for the recording of documents in municipal land records, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Sheridan, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Merscorp Holdings, Inc. v. Malloy, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1238 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 19, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-34a(a)(2) and 49-10(h), governing fees imposed for recording mortgage documents in the public land records, violated provisions of the Connecticut and U.S. Constitutions. HOLDINGS: [1]-Although §§ 7-34a(a)(2) and 49-10(h) required plaintiffs' mortgage electronic registration database to pay higher fees that other mortgagees, they did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses of either Constitution because the database was not a suspect class and the statutes were rationally related to the legitimate government purpose of raising revenue and recouping lost fees; [2]-The statutes did not violate the dormant Commerce Clause, as there was no indication that imposing higher fees on nominees of mortgagees that operated national mortgage databases was an attempt to discriminate against out-of-state interests or an effort to favor Connecticut-based companies.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Obas

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 426; 130 A.3d 252; 2016 Conn. LEXIS 37

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the second degree and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the defendant was presented to the court, Mintz, J., on a plea of guilty to sexual assault in the second degree; thereafter, the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the remaining charges and the court, Mintz, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the plea; subsequently, the court, Blawie, J., granted in part the defendant's motion to modify probation and denied the state's request for permission to appeal, and the state appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Sheldon and Flynn, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment only with respect to the denial of the state's request for permission to appeal and affirmed the judgment in all other respects, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the intermediate appellate court erred in affirming the trial court's order granting appellee's application under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-251(b) to be exempted from continued sex offender registration. HOLDINGS: [1]-That appellee had been on the sex offender registry for about seven years did not preclude the exemption, as the plain language of § 54-251(b) indicated that an individual could apply for an exemption from registration at any point during the required period of registration; [2]-A provision in his plea agreement with the state requiring him to register as a sex offender for 10 years did not preclude him from exercising his statutory right to apply for an exemption from registration, as that provision was ambiguous and he did not explicitly waive his right to file an application for an exemption under § 54-251(b).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

January 19, 2016, Officially Released

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Administrative appeal from the decision of the named defendant determining that the plaintiffs did not have standing to seek reconsideration of an order removing a name from the child abuse and neglect registry, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Abrams, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Kolesnik v. State Dep't of Children & Families, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 285 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 31, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an appeal by a child abuse victim challenging a decision that she lacked standing to seek reconsideration of an order removing a name from the child abuse and neglect registry, the Court held that the trial court properly dismissed the victim's claim because she failed to establish that she had a specific, personal and legally protected interest in the substantiation process greater than any other member of the general public; [2]-Ultimately, the statutory scheme under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101k governing the substantiation appeal process, to which alleged victims were not a party, was designed to protect the community and, the victim could not demonstrate that she had a specific, personal and legal interest in the substantiation process for the purpose of statutory aggrievement.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Jones


SC 19097, SC 19098


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


320 Conn. 22; 128 A.3d 431; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 404


April 21, 2015, Argued 
December 22, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit assault in the first degree, assault in the second degree and possession of marijuana, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, geographical area number three, where the court, Pavia, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before the court, Pavia, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Beach and Alvord, Js., which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state and the defendant, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals with this court.
State v. Jones, 139 Conn. App. 469, 56 A.3d 724, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 585 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Prosecutorial improprieties in asking defendant to comment on the veracity of other witnesses and in referring to defendant's response in closing argument did not deprive him of a fair trial, as the improprieties were neither pervasive nor confined to a discrete portion of the trial, the arguably most serious violations concerned a charge of which defendant was acquitted, and because it was apparent that either the victim or defendant was lying, the risks that ordinarily were associated with such a question were not present; [2]-The warrantless retention of a knife beyond the initial, temporary period of safekeeping while defendant was intoxicated was reasonable under the Fourth Amendment because the police lawfully had it in their possession when they obtained probable cause to believe that defendant had used the knife to assault the victim.


OUTCOME: Judgment of Connecticut Appellate Court reversed and case remanded with direction to affirm judgment of trial court.

OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

November 3, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for, inter alia, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Wilson, J., granted the defendant John Murray's motion to strike the counts of the complaint against him; thereafter, the court granted the defendant John Murray's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon in his favor; subsequently, the plaintiff B and B Transportation, Inc., withdrew its claims against the named defendant et al.; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Hon. Thomas J. Corradino, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment in part for the named plaintiff, from which the named defendant et al. appealed to the Appellate Court, Alvord, Bear and Sheldon, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the named defendant et al., on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Gleason v. Smolinski, 149 Conn. App. 283, 88 A.3d 589, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 148 (2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiff sued defendants, who had accused her of involvement in her ex-boyfriend's disappearance, for defamation and IIED, the intermediate appellate court erred in rejecting their unpreserved claim that the First Amendment barred the IIED claim to the extent it was based on their protected conduct in putting up missing person posters; even though their purpose was to hound plaintiff into explaining the disappearance, their conduct pertained to a matter of legitimate public concern and they thus established a constitutional violation under State v. Golding; [2]-With respect to the defamation claim, as defendants' statements related to a matter of public concern, the trial court had been required to determine whether plaintiff met her burden to prove the statements were demonstrably false; as it failed to analyze this issue, defendants were entitled to a new trial.

Trusz v. UBS Realty Investors, LLC


SC 19323


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


319 Conn. 175; 123 A.3d 1212; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 282; 40 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1275; 166 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,639


March 24, 2015, Decided 
October 13, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted, in part, summary judgment denied, in part by Trusz v. UBS Realty, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 39239 (D. Conn., Mar. 25, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to recover damages for the allegedly wrongful termination of the plaintiff's employment, and for other relief, brought to the United States District Court for the District of Connecticut, where the defendants filed a motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the court, Squatrito, J., certified to this court a question of law regarding the interpretation of General Statutes § 31-51q [***1] .
Trusz v. UBS Rlty Investor LLC, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 4464 (D. Conn., Jan. 14, 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Pursuant to a certified question from a federal court, the scope of the protection afforded by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51q to employee speech in the private workplace pursuant to his or her official duties is best addressed by a modified balancing test under the Supreme Court's decisions in Pickering v. Board of Education, 391 U.S. 563, and Connick v. Myers, 461 U.S. 138, wherein the Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4, 5, and 14 principle that speech on all subjects should be protected to the maximum extent possible are balanced against an employer's interests in controlling its own message and preserving workplace discipline, harmony, and efficiency, because it would minimize unilateral governmental interference with employee speech that was compatible with the legitimate interests of employers more effectively than the rigid rule in Garcetti v. Ceballos, 547 U.S. 410.


OUTCOME: Certified question answered negatively.

 

31 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Persels & Assocs., LLC v. Banking Comm'r


SC 19359


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


318 Conn. 652; 122 A.3d 592; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 251


April 23, 2015, Argued 
September 15, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 16, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a declaratory ruling of the defendant interpreting the statutory exemption for Connecticut attorneys engaged in debt negotiation from certain regulatory requirements set forth in General Statutes § 36a-671 et seq. [***1] , and holding that the exemption was inapplicable to the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the court, Prescott, J., rendered judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Persels & Assoc., LLC v. State Dep't of Banking, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 738 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 28, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-As the debt negotiation (DN) services provided by a national law firm from Maryland were inextricably bound with the practice of law under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 2-44A(a) by licensed Connecticut attorneys (CAs) who were regulated exclusively by the Judicial Branch, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36a-671c violated the separation of powers provision of Conn. Const. art. II, § 1 such that it was unenforceable as to CAs engaged in the bona fide practice of law; [2]-Although DN services could be performed by nonattorneys without violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-88, and the legislature could regulate CAs as to entrepreneurial or commercial aspects of the profession of law, when the DN services were performed by CAs within the context of an attorney-client relationship, it constituted the actual practice of law and remained the sole province of the Judicial Branch.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; matter remanded with directions to trial court to render judgment sustaining firm's appeal.

In re Shane M.

318 Conn. 569; 122 A.3d 1247; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 249


October 24, 2014, Argued

34 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Santiago


SC 17413


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


318 Conn. 1; 122 A.3d 1; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 228


April 23, 2013, Argued 
August 25, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Santiago, 319 Conn. 912, 124 A.3d 496, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 290 (2015)
Stay denied by State v. Santiago, 319 Conn. 935, 125 A.3d 520, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 344 (Conn., Oct. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, conspiracy to commit murder, stealing a firearm, and larceny in the sixth degree, and with two counts each of the crimes of burglary in the first degree and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the state filed a notice of the aggravating factor that it intended to prove during the penalty phase of the proceedings and where the defendant filed a notice of mitigating factors; subsequently, the case was tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, during the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found that the state had proven the existence of the aggravating factor beyond a reasonable doubt, at least one or more jurors found that the defendant had proven the existence of one or more mitigating factors by a preponderance of the evidence, and the jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating factor outweighed the mitigating factor or factors; subsequently, the court, Lavine, J., denied the defendant's postverdict motions to impose a life sentence, [***2] to declare the death penalty in this state unconstitutional, to impose a life sentence because of the allegedly arbitrary imposition of the sentence of death in this case, and for an order barring the defendant's execution because of the discriminatory nature of the state's death penalty system, and also denied the defendant's postverdict motions concerning allegedly improper jury deliberations and juror misconduct, and the improper exclusion of a mitigating factor alleged by the defense; thereafter, the court, Lavine, J., rendered judgment of guilty and sentenced the defendant to death by lethal injection and to a consecutive term of imprisonment of forty-five years and ninety days, and the defendant appealed to this court, which reversed in part the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for a new penalty phase hearing; subsequently, this court granted the defendant's motion for reconsideration and ordered supplemental briefing and additional oral argument on the issue of whether legislation enacted after the imposition of the defendant's original sentence barred the imposition of the death penalty in his case.
State v. Santiago, 305 Conn. 101, 49 A.3d 566, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 218 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's death sentence was reversed because following the enactment of 2012 Conn. Acts 5, capital punishment no longer measurably contributed to the legitimate penological goals of deterrence and retribution, and thus, capital punishment in Connecticut violated Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 8 and 9; [2]-In light of the abolition of capital punishment for all future crimes in Connecticut, the death penalty could no longer serve as a deterrent for such crimes, and, even if capital punishment had not been prospectively abolished, the majority of social science research had concluded that the death penalty had no deterrent effect on the homicide rate, primarily because of the substantial delays involved in actually carrying out death sentences.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part. Case remanded to trial court with direction to sentence defendant to life imprisonment without possibility of release on capital felony count.

State v. Miranda


SC 19228


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


317 Conn. 741; 120 A.3d 490; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 218


February 10, 2015, Argued 
August 18, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of capital felony, and with one count each of the crimes of murder, felony murder and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Dewey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of capital felony, murder, felony murder and kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Beach and Borden, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to that court with direction to vacate the defendant's conviction of felony murder and murder, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Miranda, 145 Conn. App. 494, 75 A.3d 742, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 451 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's cumulative convictions and sentences for capital felony, murder, and felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54b(5), 53a-54a(a), and 53a-54c (Rev. to 1987), violated his constitutionally protected right against double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 because they arose from the killing of a single victim; [2]-However, the proper remedy was vacatur of both the murder and felony murder convictions because they were cumulative of the controlling capital felony conviction, the remedy of merger would not consistently protect defendants from the potential collateral consequences of cumulative homicide convictions, and resurrecting a cumulative conviction was a possibility when necessary.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

36 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp.


SC 19131, SC 19132


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


317 Conn. 357; 119 A.3d 462; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 190


September 22, 2014, Argued 
July 7, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for injuries sustained by the plaintiff as a result of the defendant's negligence and recklessness, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket, where the court, Dubay, J., granted the plaintiff's motions to strike the defendant's sixth special defense and to preclude certain expert testimony; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Dubay, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to set aside the verdict, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the court, Dubay, J., awarded the plaintiff punitive damages and rendered judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant filed a separate appeal to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the appeals were consolidated and transferred to this court.
Doe v. Hartford Roman Catholic Diocesan Corp., 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1178 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 2, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiff alleged he was molested by a priest employed by defendant, the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict that defendant had acted negligently, as expert testimony was not required to establish the lay standard of care; [2]-Laches is not an available defense because plaintiff's claim for damages sounded in law, not equity, and was timely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577d; [3]-The retroactive application of amendments to § 52-577d, which revived plaintiff's otherwise time-barred claims, did not violate defendant's substantive due process rights under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 10, as the Connecticut Constitution did not provide greater protection to defendant's interest in the lapse of the statute of limitations than the U.S. Constitution, and the revival of child sexual abuse victims' time-barred claims served a legitimate public interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

37 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Casiano v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 19345


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


317 Conn. 52; 115 A.3d 1031; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 151


September 16, 2014, Argued 
May 26, 2015, Officially Released*


* May 26, 2015, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Semple v. Casiano, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 1826 (U.S., Mar. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Toll and, where the court, Cobb, J., granted the respondent's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon; thereafter, the court denied the petitioner's motion for reconsideration, and the petitioner appealed.
Casiano v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1271 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 30, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the rule announced in Miller was a watershed rule of criminal procedure because it implicated the fundamental fairness and accuracy of a juvenile sentencing proceeding and, therefore, the rule must be applied retroactively under Connecticut law to petitioner's case; [2]-As such, the Court held that the habeas court improperly granted respondent's motion for summary judgment on the ground that Miller did not apply to the petitioner's sentence, as the procedures set forth in Miller must be followed when considering when considering whether to sentence a juvenile offender to fifty years imprisonment without the possibility of parole; [3]-The Court further held that although Connecticut law presumes that a sixty year term of imprisonment is the functional equivalent of a life sentence, a term of years less than the sixty year threshold may be deemed a life sentence for a juvenile offender for the purposes of Miller.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to the habeas court for further proceedings.

 

38 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Martorelli v. DOT


SC 19307


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


316 Conn. 538; 114 A.3d 912; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 102


January 15, 2015, Argued 
April 28, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the decision of the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a livery permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the case was tried to the court, Prescott, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Martorelli v. Conn. DOT, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2826 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 3, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The agency applied the wrong standard of public convenience and necessity (PCN) under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13b-103(a) in denying an applicant's request for a livery service permit as PCN required consideration of the effect certification of a new carrier would have upon the public, not the effect it would have upon existing carriers; [2]-The factors to be considered in analyzing PCN were set forth; [3]-Section § 13b-103(a)(4) did not violate the Equal Protection Clauses, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, as amended by Conn. Const. amend. arts. V and XXI, the Dormant Commerce Clause, or the negative implications of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3; [4]-PCN was not void for vagueness under the Connecticut and Federal Due Process Clauses, Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part. Case remanded with direction.

 

39 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Thiersaint v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 19134


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


316 Conn. 89; 111 A.3d 829; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 90


April 29, 2014, Argued 
April 14, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Cobb, J.; judgment granting the petition, from which the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed.
Thierst v. Warden, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3004 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 7, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the rule in Padilla, wherein it was held that advising noncitizen criminal defendants of possible deportation consequences of a guilty plea fell within the scope of representation required of criminal defense attorneys by U.S. Const. amend. VI, did not apply retroactively; [2]-The court found that the habeas court's decision in the case at bar was released prior to the decision in Chaidez v. United States, wherein that United States Supreme Court subsequently determined that Padilla, by making the Strickland test operative in the context of immigration consequences for the first time, announced a new rule that applied only to future criminal matters or to matters pending on direct appeal when Padilla was decided; [3]-As a result, petitioner could not prevail on his claim that the habeas court's judgment could be affirmed as a matter of state law.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to the habeas court with direction to render judgment denying the amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


 

40 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lapointe v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 19079


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


316 Conn. 225; 112 A.3d 1; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 89


September 17, 2013, Argued 
March 31, 2015, Officially Released*


* March 31, 2015, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Nazzaro, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Appellate Court, Alvord, Bear and Pellegrino, Js., which dismissed the appeal in part, reversed in part the habeas court's judgment, and ordered a new trial, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Lapointe v. Comm'r of Corr., 138 Conn. App. 454, 53 A.3d 257, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 443 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a habeas petitioner's trial rape, murder, and arson, his due process rights were violated because the State failed to disclose a note regarding the length of time that the fire burned at the victim's apartment prior to its discovery, which would have supported the applicant's wife's claim that he was at home watching television at the time the fire was set; [2]-The testimony of two highly regarded and credentialed fire experts regarding the burn time of the fire called into question the reliability of the petitioner's conviction, particularly given the questionable validity of petitioner's statements to police because of his mental disability and the nine-hour interrogation; [3]-The thirty to forty minute minimum burn time, if credited, established that the fire was set at or before 7:50 p.m., a time when the petitioner was watching television with his wife and son.


OUTCOME: Grant of new trial affirmed.

 

41 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor G.


SC 19222


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


315 Conn. 734; 110 A.3d 338; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 62


September 16, 2014, Argued 
March 17, 2015, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute informations in two cases charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the fourth degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Gold, J.; verdicts and judgments of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Goodwin, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 475 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 27, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant juvenile's sentence to the mandatory minimum sentences for first degree sexual assault and risk of injury to a child did not violate the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII, as defendant's sentences were far less severe than the sentences at issue in Roper, Graham and Miller, and given the gravity of the offenses, the age of the victim and the likelihood that the victim would suffer from the effects of the abuse for the rest of his life, the mandatory minimum sentences were not disproportionate. Defendant's youth and immaturity when he committed the crimes were properly considered and defendant's future release at a relatively young age was guaranteed; [2]-The State's expert did not vouch for the victim's credibility; [3]-Defendant did not preserve his claim that the evidence of defendant's prior misconduct when he was 13 years old was improperly admitted.


OUTCOME: The judgments are affirmed.

 

42 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Riley


SC 19109


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


315 Conn. 637; 110 A.3d 1205; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 50


September 16, 2014, Argued 
March 10, 2015, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Conn. v. Riley, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 1825 (U.S., Mar. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of attempt to commit murder and assault in the first degree, and with one count each of the crimes of murder and conspiracy to commit murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Beach and Alvord, Js., with Borden, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Riley, 140 Conn. App. 1, 58 A.3d 304, 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 9 (2013)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a life sentence without parole was properly imposed, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. VIII and XIV, in the exercise of a sentencing authority's discretion on a juvenile homicide defender. HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court was required to have considered defendant's youth and circumstances attendant to his youth as mitigating against the functional equivalent to a life sentence without parole when exercising its sentencing discretion. Defendant was to be afforded a subsequent opportunity to obtain release based on his demonstrated maturity and rehabilitation; [2]-Defendant was entitled to a new sentencing proceeding at which the court was to consider as mitigation defendant's age at the time he committed the offenses and the hallmarks of adolescence deemed constitutionally significant when a juvenile offender was subject to a potential life sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed as to defendant's sentence, and case remanded for a new sentencing proceeding.

In re Emma F.


SC 19417


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


315 Conn. 414; 107 A.3d 947; 2015 Conn. LEXIS 5; 43 Media L. Rep. 1633


December 23, 2014, Argued 
January 22, 2015, Officially Released.*


* January 22, 2015, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking the release of the respondent father's minor children from the custody of the Commissioner of Children and Families, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, and transferred to Juvenile Matters, where the court, Frazzini, J., denied the respondent mother's ex parte motion to prohibit the Connecticut Law Tribune from publishing any information about the matter and ordered that the newspaper be made a party to the action; thereafter, the court issued an oral memorandum of decision enjoining the Connecticut Law Tribune from publishing the contents of the habeas corpus petition, and the Connecticut Law Tribune appealed to the Appellate Court and filed an emergency motion for a stay of the permanent injunction prohibiting it from publishing any information about the case; subsequently, the appeal was transferred to this court; thereafter, the trial court, Frazzini [***1] , J., issued a supplemental decision expanding on its previous oral decision and ordering, inter alia, additional confidentiality restrictions, and scheduled an immediate hearing at which it would consider vacating the injunction, and, following that hearing, [***2] the court vacated the injunction that barred the Connecticut Law Tribune from publishing any information regarding the case that already had been in the public domain, but prohibited the parties from making any further disclosures; following the trial court's order, this court marked over the Connecticut Law Tribune's pending emergency motion for a stay, and ordered the parties to file statements regarding whether the appeal was moot.
In re Emma F., 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1533 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 20, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Review on the merits of a newspaper's appeal from an injunction that prohibited it from publishing information about a child protection case due to confidentiality under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-124 was declined because the injunction had been vacated by the trial court, and the capable of repetition yet evading review exception to the mootness doctrine did not apply; [2]-The newspaper was not entitled to vacatur of the decisions relating to the vacated injunction, as it was somewhat responsible for the events that led to mootness of the case, leaving the decision intact would not result in preclusive consequences to it, and the trial court's decision was devoid of precedential value.


OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.
