State v. Dort


SC 19066


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


315 Conn. 151; 106 A.3d 277; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 466


April 24, 2014, Argued 
December 30, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of burglary in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and strangulation in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Wenzel, J., denied the defendant's motion for a competency evaluation; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Wenzel, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of burglary in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Robinson, Alvord and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Dort, 138 Conn. App. 401, 51 A.3d 1186, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 435 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that the appellate court properly concluded that the trial court had abused its discretion in finding that the allegations made by defense counsel in support of his motion for a competency evaluation for the defendant did not constitute substantial evidence of mental impairment and by not ordering a competency hearing; [2]-The Court found that defense counsel provided multiple, specific representations to the trial court regarding the conduct that led him to believe that further inquiry into the defendant's competency was required and that those representations, if true, suggested both a lack of ability of the defendant to communicate rationally with counsel, and a lack of comprehension by the defendant of the charges that he currently faced; [3]-The Court further agreed with the appellate court that the reversal of defendant's convictions was the appropriate remedy under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.


 

45 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Deciccio


SC 19104


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


315 Conn. 79; 105 A.3d 165; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 447


October 23, 2013, Argued 
December 23, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with six counts of the crime of having a weapon in a motor vehicle, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, geographical area number nine, and tried to the jury before Abrams, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of having a weapon in a motor vehicle, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38 (2009) was not void for vagueness as applied to defendant because the core meaning of the term "dirk knife" could be ascertained from case law in other states and available print reference materials on cutlery; [2]-The statute's ban on having a police baton in a vehicle was not void for vagueness as applied to defendant; [3]-Section 29-38's complete proscription against using a vehicle to transport the two protected weapons deprived their owner of any realistic opportunity either to bring them home after purchase or to move them from one home to another. The statute was not substantially related to the public safety interest because its ban on transporting dirk knives and police batons extended unnecessarily to conduct that was entitled to Second Amendment protection. Section 29-38 was unconstitutional as applied to the facts of the case.


OUTCOME: Conviction reversed. Judgment directed.

 

46 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



State v. Artis


SC 19035


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


314 Conn. 131; 101 A.3d 915; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 308


December 11, 2013, Argued 
October 21, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Amended information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of conspiracy to commit assault in the first degree and with one count each of the crimes of assault in the first degree and assault in the first degree as an accessory, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Hon. John F. Mulcahy, Jr., judge trial referee; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain identification testimony and granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to the charge of assault in the first degree; subsequently, verdict and judgment of guilty of assault in the first degree as an accessory, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop and Peters, Js., with Lavine, J., concurring in part and dissenting in part, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Artis, 136 Conn. App. 568, 47 A.3d 419, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 329 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Harmless error review applied to the admission of unreliable eyewitness identifications that were the product of unnecessarily suggestive procedures; [2]-The State's use of unreliable eyewitness identifications resulting from unduly suggestive police procedures was not one of the rare circumstances necessitating a new trial, as such identification evidence did not inevitably undermine the integrity or legitimacy of the adjudicatory process, but rather, reviewing courts were fully capable of ascertaining whether the admission of such tainted evidence affected the fact finder's ultimate determination; [3]-Even if the admission of the victim's identification testimony was improper, it was harmless in light of a witness's independent identification of defendant, whom she knew, as the individual who initially confronted the victim and as one of the individuals who assaulted him.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

State v. Eleck

Fairwindct, Inc. v. Conn. Siting Council


SC 19090, SC 19091


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


313 Conn. 669; 99 A.3d 1038; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 296


February 21, 2014, Argued 
September 23, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the decisions of the named defendant authorizing the construction of two wind turbine projects in the town of Colebrook by the defendant BNE Energy, Inc., brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss the plaintiffs' appeals and rendered judgments thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Fairwindct, Inc. v. Conn. Siting Council, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2465 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 1, 2012)
Fairwindct, Inc. v. Conn. Siting Council, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2456 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In dismissing plaintiffs' appeal of the Siting Council's authorization of an applicant's construction of wind turbine projects, the trial court properly held the Council had jurisdiction over the applicant's petitions because the projects were "facilities" for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-50x, the Council had jurisdiction to consider state noise law when ruling on the petitions, but had not been required to do so; [4]-The Council's approval of shorter hub heights for one project was supported by substantial evidence; [5]-Any error in the Council's preventing plaintiffs from cross-examining witnesses, issuing protective orders, and denying motions for continuance was harmless.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

50 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Tyriq T.


SC 19153


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


313 Conn. 99; 96 A.3d 494; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 276


March 20, 2014, Argued 
August 19, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition to adjudicate the respondent minor a delinquent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Juvenile Matters, where the court, Eschuk, J., granted the state's motion to transfer the case to the regular criminal docket of the Superior Court, from which the respondent appealed to the Appellate Court, which, sua sponte, dismissed the respondent's appeal for lack of a final judgment, and the respondent, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Tyriq T., 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2828 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 15, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether a trial court's interlocutory order granting a motion seeking a discretionary transfer of defendant juvenile's case to the regular criminal docket pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127(b)(1) (Supp. 2014) was a final judgment; [2]-The appellate court properly dismissed defendant's appeal for lack of a final judgment because the legislature expressed a clear intent to prohibit the immediate appeal of discretionary transfer orders; [3]-Although the text of § 46b-127 did not resolve the question of whether a discretionary transfer order constituted a final judgment, under the statutory language, a discretionary transfer order could not be immediately appealed; [4]-By clearly expressing its intent to prohibit interlocutory appeals of youthful offender transfers, the legislature ensured a consistent interpretation of all of the transfer provisions in § 46b-127.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Kelly


SC 18849


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


313 Conn. 1; 95 A.3d 1081; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 263


April 16, 2013, Argued 
August 12, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics, interfering with an officer, and criminal trespass in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Blue, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Gold, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charge of possession of narcotics with intent to sell; judgment of conviction, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop, Lavine and Borden, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that it was reasonable, and therefore permissible, under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9 for officers to briefly detain a suspect's companion incident to the lawful stop of the suspect when the officers reasonably believe that the suspect presents a threat to their safety; [2]-As such, the Court held that the police were authorized to stop and briefly detain the defendant, as a reasonable safety measure, in connection with the lawful detention of the individual he was accompanying, because the police reasonably believed that that other individual was armed and dangerous.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Johnson


SC 19102


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 687; 94 A.3d 1173; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 253


December 11, 2013, Argued 
July 29, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree and carrying a pistol without a permit, and, in the second part, with criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, B. Fischer, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress a certain identification; thereafter, the first part of the information was tried to the jury before B. Fischer, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the second part of the information was tried to the court; finding of guilty; thereafter, the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the finding, and the defendant appealed.
State v. Johnson, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2138 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 18, 2011)

OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed.


 

53 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



State v. Henderson


SC 19213


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 585; 94 A.3d 614; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 242


March 26, 2014, Argued 
July 22, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of assault in the third degree and one count each of the crimes of robbery in the first degree, criminal mischief in the third degree, threatening, and attempt to escape from custody, and, in the second part, with one count each of being a persistent dangerous felony offender and being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain, where the defendant was presented to the court, Espinosa, J., on a plea of guilty to the crime of criminal mischief in the third degree and where the remaining counts of the first part of the information were tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict of guilty of one count of assault in the third degree and robbery in the first degree, threatening, and attempt to escape from custody; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Espinosa, J., on a plea of guilty to the charges of being a persistent dangerous felony offender and being a persistent serious felony offender; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the pleas, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate [***2] Court, O'Connell, Heiman and Schaller, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment; subsequently, this court denied the defendant's petition for certification to appeal; thereafter, the court, Gold, J., dismissed the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Bear and Borden, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the motion and remanded the case with direction to deny the defendant's motion, and the defendant appealed to this court; subsequently, the court, Dewey, J., rendered judgment denying the defendant's second motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed; thereafter, this court dismissed the defendant's prior appeal on the ground that certification had been improvidently granted.
State v. Henderson, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3512 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 26, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence was properly denied on the alternative ground that the trial judge made the necessary finding that imposing an enhanced sentence would best serve the public interest, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(f), (g) (1993); it was implicit in the trial judge's remarks regarding defendant's serious and violent criminal history, and in her statement that she had no alternative but to impose a lengthy sentence, that she found that an enhanced sentence would best serve the public interest.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.


 

54 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mueller v. Tepler


SC 18939


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 631; 95 A.3d 1011; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 251


December 3, 2013, Argued 
July 16, 2014, Officially Released*


* July 16, 2014, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for the defendants' alleged medical malpractice, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the plaintiff amended her complaint to add loss of consortium claims by the plaintiff Charlotte Stacey; thereafter, the court, Tobin, J., granted the defendants' motions to strike counts two, four, six, and eight of the third amended complaint; subsequently, the court, Karazin, J., granted the motion for judgment as to counts six and eight filed by the defendant Iris Wertheim et al., and rendered partial judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff Charlotte Stacey appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Bear and Schaller, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the plaintiff Charlotte Stacey, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Mueller v. Tepler, 132 Conn. App. 742, 33 A.3d 814, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 616 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a medical malpractice action, the Court held that it recognizes, as a matter of public policy based on the changing attitudes and needs of society, the right to maintain a loss of consortium claim should be expanded to same sex couples who can prove that they would have been married as of a particular date if their marriage had not been barred; [2]-The Court held that because plaintiffs in the case at bar could not have been married before the date of the tortious conduct even if they had the requisite commitment and desire, and because the bar on same sex marriage was inconsistent with public policy, it would be illogical and inequitable to require proof that plaintiffs were actually married when the underlying tort occurred as a prerequisite to allowing the partner to bring her loss of consortium claims.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to appellate court with direction to reverse the trial court's judgment in favor of defendants on the partner's loss of consortium claims and to remand the case to the trial court affirming that ruling on the motion to strike, but with direction to allow the partner to amend her complaint, and, in the event that the partner does amend her complaint, for further proceedings.

Gen. Stat. § 12-391 amounted to an unconstitutional taking of the taxpayer's property.

Taylor v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 18981


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 215; 91 A.3d 898; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 156


December 4, 2013, Argued 
June 17, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the petitions were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Solomon, J., rendered judgments dismissing the petitions and denied the petition for certification to appeal; subsequently, the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the petitioner filed additional petitions for a writ of habeas corpus, and the court, Solomon, J., and T. Santos, J., declined to issue a writ of habeas corpus and denied the petitions for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, which consolidated the appeals; subsequently, the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Beach and West, Js., dismissed the appeals, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Taylor v. Comm'r of Corr., 134 Conn. App. 405, 40 A.3d 336, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 151 (2012)

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The appellate court properly upheld the habeas court's denial of the inmate's petition as frivolous under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book R. Super. Ct. §§ 23-42 and 23-41 because the inmate could have sought appellate review of the dismissal of his petitions. Although the inmate challenged the appellate court's conclusion that the habeas court was not constitutionally required to provide him with an evidentiary hearing before dismissing his habeas petitions, the appeal was dismissed on the ground that certification was improvidently granted.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

57 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Single Source, Inc. v. Cent. Reg'l Tourism Dist., Inc.


SC 18819


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 374; 93 A.3d 1065; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 205


September 19, 2013, Argued 
July 8, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action to recover damages for breach of contract, brought to the United States District Court for the District of Massachusetts, where the defendant filed a motion for summary judgment and where the court, Saylor, J., certified to this court certain questions of law.
Single Source, Inc. v. Cent. Reg'l Tourism Dist., Inc., 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 52784 (D. Mass., May 17, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiff sued defendant regional tourism district (RTD) under a contract plaintiff had executed with a local tourism district (LTD); the United States District Court for the District of Massachusetts certified this question: Was defendant the legal successor to the LTD? The high court held the statutory scheme indicated the legislature did not intend to make the RTDs the legal successors to the LTDs, but allowed the RTDs to choose whether to assume the LTDs' obligations; [2]-As to the third certified question--Which entity, if any, was responsible for the LTD's obligations?--as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-397a required the LTD to account for its liabilities before distributing its cash assets, if it transferred assets to defendant and rendered itself unable to pay its debt to plaintiff, then plaintiff could be entitled to hold defendant responsible for the LTD's obligations.


OUTCOME: The first question was answered in the negative, the second question was moot, and as to the third, if plaintiff could establish that the LTD fraudulently conveyed its assets to defendant, defendant could be responsible for the LTD's obligations to the extent of the value of the assets received.

 

58 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Frank v. Dep't of Children & Families


SC 18980


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


312 Conn. 393; 94 A.3d 588; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 204


December 2, 2013, Argued 
July 8, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Administrative appeal from the decision by the defendant substantiating allegations of emotional abuse by the plaintiff and placing the plaintiff's name on the defendant's child abuse and neglect central registry, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, Beach, Alvord and Pellegrino, Js., which reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to that court with direction to render judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal and for further proceedings, from which the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Frank v. Dep't of Children & Families, 134 Conn. App. 288, 37 A.3d 834, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 140 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In reversing the trial court's order dismissing a teacher's appeal from the Department of Children and Families' (DCF's) decision substantiating allegations of the teacher's emotional abuse of a student and placing his name on the central child abuse and neglect registry, the intermediate appellate court erred in substituting its findings for those of DCF; the hearing officer's findings that the teacher had emotionally abused the student were supported by substantial evidence; [2]-The intermediate appellate court erred in finding Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-120(3)'s definition of "abused" void for vagueness as applied, since DCF's policy manual, related statutes, and case law gave the teacher fair notice that his conduct, including calling the student names and pinching his cheeks, could qualify as emotional abuse that might lead his name to be placed on the central registry.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

 

59 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Elson


SC 18737


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


311 Conn. 726; 91 A.3d 862; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 140


September 24, 2012, Argued 
June 3, 2014, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of assault in the first degree, attempt to commit assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree, and, in the second part, with having committed an offense while on pretrial release, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Schuman, J.; verdict of guilty of assault in the first degree and unlawful restraint in the first degree; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Schuman, J., on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Harper and Dupont, Js., with Bishop, J., dissenting in part, which affirmed the trial court's judgment; subsequently, the Appellate Court granted the defendant's motion for reconsideration and reargument en banc, and that court, DiPentima, C. J., and Gruendel, Harper, Beach, Robinson, Alvord and Dupont, Js., with Bishop and Lavine, Js., dissenting in part, again affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on [***2] the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Elson, 125 Conn. App. 328, 9 A.3d 731, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 545 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The intermediate appellate court erred by refusing State v. Golding review of defendant's unpreserved claim that the trial court penalized him for exercising his right to a jury trial. His failure to address in his brief issues related to the claim's reviewability, to request any extraordinary level of review, to refer to Golding, to address the adequacy of the record to review the claim, or to argue that the claim should be reviewed even if unpreserved, did not preclude consideration of his constitutional claim; [2]-State v. Ramos and its progeny were reversed to the extent they required a defendant to affirmatively request such review or imparted a threshold level of analysis of entitlement to review under Golding; [3]-Though defendant did not show he was penalized for exercising his right to a jury trial, resentencing was required to avoid the perception of unfairness.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed.

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


311 Conn. 626; 88 A.3d 534; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 104

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]

I, § 7, but instead reaffirmed its settled jurisprudence allowing police officers with probable cause to search any and all containers located in a vehicle that properly was subject to a warrantless on-the-scene automobile search.


OUTCOME: judgment is affirmed.

State v. Davis

SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


311 Conn. 468; 88 A.3d 445; 2014 Conn. LEXIS 100

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Holden, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a plea of guilty to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict and the plea, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Alvord, Espinosa and Pellegrino, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

In re Elvin G.


SC 19108


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


310 Conn. 485; 78 A.3d 797; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 378


March 18, 2013, Argued 
November 12, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petitions by the Commissioner of Children and Families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to certain of their minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters, and tried to the court, Epstein, J.; judgments terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent father appealed.
In re Elvin G., 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2529 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court erred in concluding that parental rights could be terminated pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(3)(B)(i) without the prior provision of specific steps toward rehabilitation, as such steps were required in any case in which the Commissioner of Children and Families sought to terminate parental rights on the ground of failure to rehabilitate; [2]-However, the error was harmless in the particular circumstances with respect to a father's parental rights over two of his children, as the trial court's finding of failure to rehabilitate was based on his long-term and ongoing inability to provide financial, physical, and emotional support to his children in addition to his incarceration, such that provision of the steps would not have made a difference.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed.

 

63 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moulton


SC 18632


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


310 Conn. 337; 78 A.3d 55; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 348


September 18, 2012, Argued 
October 29, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of breach of the peace in the second degree and harassment in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, geographical area number twenty-one, and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Beach and Robinson, Js., with McDonald, J., concurring in part and dissenting in part, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to that court for a new trial on the charge of breach of the peace in the second degree and with direction to render judgment of not guilty on the charge of harassment in the second degree, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Moulton, 120 Conn. App. 330, 991 A.2d 728, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 139 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; improper form of judgment; judgment directed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State could not prosecute defendant under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-183(a) because she did not have fair notice that she could be subjected to punishment solely on the basis of the content of her speech; [2]-The content of a person's communications, in and of itself, could not subject him or her to prosecution, either for an alarming or harassing telephone call or for an alarming or harassing mailing; [3]-Thus, defendant reasonably could not have anticipated that she could be found to have violated the statute on the basis of statements that she made during a telephone conversation, and she was entitled to rely on precedent holding that the content of one's communications could not be used as substantive evidence of that offense; [4]-.Because the State's case against defendant was founded entirely on the content of her speech, she was entitled to a dismissal of the charge.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and case remanded to render judgment dismissing charge.

Chief Info. Officer v. Computers Plus Ctr., Inc.


SC 19029, SC 19030, SC 19031


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


310 Conn. 60; 74 A.3d 1242; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 296


January 3, 2013, Argued 
September 3, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract and fraud in connection with the procurement of a contract pursuant to which the defendants were to provide computer equipment to the state, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the defendants filed several counterclaims, and transferred to the Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the court, Shortall, J., denied the plaintiffs' motion to dismiss the counterclaims; subsequently, the matter was transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket, and tried to the jury before Stevens, J.; following the plaintiffs' withdrawal of five counts of the complaint, the court, Stevens, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for a directed verdict on one count of the defendants' counterclaims; thereafter, verdict in part for the plaintiffs and verdict in part for the defendants on the complaint and on the counterclaims; subsequently, the court, Stevens, J., denied the plaintiffs' motions to set aside the verdict as to the complaint, and the plaintiffs appealed; thereafter, the court, Stevens, J., denied the plaintiffs' motions to dismiss and to set aside  [***2] the verdict as to the defendants' counterclaims, and granted the plaintiffs' motion to reduce the verdict award on the procedural due process counterclaim and ordered a new trial on that counterclaim if the defendants failed to accept the remittitur within a specific period of time, and the plaintiffs filed a second appeal and the defendants filed a cross appeal; subsequently, the court, Stevens, J., set aside the defendants' verdict on the procedural due process counterclaim and rendered judgment in accordance with the verdicts, and ordered a new trial on that counterclaim as to damages only, and the plaintiffs filed a third appeal and the defendants filed a cross appeal.
Regan v. Computers Plus Ctr., Inc., 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1435 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 11, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; judgment directed; cross appeals dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-That plaintiffs, the Connecticut Department of Information Technology and its Chief Information Officer, sued a private company for breach of contract and fraud did not result in Connecticut's waiving its sovereign immunity as to the company's counterclaims for money damages based on an alleged procedural due process violation; [2]-As the company failed to present its counterclaims for damages to the Connecticut Claims Commissioner and failed to obtain legislative permission to being an action against plaintiffs pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the counterclaims; [3]-The company president's testimony about criminal charges against her was properly admitted because it was relevant to the company's procedural due process counterclaim by showing that it was harmed by false statements the Department made to police.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part and affirmed in part.

A. Gallo & Co. v. Comm'r of Envtl. Prot.


SC 18764


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


309 Conn. 810; 73 A.3d 693; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 397


January 2, 2013, Argued 
August 20, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by A. Gallo & Co. v. Esty, 134 S. Ct. 1540, 188 L. Ed. 2d 581, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 1972 (U.S., Mar. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for, inter alia, a judgment declaring unconstitutional certain legislation requiring the plaintiffs to pay to the state's general fund the value of the unclaimed beverage container deposits that they had collected during a certain four month period, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Domnarski, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment as to liability and denied the defendants' motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the court, Miller, J., granted the motion to intervene filed by Adirondack Beverages Corporation et al.; subsequently, the court, Domnarski, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, rendered judgment awarding the plaintiffs damages and the named plaintiff et al. attorney's fees, and the defendants appealed and the named plaintiff et al. cross appealed; thereafter, the named plaintiff et al. withdrew the cross appeal.
A. Gallo & Co. v. McCarthy, 51 Conn. Supp. 425, 2 A.3d 56, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 984 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in granting plaintiff beverage distributors summary judgment in their suit challenging the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-245a(d) (Supp. 2010), which required them to pay the State the value of unclaimed beverage container deposits they had collected in the four months prior to § 22a-245a(d)'s enactment. The retroactive provision of § 22a-245a(d) did not result in an unconstitutional taking of plaintiffs' property; they had no vested property interest in the unclaimed deposits because their right to use and control them was severely limited by the regulatory scheme.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

66 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Conn. Med. Examining Bd.


SC 18843


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


309 Conn. 727; 72 A.3d 1034; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 270


March 14, 2013, Argued 
August 13, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the defendant reprimanding and imposing fines and other discipline on the plaintiff in connection with his license to practice medicine, brought in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, and tried to the court, Schuman, J.; judgment sustaining the plaintiff's appeal in part, from which the plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Bishop and Gruendel, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Jones v. Conn. Med. Examining Bd., 129 Conn. App. 575, 19 A.3d 1264, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 343 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the applicable standard of proof in a physician disciplinary proceeding before the Connecticut Medical Examining Board was the preponderance of the evidence standard rather than clear and convincing evidence. HOLDINGS: [1]-The preponderance of the evidence standard applied at the proceeding before the Board, an administrative agency within the meaning of the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act; [2]-The use of the preponderance of the evidence standard did not offend the physician's due process rights; [3]-The Board's procedures adequately protected against an unacceptable risk of error; [4]-The governmental interest weighed in favor of maintaining the preponderance of the evidence standard because a heightened standard of proof would necessarily render it more difficult for the state to protect the public from unsafe medical practitioners.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

In re Azareon Y.


SC 19087


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


309 Conn. 626; 72 A.3d 1074; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 264


May 16, 2013, Argued 
July 30, 2013, Officially Released**


** July 30, 2013, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petitions by the commissioner of children and families to terminate the respondents' parental rights with respect to their minor children, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Juvenile Matters, and tried to the court, Cofield, J.; judgments terminating the respondents' parental rights, from which the respondent mother appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavine, Robinson and Espinosa, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgments, and the respondent mother, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
In re Azareon Y., 139 Conn. App. 457, 60 A.3d 742, 2012 Conn. App. LEXIS 559 (2012)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case involving the termination of parental rights, the mother's unpreserved constitutional claim concerning the least restrictive means necessary to ensure the State's compelling interest in protecting the children's safety and well-being (best interests), was unreviewable because the record was inadequate. The record was also ambiguous as to whether the trial court concluded that the petitioner proved by clear and convincing evidence that termination was the only option available to satisfy the best interests of the children.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

68 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Medrano


SC 18895


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


308 Conn. 604; 65 A.3d 503; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 158


February 6, 2013, Argued 
May 21, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and carrying a dangerous weapon, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of intentional manslaughter in the first degree and carrying a dangerous weapon, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Robinson and Mihalakos, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Medrano, 131 Conn. App. 528, 27 A.3d 52, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 474 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted on a jury verdict of first-degree intentional manslaughter and carrying a dangerous weapon; he appealed. The Appellate Court of Connecticut affirmed; he sought further review.


OVERVIEW: During a fight, defendant stabbed the victim with a pocket knife defendant was carrying. He argued that he was deprived of his due process right to a fair trial due to prosecutorial misconduct during his cross-examination and the closing argument. The high court held that the prosecutor improperly insinuated that defendant had started the fight, as this was not based on reasonable inferences from the facts. Her statements that defendant acted as the victim's "judge, jury and executioner," and that, if the jurors believed his testimony, she had a "bog in Ireland" she would like to sell them, were also improper. However, these improper statements did not deprive defendant of a fair trial, as defense counsel's failure to object to them indicated that counsel did not regard them as seriously prejudicial, and the state's case was strong. An instruction regarding defendant's interest in the outcome of the case was proper as it was not unduly repetitive and did not transcend the bounds of evenhandedness. But in the future, courts should refrain from instructing jurors, when a defendant testified, that they could consider his interest in the outcome of the trial and its importance to him.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

69 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Polanco


SC 18771


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


308 Conn. 242; 61 A.3d 1084; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 121


September 17, 2012, Argued 
April 2, 2013, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 27, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of drug paraphernalia, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, and tried to the jury before Oliver, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Alvord and Mihalakos, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to merge the two convictions of possession of narcotics and to vacate the sentence on the conviction of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Polanco, 126 Conn. App. 323, 11 A.3d 188, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 37 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed, in part, a judgment of the trial court that convicted him of various drug possession offenses. The Appellate Court remanded the matter with directions to merge two possession of narcotics convictions, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b) and 21a-277(a), and to vacate the sentence on the conviction of possession of narcotics with intent to sell (PNIS).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple drug possession offenses. After a jury trial, he was convicted of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b), 21a-277(a), and 21a-267. The trial court imposed concurrent terms of imprisonment on the PNIS convictions. The Appellate Court concluded that defendant was sentenced for both a greater and lesser included offense that arose from the same transaction, which ran afoul of the prohibition against double jeopardy under U.S. Const. amend. V. Applying the merger of convictions approach, it directed that the PNIS convictions were to be merged, and that the sentence on the lesser offense under § 21a-277 was to be vacated. On further review, the court exercised its inherent supervisory authority over the administration of justice rather than relying on amend. V. It found that the proper remedy for defendant's convictions of greater and lesser included offenses was to vacate the conviction for the lesser included offense rather than merge it. The court accordingly overruled State v. Chicano, 584 A.2d 425 (1990), to the extent that it applied the merger of convictions approach for a defendant convicted of greater and lesser included offenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the Appellate Court with respect to its order to the trial court to merge defendant's PNIS convictions. The court remanded the matter to the Appellate Court with directions for reversal as noted, and to remand the case to the trial court with directions to vacate the conviction for the lesser included offense of PNIS. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

70 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kumah v. Brown


SC 18777


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 620; 58 A.3d 247; 2013 Conn. LEXIS 1


September 25, 2012, Argued 
January 22, 2013, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, personal injuries sustained by the named plaintiff as a result of the alleged negligence of the named defendant et al., and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Bellis, J., granted the motion filed by the defendant town of Greenwich to strike certain counts of the plaintiffs' complaint; thereafter, the court granted the town's motion for judgment on those counts; subsequently, the court, Arnold, J., granted the town's motion to strike certain other counts of the plaintiffs' amended complaint, granted the plaintiffs' motion for judgment on those counts, and rendered judgment for the defendant town of Greenwich et al., from which the plaintiffs appealed to the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Robinson and Borden, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment, and the town, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Kumah v. Brown, 127 Conn. App. 254, 14 A.3d 1012, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 110 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed a judgment that had stricken the nuisance claims filed by plaintiffs, an injured motorist and spouse, after they sued defendant town. They had done so after his vehicle struck a town fire truck parked across two lanes on an interstate highway in the town while rescue personnel were responding to an accident. The state supreme court granted the town's request for certification to review the case.


OVERVIEW: The town's rescue personnel responded to an accident. In doing so, they parked the town's fire truck across two lanes of an interstate highway. Shortly thereafter, the injured motorist, who had been driving his automobile on the interstate highway, collided with the parked fire truck. The injured motorist and spouse sued, inter alia, the town and claimed the fire truck was a nuisance. The town moved to strike. The trial court granted the motion based on the appellate court's Himmelstein decision. The appellate court reversed. The state supreme court found that Himmelstein could be distinguished. It so concluded because it found that recovery by the injured motorist and spouse was not barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n(a)(1) that limited claims involving damages arising out of a defective road or bridge filed against a municipality to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149, the municipal highway defect statute. It then explained that the injured motorist and spouse had not alleged the roadway at issue was one which the town was obligated to keep in repair since it was an interstate highway and, thus, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-149 did not provide the exclusive means of recovery for them.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

 

71 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


O'Dell v. Kozee


SC 18851


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 231; 53 A.3d 178; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 350


April 18, 2012, Argued 
September 28, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 28, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged wrongful death of the plaintiff's decedent, brought to the Superior court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Tanzer, J., granted the plaintiff's motion to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Tanzer, J.; verdict for the plaintiff; subsequently, the court denied the defendants' motion to set aside the verdict and for a directed verdict, and granted the defendants' motion to reduce the verdict, and rendered judgment for the plaintiff in accordance with the reduced verdict, from which the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, C. J., and Beach and Bear, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to that court with direction to render judgment for the defendants, and the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
O'Dell v. Kozee, 128 Conn. App. 794, 19 A.3d 672, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 285 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator filed a wrongful death suit against defendants, a restaurant and its permittee, alleging the restaurant violated Connecticut's Dram Shop Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 30-102. A jury returned a verdict for plaintiff; defendants appealed. The Connecticut Appellate Court it reversed and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment for defendants. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: A patron consumed several alcoholic drinks at the restaurant, but no one saw him exhibiting any obvious physical signs of intoxication. As he was driving the decedent home, he caused an auto accident in which the decedent was killed. The patron had a blood alcohol content (BAC) of 0.187 shortly after the accident. Plaintiff's expert opined that the patron would have had to have consumed between 15-20 drinks to have reached that BAC. The intermediate appellate court held that 1) plaintiff had the burden to prove the patron was visibly or otherwise perceivably intoxicated at the time he was sold liquor, and 2) as plaintiff failed to meet that burden, defendants were entitled to judgment in their favor. The high court agreed with the first holding, but not the second. As plaintiff's failure to present evidence of the patron's visible or perceivable intoxication was due to the trial court's pretrial ruling that this evidence was not required, plaintiff had to be afforded an opportunity to produce such evidence at a new trial. He had to prove only that signs of intoxication could have been observed, not that they would have been obvious.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed as to its holding regarding plaintiff's burden of proof, but was reversed as to its order that the trial court render judgment for defendants. The case was remanded to the intermediate appellate court with direction to remand the case to the trial court for a new trial.

State v. LaFleur


SC 18757


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 115; 51 A.3d 1048; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 352


November 28, 2011, Argued 
September 28, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 28, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by State v. Lafleur, 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 123 (Conn. App. Ct., Mar. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information, in one case, charging the defendant with one count of the crime of assault in the third degree and three counts of the crime of violating a protective order, and substitute two part information, in a second case, charging the defendant in the first part with one count each of the crimes of assault in the first degree and violation of the conditions of release in the first degree, and in the second part with being a persistent dangerous felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Holden, J., granted the state's motion to consolidate the cases; thereafter, the cases were tried to the jury before Holden, J.; verdict of guilty in the first case of one count of assault in the third degree and two counts of violating a protective order, and verdict of guilty in the second case of one count each of assault in the first degree and violation of the conditions of release in the first degree; subsequently, the defendant pleaded guilty to being a persistent dangerous felony offender and the court rendered judgments of guilty in accordance with the verdicts and the plea, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed  [***2] in part; affirmed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was accused of assaulting his former girlfriends in two separate incidents; the cases were consolidated. After a jury trial in the Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), he was convicted of third-degree assault, first-degree assault, first-degree violation of the conditions of release, and two counts of violating a protective order; he pled guilt to being a persistent dangerous felony offender. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Both girlfriends testified that defendant punched them in the face; girlfriend two sustained multiple facial fractures. He argued that his conviction in the second case of first-degree assault with respect to girlfriend two had to be reversed because the trial court erred in instructing the jury that a fist could be a "dangerous instrument." The high court agreed. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-3(7) and 53a-59(a)(1), a "dangerous instrument" was limited to tools and implements that were external to, and separate and apart from, the perpetrator's body. As defendant's fists alone caused girlfriend two's facial fractures, there was insufficient evidence to prove he committed first-degree assault. The high court could not modify the conviction to the lesser included offense of second-degree assault, as there had been no jury charge regarding that offense. Joinder of the two cases did not deny defendant his right to a fair trial under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as 1) his alleged conduct was the same in both cases--punching young women in the face; 2) his alleged conduct in the second case was not "shocking"; and 3) some evidence was admissible in both cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment in the second case was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to render judgment of acquittal on all counts in that case. The judgment in the first case was affirmed, but the sentence was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to resentence defendant in accordance with the high court's opinion.

State v. Dyous


SC 18871


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 299; 53 A.3d 153; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 349


March 19, 2012, Argued 
September 28, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 28, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition by the state for the continued commitment of the defendant, who had been found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of two counts each of the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree and threatening in the second degree, and one count of the crime of carrying a dangerous weapon, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, where the court, Swords, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss the petition; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, which rendered judgment granting the state's petition for continued commitment, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Dyous, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 682 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 19, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham (Connecticut) which granted the State's petition for an order of continued commitment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c). Defendant had been under the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-582 following his acquittal by reason of mental disease or defect of kidnapping in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Approximately one year before the end of defendant's 25-year term, the State petitioned for continued commitment, arguing that he remained mentally ill and that his discharge from the jurisdiction of the board would constitute a danger to himself or others. The trial court ordered that defendant be committed to the jurisdiction of the board for an additional three years. Defendant's principal claim was that § 17a-593, which set out the continued commitment procedure that was applicable to insanity acquittees, violated his federal constitutional right to equal protection. The appellate court rejected defendant's claim that § 17a-593 was unconstitutional as applied to him because subjecting defendant to a recommitment procedure that tilted more strongly in favor of commitment than did its civil counterpart substantially related to the achievement of the important governmental interest of protecting society. It also comported with common sense to conclude that someone whose mental illness was sufficient to lead him to commit a dangerous crime and had persisted despite years of intensive treatment, was someone whose prospective release raised a special concern for public safety.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Bernacki


SC 18674


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 1; 52 A.3d 605; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 348


January 9, 2012, Argued 
September 26, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 26, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bernacki v. Connecticut, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 2968 (U.S., Apr. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of a machine gun, criminal possession of a firearm and criminal violation of a protective order, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number five, and tried to the jury before, Cronan, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of criminal possession of a firearm and criminal violation of a protective order, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Flynn, C. J., and Beach and West, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Bernacki, 122 Conn. App. 399, 998 A.2d 262, 2010 Conn. App. LEXIS 294 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of criminal possession of a firearm, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217(a)(3)(A), and criminal violation of a protective order, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-223(a). The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the convictions, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said his convictions arising from the same act violated double jeopardy. The supreme court disagreed because (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-217(a)(3)(A) and 53a-223(a) were not the "same offense" under Blockburger, when confining the analysis to the statutes and charging documents, without regard to the evidence at trial, including the protective order at issue, as each statute had an element requiring proof of a fact the other did not, and (2) defendant did not rebut the presumption that the legislature intended to allow convictions and punishments for violations of both statutes, as the statutory scheme lacked language expressly indicating the legislature intended to bar multiple punishments for violating both statutes based on the same act, and nothing in the legislative history of either statute clearly indicated the legislature's intent to bar multiple convictions and punishments for violations of the statutes arising from the same conduct. It was error for the Appellate Court to find defendant could not have committed one of the crimes without committing the other because this focused on the facts of the case, rather than a technical analysis of statutory elements.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Republican Party of Conn. v. Merrill


SC 19010


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


307 Conn. 470; 55 A.3d 251; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 442


September 12, 2012, Argued 
September 26, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 26, 2012, the date that we issued the decision in this case as an order, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a declaratory judgment to determine whether by statute the plaintiff's candidates for office in the November, 2012 election are required to be listed first on the ballot, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court for the judicial district of Hartford, where the parties entered into a joint stipulation of facts and the court, Graham, J., granted the parties' motion to reserve two questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Republican Party of Connecticut brought a declaratory judgment action to determine that, because its candidate for the office of governor in the last election received the highest number of votes under the designation of the Republican Party line on the ballot, defendant Secretary of the State was required to list the Republican Party candidate first on the ballots for the current election pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-249a(a).


OVERVIEW: The Secretary of the State contended that the Republican Party was required pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176 to request from the Secretary of the State a declaratory ruling on the meaning and proper application of § 9-249a before the Republican Party could bring an action in the trial court. The Supreme Court of Connecticut held that, prior to bringing an action in the trial court, the Republican Party was required to exhaust its administrative remedies by requesting a declaratory ruling from the Secretary of the State. The Republican party exhausted its administrative remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176 because its letter to the Secretary of the State constituted a request for a declaratory ruling on the applicability to specified circumstances of a provision of the General Statutes. Because the Republican Party's gubernatorial candidate received more votes on his party's line in the prior election than the Governor received on either the Democratic Party or the Working Families Party lines, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-249a directed the Secretary of the State to place the Republican Party at the top of the ballot in the current general election.


OUTCOME: The Court held that § 9-249a was an ambiguous statute, and that the legislative history, genealogy, and public policy all supported a construction requiring the party whose candidate for governor polled the highest number of votes on that party's line be given precedence on the ballot in the subsequent general election. The Republican Party candidate was to be placed at the top of the ballot.

State v. Ward


SC 18897


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


306 Conn. 718; 51 A.3d 970; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 344


March 19, 2012, Argued 
September 18, 2012, Officially Released*


* September 18, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, where the matter was tried to a jury before Swords, J.; verdict of guilty, thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal and rendered judgment of not guilty as to the charge of kidnapping in the first degree and guilty as to the charge of sexual assault in the first degree, and the state, on the granting of permission, appealed.
State v. Ward, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2533 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 9, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury found defendant guilty of first-degree kidnapping (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A)) and first-degree sexual assault, the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Windham (Connecticut) granted defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the kidnapping charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed a woman in her kitchen, held a tool to her neck, dragged her down a hallway, and moved her to a bedroom, where he raped her. The trial court granted his motion for judgment of acquittal on the kidnapping charge on the ground the State failed to prove he intended to prevent the victim's liberation for a longer period of time or to a greater degree than that which was necessary to commit the sexual assault. The high court disagreed. The jury could have reasonably found that his confinement and movement of the victim exceeded that which was necessary to sexually assault her, increased the risk of harm to her, and were intended to impede her ability to escape or summon help. The terms "restrain" and "abduct" in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-91(1) and (2) were not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct, as he had fair warning in 1988, when he committed the crimes, that his movement of the victim while he was sexually assaulting her could constitute the basis for an independent kidnapping conviction. The trial court's kidnapping instructions were not misleading but properly informed the jury of the elements of the offense and the State's burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the judgment of the trial court only as to the kidnapping charge and remanded the case to that court with direction to render judgment in accordance with the jury verdict.

Harris v. Bradley Mem. Hosp. & Health Ctr.


SC 18944


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


306 Conn. 304; 50 A.3d 841; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 329


May 16, 2012, Argued 
September 4, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harris v. Bradley Mem. Hosp., 2013 U.S. LEXIS 3025 (U.S., Apr. 15, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendant's alleged breach of contract, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Burke, J., granted in part the defendant's motion for summary judgment; thereafter, the court, Shaban, J., denied the defendant's second motion for summary judgment, and the case was tried to the jury before Schuman, J., with respect to the plaintiff's claim for damages, and to the court, Schuman, J., with respect to the plaintiff's claim for injunctive relief; subsequently, the court, Schuman, J., granted the defendant's motion for a directed verdict only as to the plaintiff's claim under the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, and the jury returned a verdict for the plaintiff on the claim for damages; thereafter, the court, Schuman, J., granted the defendant's motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and for remittitur, denied the plaintiff's motions for injunctive relief and for punitive damages, and rendered judgment thereon for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed; subsequently, this court affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded  [***2] the case for further proceedings; on remand, the court, Pittman, J., awarded the plaintiff certain compensatory and punitive damages, attorney's fees and costs, and the defendant appealed; thereafter, the court, Pittman, J., awarded the plaintiff offer of judgment interest, and the defendant filed an amended appeal.
Harris v. Bradley Mem. Hosp., 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 369 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 17, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed a judgment entered by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain, Connecticut, for plaintiff surgeon on his breach of contract, breach of the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing, and tortious interference with business expectancies claims, which awarded the surgeon punitive damages and offer of judgment interest on remand. The appeal was transferred by the state's highest court to itself.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that because the hospital was the appellee in a previous appeal, any deficiency with regard to raising claims on appeal did not result in forfeiture. The hospital's immunity claim under the Health Care Quality Improvement Act of 1986, 42 U.S.C.S. § 11101 et seq., had never been considered by the state's highest court on the merits, and the court had not expended considerable judicial resources in ascertaining whether it could review the claim. The surgeon's claim that the hospital's immunity claim was beyond the scope of the remand was rejected. The hospital had remedied the procedural defect that the state's highest court had identified previously. A summary suspension followed by notice and a hearing under 42 U.S.C.S. § 11112(c)(2) was entitled to a presumption of immunity when necessary to prevent imminent danger to patients. Section § 11112(c) was an exception to literal compliance with § 11112(a)(3), rather than a freestanding ground for immunity, and therefore was covered by the presumption of immunity that applied to § 11112(a). The surgeon did not advance any substantive argument in opposition to the hospital's immunity claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment in favor of the hospital.

State v. Guilbert


SC 17948


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


306 Conn. 218; 49 A.3d 705; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 327


February 10, 2011, Argued 
September 4, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Stay denied by, As moot, Motion denied by, As moot Guilbert v. Murphy, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 109 (D. Conn., Jan. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information in the first case charging the defendant with one count of attempt to commit murder and two counts of assault in the first degree, and information in the second case charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of murder and one count of the crime of capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Schimelman, J., granted the state's motion for joinder and its motion in limine to preclude certain expert testimony; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Schimelman, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of assault in the first degree in the first case and verdict and judgment of guilty of two counts of murder and one count of capital felony in the second case, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of capital felony in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(7), two counts of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a, and assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1). The Superior Court in the judicial district of New London (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to a term of life imprisonment without the possibility of release, plus 20 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court improperly precluded him from presenting expert testimony on the fallibility of eyewitness testimony and that case law concluding that the average juror knows about the factors affecting the reliability of eyewitness identification should be overruled. The supreme court agreed it was time to overrule State v. Kemp, 199 Conn. 473, 477, 507 A.2d 1387 (1986), and State v. McClendon, 248 Conn. 572, 586, 730 A.2d 1107 (1999). The supreme court held that reliability of eyewitness identification was frequently not a matter within the knowledge of an average juror and that admission of expert testimony on the issue did not invade the province of the jury to determine what weight to give the evidence. Many of the factors affecting reliability of eyewitness identification were either unknown to the average juror or contrary to common assumptions. While the trial court erred in excluding defendant's expert on the issue, the error was harmless, as the jury instructions provided assistance to the jury and, in combination with the evidence of defendant's guilt, ensured that the exclusion of the expert's testimony did not substantially affect the verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Makee R.


SC 18494


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


306 Conn. 371; 50 A.3d 305; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 331


February 7, 2012, Argued 
September 1, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Rodriguez, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; thereafter, the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Alvord and Pellegrino, Js., which affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Makee R., 117 Conn. App. 191, 978 A.2d 549, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 426 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(2), and risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2). The trial court sentenced defendant to 25 years, suspended after 15 years, and 25 years probation. Defendant appealed. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the appellate court improperly affirmed the trial court's judgment because he was denied a fair trial, in violation of the Fifth, Sixth, and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. Defendant claimed that the trial court's preliminary instruction to the jury regarding posttrial procedures and the trial court's final instruction to the jury regarding the minor victim's credibility were improper. The State asserted that the trial court's instructions, when considered in their entirety did not deny defendant his right to a fair trial. The supreme court agreed with the State, concluding that the improper instructions neither affected the fairness of the trial, nor prejudiced defendant. Among other things, the trial court explicitly instructed the jury panel that the jury's role was that of fact finder and prefaced and concluded each instruction to the venire panel by stating that sentencing was not the function of the jury. In addition, the jury was instructed on the presumption of innocence, the State's burden of proof, the elements of the crimes, and the fact that time was not an element of the offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.
