State v. Drupals


SC 18697


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


306 Conn. 149; 49 A.3d 962; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 324


March 14, 2012, Argued 
August 28, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended October 22, 2012.
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Dismissed without prejudice by, in part, Motion denied by, As moot Drupals v. Mabey, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 100056 (D. Conn., July 23, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of failure to comply with the sex offender registration requirements, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the court, Nigro, J.; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one (Connecticut) convicted defendant of two counts of failing to comply with the sex offender registry requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-251. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court improperly determined that there was sufficient evidence to prove that he violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-251. The appellate court agreed. As to the first count, there was evidence that defendant notified the registry, in writing on the day he moved, that the listed address was no loner his place of residence. Three days later he notified the registry of the address of his newly claimed residence in Maryland. Defendant registered in Maryland four days later. The supreme court concluded that defendant notified the registry of the change of residence address from Connecticut without "undue delay," as required by § 54-251. Defendant was not required to notify the registry of his temporary address while traveling. As to the second count, the trial court found that defendant moved from Maryland back to Connecticut and sent notice of said change in residence to Maryland four days later and notified the unit in Connecticut of the change three days after that, which was the fifth business day after the move, thereby fulfilling the requirements of § 54-251(e).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to vacate defendant's convictions.

 

81 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Shanahan v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


SC 18575


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


305 Conn. 681; 47 A.3d 364; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 279


January 5, 2012, Argued 
July 24, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision by the named defendant ordering the plaintiff to remove a seawall that was constructed on certain of his real property without the statutorily required permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., denied the plaintiff's motion to allow discovery or to supplement the record with regard to the issue of the constitutionality of the permitting statute; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgment dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Shanahan v. Conn. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2692 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 15, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed a decision by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut) which found in favor of defendant department of environmental protection ordering him to remove a new seawall that he had constructed. The trial court concluded, inter alia, that the department had produced substantial evidence supporting its jurisdiction and that Conn. Gen. Sat. § 22a-359 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The department had exercised its statutory jurisdiction to regulate activity in the tidal, coastal, or navigable waters of the state waterward of the high tide line because the property owner constructed the contested seawall without obtaining the permit required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-361(a)(1). The appellate court held that substantial evidence showed the seawall was constructed waterward of the high tide line. Numerous photographs showing direct evidence of water coming into contact with the seawall and the multitude of surveys of the property consistently showing at least part of the seawall waterward of even the 5.7 foot elevation claimed by the property owner to be the high tide line provided more than sufficient nontechnical evidence to determine that the seawall lay waterward of the high tide line. Thus, it fell within the department's jurisdiction. The property owner could not prevail on his claim that the definition of "high tide line" contained in § 22a-359(c) was unconstitutionally vague. However, the department abused its discretion in issuing an order requiring the property owner to submit a plan for the removal of the entire seawall.


OUTCOME: The part the judgment denying the appeal from the department's removal order was reversed, insofar as that order pertained to the portion of the seawall not waterward of the high tide line. The trial court was directed to remand the case to the department for further proceedings to determine which portions of the seawall were constructed "waterward of the high tide line" and thus were subject to the department's jurisdiction.


 

82 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



In re Emoni W.


SC 18841


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


305 Conn. 723; 48 A.3d 1; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 290


March 16, 2012, Argued 
July 19, 2012, Officially Released**.


** July 19, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petitions by the commissioner of children and families to adjudicate the respondents' minor children neglected, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, Juvenile Matters at Waterford, where the court, Mack, J., issued orders of temporary custody; thereafter, the court, Driscoll, J., ordered the petitioner to initiate an interstate compact study on the placement of the children, and the respondent father and the minor children filed separate appeals to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the court, Driscoll, J., rendered judgments adjudicating the minor children neglected and awarding joint legal custody to the respondents and physical custody to the respondent father; thereafter, the Appellate Court, Lavine and Beach, Js., with Bishop, J., dissenting, dismissed the appeals, and the respondent father, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
In re Emoni W., 129 Conn. App. 727, 21 A.3d 524, 2011 Conn. App. LEXIS 362 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Commission of Children and Families was granted temporary custody of respondent father's children. The father appealed the ruling that the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-175, applied to the placement of the children, even though he was their noncustodial parent. He challenged an order of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which dismissed his appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the father's appeal was moot because he was awarded physical custody of the children. The supreme court held that the appellate court improperly dismissed the appeal. The father's fell within the "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception to the mootness doctrine. His claim that when the placement of a child with a parent was approved pursuant to the recommendation of a compact study application of § 17a-175 to the parent violated substantive due process principles met the evading review requirement because it would become moot in the substantial majority of cases in which it could be raised, and resolution of the statutory interpretation claim was a necessary prerequisite to the resolution of the constitutional claim. The trial court improperly ruled that § 17a-175 applied to out-of-state, noncustodial parents. The ordinary meaning of the phrase "for placement in foster care or as a preliminary to a possible adoption" as used in § 17a-175, article III(a), did not encompass placement with a noncustodial parent. Children in the care of their own parents were not in "foster care," and parents were not required to adopt their own children.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to that court with direction to sustain the father's appeal and to remand the case to the trial court with direction to reverse the judgment.


 

83 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rose


SC 18323


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


305 Conn. 594; 46 A.3d 146; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 277; 99 A.L.R.6th 765


November 30, 2011, Argued 
July 10, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of assault of public safety personnel, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, and tried to the jury before Bellis, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, McLachlan and Lavine, Js., with Foti, J., concurring in part and dissenting in part, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Rose, 112 Conn. App. 324, 963 A.2d 68, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 30 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of assaulting a public safety personnel by the trial court in connection with an incident in which he spat on a correction officer while incarcerated. Defendant appealed to the Appellate Court which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for a new trial. The State, on the granting of certification, appealed to the Supreme Court of Connecticut.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly compelled him to wear identifiable prison clothing during his jury trial in violation of his constitutional right to a fair trial pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The Appellate Court concluded that the trial court impermissibly compelled defendant, who had objected to wearing prison clothing during trial, to stand trial in such clothing, that the doctrine of harmless error did not apply, and that, even if it did apply, the State failed to prove harmlessness beyond a reasonable doubt. The Supreme Court held that although the Appellate Court properly reversed defendant's conviction, in the exercise of its supervisory authority over the administration of justice, the Supreme Court was announcing a per se rule of reversibility when, as in the present case, the trial court compelled a defendant to stand trial before a jury in identifiable prison clothing in violation of his constitutional rights as that undermined the integrity of the trial and diminished the perceived fairness of the judicial system as a whole by compromising the jury's ability to engage in neutral fact-finding and eroding the presumption of innocence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed.

State v. Santiago


SC 17413


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


305 Conn. 101; 49 A.3d 566; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 218


April 27, 2011, Argued 
May 29, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended July 31, 2012.
Different results reached on reconsideration by, in part, Supplemental opinion at, Remanded by State v. Santiago, 318 Conn. 1, 2015 Conn. LEXIS 228 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of capital felony, murder, felony murder, conspiracy to commit murder, stealing a firearm and larceny in the sixth degree, and with two counts each of the crimes of burglary in the first degree and conspiracy to commit burglary in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the state filed a notice of the aggravating factor that it intended to prove during the penalty phase of the proceedings and where the defendant filed a notice of mitigating factors; thereafter, the court, Lavine, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, in the penalty phase of the proceedings, the jury found that the state had proven the existence of the aggravating factor beyond a reasonable doubt, at least one or more jurors found that the defendant had proven the existence of one or more mitigating factors by a preponderance of the evidence, and the jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravating factor outweighed the mitigating factor or factors; subsequently,  [***2] the court, Lavine, J., denied the defendant's postverdict motions to impose a life sentence, to declare the death penalty in this state unconstitutional, to impose a life sentence because of the arbitrary imposition of the sentence of death in this case, and for an order barring the defendant's execution because of the discriminatory nature of the state's death penalty system, and also denied the defendant's postverdict motions concerning allegedly improper jury deliberations and juror misconduct and the improper exclusion of a mitigating factor alleged by the defense; thereafter, the court, Lavine, J., rendered judgment of guilty and sentenced the defendant to death by lethal injection and to a consecutive term of imprisonment of forty-five years and ninety days, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Santiago, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 203 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new penalty phase trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) of, inter alia, capital felony and murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court improperly failed, under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, to disclose certain documents from social service's file that potentially would have given the jury a broader and more comprehensive picture of defendant's family history to consider as a mitigating factor at sentencing. The supreme court agreed. The trial court improperly failed to disclose numerous entries and records that, if made available to the defendant, his counsel and supporting experts, during their mitigation investigation, could well have shed additional light on the significant dysfunction and violence that systemically plagued defendant's entire family. There were multiple sexual molestations of one child. The supreme court could not find that, had those facts, and others in the nondisclosed department records, been properly presented to the jury as part of a comprehensive family history, they would not have swayed the case in mitigation by painting an even more harrowing picture of defendant's family life, especially in light of the failure of anyone from defendant's immediate family to testify on his behalf at the penalty hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed insofar as it imposed a sentence of death and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new penalty phase hearing, following a new in camera review, according to law, of the department's files and disclosure of evidence material to defendant's case in mitigation; the judgment was otherwise affirmed.

86 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benton


SC 18850


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 838; 43 A.3d 619; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 198


March 22, 2012, Argued 
May 22, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, A. Hadden, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Richards, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his weapon-related convictions by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut). He claimed the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress evidence obtained in a search incident to his arrest as the police seized him prior to his arrest without reasonable and articulable suspicion that he was engaged in criminal activity as required by U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9.


OVERVIEW: Police officers were aware that several shootings had recently occurred in a neighborhood occupied by members of a gang, some involving bicycle riding perpetrators. They observed defendant on a bicycle make a gesture consistent with adjusting an unholstered handgun tucked into his pants' waistband. Defendant yelled an obscenity when he saw the officers and attempted to quickly ride away. The officers ordered defendant to stop. He ignored the command and continued to pedal away. The officers then apprehended defendant, and, in the course of the ensuing struggle, they discovered a loaded handgun. The appellate court held that defendant was not seized until the officers ordered him to stop. By simply stepping into the road, the police officers did not exercise physical force or make a show of authority such that a reasonable person would feel restrained from departing. Defendant's acts collectively could, at the very least, be reasonably construed as "nervous, evasive behavior," which was a pertinent factor in determining reasonable suspicion. That, coupled with his attempted flight and appearance, provided a basis for adequate reasonable and articulable suspicion to stop defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Perez-Dickson v. City of Bridgeport


SC 18401


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 483; 43 A.3d 69; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 147; 114 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1461; 34 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 508


May 18, 2011, Argued 
May 1, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Schumann v. Dianon Sys., 304 Conn. 585, 43 A.3d 111, 2012 Conn. LEXIS 146 (2012)
Related proceeding at Perez-Dickson v. Bridgeport Bd. of Educ., 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 118847 (D. Conn., Sept. 8, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages arising from, inter alia, the defendants' alleged unlawful employment practices, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Bridgeport, where the matter was tried to a jury before Gilardi, J.; verdict for the plaintiff awarding economic, noneconomic and punitive damages; subsequently, the court denied the defendants' motion for a directed verdict, to set aside the verdict and for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, granted in part the defendants' motion for remittitur and reduced the award of damages, and rendered judgment for the plaintiff; thereafter, the defendants appealed and the plaintiff cross appealed.
Perez-Dixon v. City of Bridgeport, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1967 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 12, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee successfully sued defendants, a board of education and administrators, in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Bridgeport (Connecticut) for racial discrimination, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-51q and 17a-101e. The trial court denied defendants' motion for a directed verdict. Defendants appealed, and the employee cross appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a school principal, said she was disciplined contrary to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-51q and 17a-101e for reporting teachers' child abuse. The supreme court held it was error to deny defendants' directed verdict motion because (1) the First Amendment did not protect the employee's reports were pursuant to her official duties, (2) alternate grounds for affirmance under the Connecticut Constitution were unpreserved, and (2) she had no private right of action under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101e. She did not show defendants' racial discrimination under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1981 and 1983 because her statistical evidence of less favorable treatment than white and African-American employees accused of abusing a student raised no inference of intentional racial discrimination, as it showed no stark pattern of disparate treatment. It was error to deny a directed verdict as to her intentional infliction of emotional distress claim because no reasonable juror could find defendants' conduct met the required threshold, as (1) she was only subjected to acts individuals in the workplace reasonably should expect, and (2) any wrongful motivation did not meet that standard.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with direction to grant defendants' directed verdict motion, to set aside the verdict, and to render judgment for defendants.

State v. Paige


SC 18495


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 426; 40 A.3d 279; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 129


February 2, 2012, Argued 
April 17, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with six counts of the crime of larceny in the first degree, three counts of the crime of perjury and one count each of the crimes of tampering with or fabricating physical evidence, forgery in the second degree and larceny in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk and tried to the jury before Holden, J.; after the court granted the defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal as to two counts of perjury, verdict and judgment of guilty of five counts of larceny in the first degree and one count each of perjury, tampering with or fabricating physical evidence, forgery in the second degree and larceny in the second degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Beach and Robinson, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty of larceny in the second degree and one count of larceny in the first degree, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Paige, 115 Conn. App. 717, 974 A.2d 782, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 328 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, perjury in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-156 and two counts of larceny. She appealed. The Appellate Court of Connecticut reversed in part and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment of not guilty of larceny in the second degree and of larceny in the first degree; it otherwise affirmed the judgment. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an attorney, had been sued in connection with her thefts from an elderly client. The State charged her with perjury based on allegedly false statements she made during a deposition taken in connection with that suit. In the instant case, the trial court rejected her request to charge the jury that it had to decide whether the statement at issue was material to the civil case, and ruled that it was material as a matter of law. The intermediate appellate court held that defendant waived her right to challenge the instruction that the trial court gave by failing to object, and by agreeing that materiality was a question of law that should not be submitted to the jury. The high court held that as defendant submitted a request to charge pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 16-20 that was rejected, and never explicitly withdrew it, she was not also required to take an exception to the contrary charge in order to preserve the issue for appeal. The high court overruled State v. Greenberg, 103 A. 897 (1918), insofar as it concluded that in a perjury prosecution, the materiality of the statement at issue presented a question of law for the court to decide.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed only as to defendant's perjury conviction and the case was remanded to that court with direction to remand the case to the trial court for a new trial on that charge. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Gross v. Rell


SC 18548


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 234; 40 A.3d 240; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 119


October 24, 2011, Argued 
April 3, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Gross v. Rell, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 20132 (2d Cir., Sept. 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' alleged negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress, brought to the United States District Court in the District of Connecticut, where Carolyn Dee King, executrix of the named plaintiff's estate, was substituted as a plaintiff; subsequently, the court, Bryant, J., dismissed the complaint and rendered judgment for the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed to the United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit; thereafter, the court, Jacobs, C. J., and Straub and Hall, Js., affirmed in part the judgment of the District Court, and, in determining whether to uphold the District Court's dismissal of certain claims against the defendants Grove Manor Nursing Home, Inc., et al., certified to this court certain questions of law concerning the defense of quasi-judicial immunity.
Gross v. Rell, 585 F.3d 72, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 23581 (2d Cir. Conn., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff conservatee against defendants, a long-term care ombudsman, a probate court judge, a conservator, an attorney, and a nursing home, the court accepted certified questions of law, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199b(d), concerning whether absolute quasi-judicial immunity extended to conservators appointed by the probate court and to attorneys appointed to represent conservatees pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-649(b).


OVERVIEW: While visiting his daughter in Connecticut, the conservatee, a New York resident, was admitted to a hospital for medical treatment. Thereafter, a hospital employee filed an application for appointment of a conservator, which was granted. The attorney appointed for the conservatee did not object to the conservatorship or inform the probate court that it lacked jurisdiction over the application under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-648(a) (Rev. 2005). The conservatee alleged that he was placed in a locked ward for no reason and that he was threatened and assaulted by his roommate. Following the conservatee's death, his executrix was substituted as plaintiff. Absolute quasi-judicial immunity extended to the conservator only when the conservator was executing an order of the probate court. When the conservator acted as a fiduciary of the conservatee, the conservator was subject to personal liability. Furthermore, absolute quasi-judicial immunity did not extend to an attorney appointed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-649(b) (Rev. 2005). Finally, absolute quasi-judicial immunity did not extend under any circumstances to a nursing home with respect to its care for a conservatee.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions.

Scholastic Book Clubs, Inc. v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs.


SC 18425


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 204; 38 A.3d 1183; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 111


October 24, 2011, Argued 
March 27, 2012, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Scholastic Book Clubs v. Ct Comm'r of Revenue Servs., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 8019 (U.S., Oct. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeals from the defendant's assessment of certain sales and use tax deficiencies against the plaintiff, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, and tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgments sustaining the appeals, from which the defendant appealed.
Scholastic Book Clubs, Inc. v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 955 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 9, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a Missouri bookseller, appealed assessments of sales and use tax deficiencies against it by defendant, the Connecticut Commissioner of Revenue Services, under Connecticut's Sales and Use Taxes Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-406 et seq. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain, Tax Session (Connecticut), sustained plaintiff's appeals. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff distributed its books by mail to Connecticut classrooms. It had no employees, offices, or property in Connecticut; teachers ordered its products on behalf of their students through catalogs. The trial court held that the taxes could not be imposed as the teachers were not plaintiff's "representatives" as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-407(a)(15)(A)(iv). The high court disagreed. "Representative" was a person who was not an employee or an agent and who did not necessarily act through delegated authority for remuneration. As plaintiff was able to sell its products in Connecticut only through the teachers who participated in its program, they were its "representatives" even though they were unpaid and had no agency relationship with plaintiff. Thus, pursuant to § 12-407(a)(15)(A), it was subject to Connecticut sales and use taxes. As teachers participating in the program were the only means through which plaintiff communicated with Connecticut schoolchildren, they provided the substantial nexus required to permit imposition of sales and use taxes under the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, pursuant to the U.S. Supreme Court's bright-line physical presence rule.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to deny plaintiff's appeals and to render judgments for defendant.

Pereira v. State Bd. of Educ.


SC 18833


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


304 Conn. 1; 37 A.3d 625; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 79


October 27, 2011, Argued 
February 28, 2012, * Officially Released


* February 28, 2012, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended April 3, 2012.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Actions seeking, inter alia, certain injunctive and declaratory relief in connection with the decision of the named defendant state board of education to authorize the defendant commissioner of education to reconstitute the named defendant board of education of the city of Bridgeport, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the cases were transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the court, Agati, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved certain questions of law for the advice of this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action involving defendant state board of education's decision to authorize defendant commissioner of education to reconstitute defendant local board of education, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket (Connecticut), certified five questions of law. The dispositive question was whether the state board violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233e(h) when it authorized the local board's reconstitution.


OVERVIEW: For at least seven consecutive years, the state board had designated the local school district a low achieving district under § 10-233e(c)(1). The local district had failed to make acceptable progress toward state benchmarks, under § 10-233e(a) and (c), and had failed to make adequate yearly progress under the federal No Child Left Behind Act of 2001, 20 U.S.C.S. § 6301 et seq. for at least two consecutive years. In three cases, plaintiffs, city residents and former members of the local board, sought declaratory and injunctive relief after the state board authorized the reconstitution of the local board. Because the state board failed to require the local board to undergo and complete training, as required by the mandatory provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-233e(h), it violated the statute when it authorized the commissioner to reconstitute the local board. The training provision was not protective of any particular individual or group, and neither the statute nor its legislative history provided that local boards of education were entitled to make their own determination as to whether training or reconstitution was appropriate. The training provision cannot be waived.


OUTCOME: The court answered the dispositive question in the affirmative.

Town of Bozrah v. Chmurynski


SC 18424, SC 18354, SC 18355, SC 18356


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


303 Conn. 676; 36 A.3d 210; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 50


October 17, 2011, Argued 
February 14, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Application, in one case, for a temporary injunction to allow the plaintiffs to inspect certain premises owned or occupied by the named defendant et al. for alleged violations of the town of Bozrah zoning regulations, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and referred to Hon. Joseph J. Purtill, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, issued a temporary injunction preventing the named defendant et al. from refusing to allow the inspection of the premises; thereafter, the court granted the defendants' motion for a stay of execution pending an appeal, and the defendants appealed to the Appellate Court, which appeal subsequently was transferred to this court. Writs of error, in three other cases, from the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, Hon. Joseph J. Purtill, judge trial referee, granting the application for a temporary injunction, brought to this court; thereafter, the three writs of error were consolidated with the appeal in the first case.
Town of Bozrah v. Chmurynski, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 809 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 20, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town and a zoning enforcement officer, sought a temporary injunction to prevent defendant owners from refusing to permit a property inspection for zoning violations. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) granted an injunction. The trial court granted the owners' motion for a stay of execution. Two of the owners appealed, three of the owners brought writs of error, and the cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The zoning officer had attempted to inspect the owners' property pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-12, but the owners refused to consent to the inspection. The trial court held that the town's interest in stabilizing property values and promoting the general welfare justified the inspection. However, a zoning inspection pursuant to § 8-12 of areas in which the owners had a reasonable expectation of privacy was a search within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV. Probable cause was necessary to justify any § 8-12 search for zoning violations that targeted a single residence. Accordingly, the zoning official was only entitled to inspect a single property, not part of a routine or area wide search, under § 8-12 if the official first obtained an injunction issued upon probable cause by a judicial officer. Because the trial court failed to make a preliminary determination of probable cause to believe that a zoning violation existed on the property, the trial court's order violated the owners' right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures under the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment setting aside the injunction.


 

93 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Francis v. Fonfara


SC 18480


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


303 Conn. 292; 33 A.3d 185; 2012 Conn. LEXIS 1


October 21, 2011, Argued 
January 3, 2012, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Writ of error from the decision of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, Berger, J., finding that the plaintiff in error was not entitled to the receipt of certain fees in connection with effectuating service of process on the named defendant et al., brought to the Supreme Court.
Francis v. Fonfara, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1407 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 21, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Writ granted; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error, a state marshal, brought a writ of error seeking reversal of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) denying her request for certain fees made in connection with her service of process in a civil action. The issue was whether she was entitled to a fee for copies of a complaint under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-261(a)(2) despite the fact that she did not personally make the copies.


OVERVIEW: Named plaintiff citizen sought and received a waiver of the entry fee and the process server's service fees pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 8-2, including a waiver of § 52-261(a)(2) fee for copies of writs and complaints. As a result of the waiver, the state, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-259b, was responsible for paying the process server's fees. In connection with serving process, the marshal received a box from the citizen with a sufficient quantity of copies to serve all 185 defendants and, subsequently, properly effectuated service by leaving process for each defendant with an associate attorney general. The marshal did not personally make the copies of the complaint, but confirmed that each was exactly the same as the original. Thereafter, the marshal submitted an invoice for $ 900 for copies of the complaint. The appellate court held that the trial court improperly denied her request for fees for copies; although § 52-261(a)(2) was ambiguous as to whether the process server must personally make the copies of the complaint, the legislative history revealed an intent that the fee for copies be paid regardless of who actually made the copies.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was a misapplication of the law. The writ of error was granted. The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to award the marshal the requested fee for copies of $ 900.


 

94 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bell


SC 18715


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


303 Conn. 246; 33 A.3d 167; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 510


April 25, 2011, Argued 
December 27, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part information charging the defendant, in the first part, with two counts of the crime of assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a pistol, and, in the second part, with being a persistent dangerous felony offender and with the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty of one count each of assault in the first degree, carrying a pistol without a permit and criminal possession of a pistol or revolver; thereafter, the second part of the information was tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdicts and enhanced the defendant's sentence for the commission of a class A, B or C felony with a firearm and for being a persistent dangerous felony offender, and the defendant appealed; thereafter, this court reversed the trial court's judgment only as to the sentence imposed and remanded the case for further proceedings; on remand, the court,  [***2] Blue, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the second part of the information and the defendant's motion in limine to introduce evidence of the costs of the defendant's extended incarceration; subsequently, the sentencing matter was tried to the jury before Blue, J., who sentenced the defendant in accordance with the verdict that extended incarceration would best serve the public interest, and the defendant appealed.
State v. Bell, 283 Conn. 748, 931 A.2d 198, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 369 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) for, inter alia, assault in the first degree and the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40(h). Upon remand, the jury again imposed an enhanced sentence. Defendant filed a second appeal, claiming, inter alia, that the trial court improperly denied his motion to dismiss the second part of the State's information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the retroactive application of the Connecticut Supreme Court's prior decision violated ex post facto principles. The court's excision in Bell of the language from § 53a-40(h) that had required the court, rather than a jury, to make the requisite public interest finding resulted in an ameliorative change to § 53a-40(h) that was merely procedural and did not make the punishment under § 53a-40(h) more onerous than it was before Bell was decided. Therefore, defendant was not disadvantaged retroactively by the statutory modification. Furthermore, defendant was on fair notice that the substantive provisions of § 53a-40(h) would apply to him even if certain procedural provisions were later found to be unconstitutional. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to introduce evidence of the costs of his incarceration to demonstrate that his extended incarceration would not best serve the public interest. Defendant could not prevail on his claim that the trial court had abused its discretion in admitting evidence of the details of the injuries sustained by the police officer whom defendant shot and the long-term effects that those injuries had on the officer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

95 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Maurice M.


SC 18454


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


303 Conn. 18; 31 A.3d 1063; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 464


March 23, 2011, Argued 
November 29, 2011, Officially released


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, geographical area number nineteen, and tried to the court, T. Sullivan, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop and Robinson, Js., with West, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Maurice M., 116 Conn. App. 1, 975 A.2d 90, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 290 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court revoked defendant's probation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-32 on the basis of its finding that he had committed the crime of risk of injury to a child (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1)). Defendant appealed; the Connecticut Appellate Court affirmed. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Motorists saw a small child in the street and called police. Defendant, the sole caretaker present in the home, told an officer that he had left his two-year-old child unsupervised in a room with an eight-year-old child, and the younger child apparently exited the home through a back door. Defendant was charged with violating § 53-21(a)(1), which in turn led to the revocation of his probation. The intermediate appellate court, in affirming that revocation, held that the evidence was sufficient to show that he failed to supervise his child adequately, despite his knowledge that the back door of his home was unsecured. The high court disagreed. Without any evidence of the back door's accessibility, and in light of testimony establishing that the child had never escaped the house in this manner before, it was not reasonably foreseeable that the child would exit the home. Therefore, the predicate facts proved by the State were insufficient to establish that defendant's failure to supervise the child while at home evinced a reckless disregard for the consequences of that conduct in violation of § 53-21(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment for defendant.

State v. Rizzo


SC 17527


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


303 Conn. 71; 31 A.3d 1094; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 463


October 22, 2010, Argued 
November 29, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rizzo v. Conn., 133 S. Ct. 133, 184 L. Ed. 2d 64, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6890 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Rizzo, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1685 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 29, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a) and capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54b(9) (Rev. to 1997). A jury was sentenced defendant to death. The supreme court reversed as to the and the case was remanded for a new penalty phase hearing, during which defendant waived his right to a jury, opting for a three judge panel. The trial court (Connecticut) panel sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's numerous assignments of error, the supreme court concluded, inter alia, that: (1) defendant's waiver of a jury for the penalty phase proceeding was valid, because the trial court's canvass was sufficiently detailed, defendant indicated that he understood that he had a right to a jury but could waive the right, defendant conferred with counsel prior to waiving the right to a jury, the court differentiated between the unanimity and majority requirements for 12 person juries and three judge panels, and there as no indication that defendant was incompetent; (2) one judge's participation in the case prior to defendant's waiver of his right to a jury did not require the judge's recusal during the penalty phase, as the judge's mere exposure to information during the judge's earlier participation was not a due process violation; and (3) the three judge panel's finding that defendant had been callous or indifferent to the extreme physical and psychological pain and suffering that he had inflicted on the victim through his intentional conduct, and that such conduct support the aggravator found in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(4), was not improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Episcopal Church in the Diocese of Conn. v. Gauss


SC 18719


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


302 Conn. 408; 28 A.3d 302; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 382


February 9, 2011, Argued 
October 11, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Gauss v. Episcopal Church in the Diocese of Conn., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4624 (U.S., June 18, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a judgment declaring that the real and personal property of Bishop Seabury Church was held in trust for the named plaintiff, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London at New London, where the Protestant Episcopal Church in the United States of America intervened as a plaintiff; thereafter, the case was transferred to the judicial district of Hartford, Complex Litigation Docket, where the named defendant et al. filed a counterclaim; subsequently, the case was transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket, where the trial court, Stevens, J., granted the plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, denied the motion for summary judgment filed by the named defendant et al., and rendered judgment in favor of the plaintiffs, from which the named defendant et al. appealed; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for an order of accounting, and the named defendant et al. filed an amended appeal; subsequently, the court granted the motion for an order of contempt filed by the named plaintiff et al. and found the named defendant et al. in contempt, and the named defendant et al. filed a second  [***2] amended appeal.
Episcopal Church v. Gauss, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 592 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 15, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in part; affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, Episcopal Church and Connecticut Diocese, moved for summary judgment as to their claim that they were entitled to certain personal property. The Judicial District of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket (Connecticut), granted that motion in addition to ordering an accounting. Defendants, a former rector of the church and twelve present or former officers or vestry members of the church, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Church and Diocese had sought a judgment declaring that the real and personal property of the church was held in trust them following a decision by the majority of voting members of the church to affiliate with an ecclesiastical society that was not part of the Episcopal Church or the Diocese. The Connecticut Supreme Court held that the trial court properly determined that church property was held in trust for the Church and the Diocese and in ordering a former rector of the church and 12 present or former officers or vestry members of the church, to relinquish possession of control of the property to the Church and Diocese. The trial court rejected the original request for an order of accounting pursuant to the accounting statutes. When the trial court granted the second request, it explained that it was granting the order on the basis of its equitable authority and discretion to protect the integrity of its prior declaration. The Supreme Court was unable to afford the individual members any practical relief by reversing the trial court's order requiring full compliance with the order of accounting.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. There was no need for remand. The appeal was dismissed.

State v. Fields


SC 18457


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


302 Conn. 236; 24 A.3d 1243; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 352


January 10, 2011, Argued 
August 30, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of kidnapping in the second degree and one count each of the crimes of burglary in the first degree, assault in the first degree, risk of injury to a child, larceny in the third degree, and larceny in the fifth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, where the court, Levin, J., denied the defendant's motion to exclude certain misconduct evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Levin, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts of kidnapping in the second degree and one count each of assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child; subsequently, the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the charge of burglary in the first degree; thereafter, the court, Levin, J., rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of two counts of second degree kidnapping under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94, one count of first degree assault under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and one count of risk of injury to a child under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four (Connecticut) sentenced him to a total effective sentence of 53 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a new trial on one charge of kidnapping, because the trial court failed to instruct the jury that it could not find him guilty of the crime unless it found beyond a reasonable doubt that the restraint or force involved was not merely incidental to the underlying assault. The supreme court agreed that such an instruction should have been given and concluded that it was not harmless. Defendant was entitled to have the jury decide whether his restraint of the victim during the assault had independent criminal significance as a kidnapping, as there was testimony that another person took the victim out to the car while defendant remained in the house. Defendant's challenge to the instruction on risk of injury to a child failed, as there was no possibility the jury was led to believe it could find defendant guilty upon proof his conduct in causing the child to be left alone for 25 minutes was merely inadvertent. Finally, the supreme court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1) was not unconstitutionally vague, but apprised a personal on ordinary intelligence that it was dangerous and unsafe to leave an infant alone for a period of time.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed as to one count of kidnapping and remanded for a new trial on the charge. The judgment of the trial court was otherwise affirmed.

Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities ex rel. Arnold v. Forvil


SC 18500


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


302 Conn. 263; 25 A.3d 632; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 354


May 16, 2011, Argued 
August 30, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages on behalf of the relators for the defendants' alleged discrimination against them on the basis of a legal source of income in connection with the relators' attempt to rent certain premises from the defendants, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Housing Session at Bridgeport, and tried to the court, Moore, J.; judgment for the plaintiff awarding damages and attorney's fees to the relators and a civil penalty to the plaintiff, from which the defendants appealed.
Conn. Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities v. Forvil, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1589 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 4, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Connecticut Commission on Human Rights and Opportunities (commission) sued defendants landlords in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, Housing Session at Bridgeport (Connecticut), on behalf of relators tenants for housing discrimination in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-64c(a). The trial court entered judgment for the commission, assessed a fine, and awarded damages to the tenants. The landlords appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landlords said the trial court lacked jurisdiction when it did not issue a decision within the 120 days required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-183b. The supreme court disagreed because, after the landlords filed a damages brief, the trial court properly reopened the case within 120 days and then rendered judgment within 120 days of that reopening. It was no error to conclude that a security deposit guarantee was a "lawful source of income," under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-64c and 46a-63(3), for purposes of unlawful discrimination based on a "lawful source of income," because it was "housing assistance" included in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-63(3)'s definition of a lawful source of income. It was no error to conclude that the guarantee's validity was irrelevant because the landlords did not reject it due to any invalidity but for the illegal reason that it was not cash. Compensatory damages were not excessive because, (1) while no findings on damages were made, the landlords did not move for articulation, and (2) a tenant's testimony provided an adequate basis for emotional distress damages for the tenant and the tenant's children, so the award did not shock the judicial conscience.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Winfrey


SC 18716


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


302 Conn. 195; 24 A.3d 1218; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 351


April 20, 2011, Argued 
August 23, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of a controlled substance, interfering with an officer, and tampering with physical evidence, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven, where the court, J. Fischer, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before J. Fischer, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of the lesser included offense of possession of narcotics, possession of a controlled substance, interfering with an officer and tampering with physical evidence, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number seven (Connecticut), of possessing narcotics, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a), possessing a controlled substance, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(c), interfering with an officer, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-167a, and tampering with physical evidence, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-155, after his motion to suppress was denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant swallowed heroin found on his person when arrested. The supreme court held his car's search did not violate the Fourth Amendment or Conn. Const. art. I, § 7 because officers who saw him swallow the heroin and found rolling papers and cash on his person had probable cause to think drugs would be found in the car. The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of the possessory crimes, under the doctrine of nonexclusive possession, because (1) he drove the car just before its search, (2) his wife was the car's registered owner, (3) when he swallowed five wax folds of heroin, it was more likely that he, rather than his wife or passenger, owned drugs found in the car, (4) his rolling papers and cash made it more likely that he owned salable quantities of drugs in the car, and (5) his medical records showed he was a drug user with cocaine and opiates in his urine when arrested. It was no abuse of discretion to admit his unredacted medical records because (1) his drug use history made it more likely he owned drugs found in the car, (2) his drug use admissions were not highly prejudicial, and (2) officers' accounts of his actions were cumulative of testimony.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State v. Stephens


SC 18702


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 791; 22 A.3d 1262; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 285


March 21, 2011, Argued 
August, 2, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with violation of probation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; judgment revoking the defendant's probation, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was placed on probation after he pled guilty to possession of child pornography. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) revoked his probation based on its findings that he violated the special sex offender conditions of his probation. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's computer had nude photos of his ex-girlfriend which had been accessed while he was on probation. The trial court found he violated a special condition of probation that he not possess sexually stimulating material deemed inappropriate by a probation officer. The high court rejected his claims that the condition was unconstitutionally overbroad on its face and thus impinged on his constitutional right to privacy; the overbreadth doctrine applied only to claims of a violation of U.S. Const. amend. I. The condition was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-193(14)--which he was presumed to know--banned the possession of images of the "lascivious exhibition of the genitals" that appeared in the photos of his ex-girlfriend, which would reasonably have been deemed sexually explicit under any definition of pornography. His conduct fell so clearly within the core meaning of the special condition that there could be no substantial concern as to its arbitrary enforcement. Evidence that, inter alia, he did not try to delete the photos and that they had been accessed during his probation was sufficient to support revocation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ryder


SC 18411


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 810; 23 A.3d 694; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 287


March 14, 2011, Argued 
August 9, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crime of risk of injury to a child and with the infraction of illegal possession of a reptile, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Tyma, J., denied the defendant's motions to dismiss the charges and to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Devlin, J., on a plea of nolo contendere to the charge of illegal possession of a reptile; subsequently, the state nolled the charge of risk of injury to a child; judgment of guilty of illegal possession of a reptile, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Beach and West, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Ryder, 114 Conn. App. 528, 969 A.2d 818, 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 201 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with risk of injury to a child and illegal possession of a reptile. Defendant's motion to suppress evidence and dismiss the charges was denied. Defendant pled nolo contendere to the reptile charge and was ordered to pay a $ 35 fine, and the State nolled the risk of injury charge. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Defendant was granted certification to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the appellate court improperly concluded that the warrantless search of his house did not violate his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures under the Fourth Amendment. He contended that the police intrusion into his house was not warranted under the emergency doctrine because a reasonable police officer in the circumstances would not have believed that a warrantless entry was necessary to assist a person in need of immediate aid, and that the exception was not satisfied when the officer stepped over the gate to the house into defendant's curtilage area. The supreme court agreed with defendant, first concluding that the warrantless search began when the officer stepped over the gate onto defendant's curtilage, an area in which defendant had a reasonable expectation of privacy and which was protected by the Fourth Amendment. The supreme court further concluded that a reasonable officer in the officer's position would not have believed an emergency existed justifying the warrantless entry. The possibility a 16-year-old son was disobeying his father did not imply a danger to human life, destruction of evidence, or the flight of a suspect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed.

State v. Lenarz


SC 18561


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 417; 22 A.3d 536; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 350


October 28, 2010, Argued 
July 19, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Conn. v. Lenarz, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 723 (U.S., Jan. 17, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute informations in three cases charging the defendant in each case with two counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child and one count of the crime of sexual assault in the fourth degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number thirteen, and transferred to geographical area number twelve, where the court, Olear, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the charges in the first two cases and consolidated all three cases for trial; thereafter, the cases were tried to the jury before Olear, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count of risk of injury to a child in the first case, and verdicts and judgments of not guilty of the remaining charges in the first case and of the charges in the second and third cases, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Lenarz, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3541 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 5, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford, Geographical Area Number 12 (Connecticut), which convicted him of risk of injury to a child, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1), and otherwise found him not guilty of other charged offenses arising in three consolidated matters. The trial court had denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with six counts of risk of injury to a child in three separate informations, which were consolidated for trial. Defendant's computer was seized by police and searched by the State forensics laboratory. Defendant obtained a court order that any communications between himself and his counsel on the computer were to remain unpublished and unread. However, defendant learned that the prosecutor was in possession of and had read certain written materials seized from the computer that discussed defendant's trial strategy with respect to two of the cases. Defendant's motion to dismiss the informations based on the claim that the State intentionally invaded the attorney-client privilege, thereby violating his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI, was denied upon the trial court's determination that the intrusion was unintentional and that defendant was not prejudiced. Defendant was convicted of one charge after a jury trial. On appeal, the court found that dismissal was warranted. Defendant was presumptively prejudiced by the prosecutor's intrusion into his privileged communications, whether the intrusion was intentional or not, and the taint was irreversible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with respect to defendant's conviction, and remanded the matter with directions for the trial court to grant defendant's motion to dismiss that charge and to render judgment thereon. The remainder of the trial court judgment was affirmed.

Morgan v. Hartford Hosp.


SC 18469


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 388; 21 A.3d 451; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 276


March 17, 2011, Argued 
July 12, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Morgan v. Hartford Hosp., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1324 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 21, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrators filed a medical malpractice action against multiple defendants, including a thoracic surgeon and a surgical group (collectively, the surgeons). The trial court (Connecticut) dismissed the complaint on the ground that the written opinion letter attached to the original complaint did not satisfy the requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(a). The administrators appealed.


OVERVIEW: In an attempt to comply with § 52-190a(a), which required a medical malpractice plaintiff to attach to the complaint a written opinion of a similar health care provider attesting to a good faith basis for the action, the administrators attached to their original complaint an opinion letter from a physician who was board certified in internal medicine with a subspecialty in cardiovascular disease. Over a year later, the administrators filed an amended complaint and also attached a written opinion letter from a vascular surgeon. The surgeons failed to move to dismiss the original complaint until more than 19 months after the administrators had commenced the action. The good faith certificate and written opinion letter required by § 52-190a were requirements of process, which the surgeons waived pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-32, by failing to file a motion to dismiss within the thirty day time period provided in Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-30. By failing to timely file a motion to dismiss, the surgeons thus waived their right to challenge the sufficiency of the original complaint and the original written opinion letter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with direction to deny the surgeons' motion to dismiss and for further proceedings according to law.

 

105 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dayner v. Archdiocese of Hartford


SC 18468


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 759; 23 A.3d 1192; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 286; 32 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1020


March 16, 2011, Argued 
August 2, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the allegedly wrongful termination of the plaintiff's employment, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Aurigemma, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss, and the defendants appealed.
Dayner v. Archdiocese of Hartford, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 606 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 11, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former principal of a parish school, sued defendants, the parish's pastor and an archdiocese, asserting claims of, inter alia, wrongful termination, breach of implied contract, and promissory estoppel. Defendants moved to dismiss on grounds the suit was barred by the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), denied the motion; defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that plaintiff's lawsuit was barred under the ministerial exception to the court's subject matter jurisdiction over employment disputes between religious institutions and their leaders. The high court held that the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss on the ground of a colorable claim to immunity under the ministerial exception was an appealable final judgment. Plaintiff's duties as a principal of a religious school rendered her a ministerial employee. Her claims of promissory estoppel, breach of implied contract, and breach of the implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing were barred by the ministerial exception as they essentially asked the trial court to police the archdiocese's compliance with its own internal procedures. Her claims of wrongful termination, negligent infliction of emotional distress, and tortious interference with business expectancies were also barred by the ministerial exception because they arose from defendants' decision to fire plaintiff, and requiring the trial court to determine whether any proffered religious reasons were a pretext for unlawful action would amount to judging the archdiocese's employment decisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment dismissing plaintiff's complaint.

 

106 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tabone


SC 18581


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 708; 23 A.3d 689; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 278


April 28, 2011, Argued 
July 26, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree, sexual assault in the third degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the defendant was presented to the court, Damiani, J., on a plea of guilty; thereafter, the court rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the defendant's plea; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, and the defendant appealed; thereafter, this court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for resentencing; on remand, the court, Damiani, J., resentenced the defendant, and the defendant appealed; subsequently, this court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for resentencing; thereafter, the court, Damiani, J., denied the defendant's motion to withdraw his plea and resentenced the defendant, and the defendant appealed.
State v. Tabone, 292 Conn. 417, 973 A.2d 74, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 201 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury (Connecticut) convicted defendant, on his guilty pleas, of second- and third-degree sexual assault and risk of injury to a child, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1)(A), (4), and 53-21(2). Defendant appealed. On remand, the trial court resentenced defendant. Defendant appealed. On second remand, the trial court denied a motion to withdraw the pleas. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On second remand for resentencing in accordance with the aggregate package theory, the appellate court suggested that, upon remand, defendant could have been sentenced to a total effective sentence of ten years incarceration followed by nine years of special parole. It left the ultimate sentencing decision, however, to the trial court. Thereafter, defendant filed his motion to withdraw his guilty pleas pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 39-26 and 39-27(2). After hearing argument on the motion to withdraw the pleas, the trial court denied the motion on its merits and, thereafter, resentenced defendant for a second time. However, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty pleas because the motion was beyond the scope of the appellate court's remand for resentencing. Because the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court solely for resentencing, the trial court's authority was limited to that task and, accordingly, the trial court should have dismissed defendant's motion to withdraw the pleas rather than denied it on its merits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case with direction to dismiss defendant's motion to withdraw his pleas.

Housatonic R.R. Co. v. Comm'r of Revenue Servs.


SC 18685


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 268; 21 A.3d 759; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 238


February 10, 2011, Argued 
June 28, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the defendant denying the plaintiff's request for a refund of certain money paid in connection with a distributor's gross earnings on the sale of petroleum products, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, where the court, Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Housatonic R.R. Co. v. Law, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1646 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 24, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain, Tax Session (Connecticut), granted defendant Commissioner of Revenue Services motion to dismiss plaintiff rail carrier's appeal of the Commission's decision denying the carrier's request for a refund of money paid to a distributor to cover the cost of a petroleum fuel products gross earning tax imposed on the distributor under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 12-587(b)(1). The carrier appealed.


OVERVIEW: The carrier bought fuel from the distributor, who separately billed the carrier for the tax it paid pursuant to § 12-587(b)(1). Although the carrier paid that amount directly to the distributor, it submitted a refund request, claiming that the tax was discriminatory because interstate water carriers were exempt from the tax, while rail carriers were not. The commission denied the refund request on the ground that the carrier was not the taxpayer. The lower court correctly held that the doctrine of sovereign immunity barred the carrier's action because it failed to establish statutory authority to bring the appeal. Although the lower court incorrectly concluded that the Railroad Revitalization and Regulatory Reform Act (the 4-R Act), 49 U.S.C.S. § 11501 et seq., applied only to ad valorem taxes of property, the carrier's request for relief exceeded that permitted under the 4-R Act because the 4-R Act did not provide for refunds of taxes already paid. Further, the carrier was not entitled to seek a refund from the State under Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. §§ 12-33 or -597 because only Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 12-597 applied and the carrier was not a taxpayer within the meaning § 12-597.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
