State v. Long


SC 18282


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 216; 19 A.3d 1242; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 227


January 13, 2011, Argued 
June 21, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Long v. Conn., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8790 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for an order to extend the commitment of the defendant, who had been found not guilty of the crime of assault in the second degree by reason of mental disease or defect, to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, geographical area number fourteen, where the court, Miano, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss the petition and rendered judgment thereon, from which the state appealed; thereafter, this court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings; subsequently, the court, Blue, J., granted the state's petition for an order of continued commitment, denied the defendant's motion to dismiss, extended the commitment of the defendant to the jurisdiction of the psychiatric security review board for three years, and rendered judgment thereon, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Long, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1690 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 7, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c), the State petitioned to continue the commitment of defendant acquittee to the psychiatric security review board. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford, Connecticut, denied defendant's motion to dismiss and granted the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant had been found not guilty of second-degree assault by reason of mental disease or defect and his mental health was assessed, the trial court had ordered his commitment for five years. On four occasions, the State had successfully petitioned to continue his commitment. The trial court had granted defendant's motion to dismiss the State's fifth petition, concluding that § 17a-593(c) was unconstitutional. The high court had reversed, finding, inter alia, that defendant's equal protection rights had not been violated. On remand, the trial court granted the State's petition. This appeal followed. The high court held that the doctrine of res judicata precluded defendant's facial challenge in the present case because the claim in the instant appeal was the same claim he had raised in the first: that an acquittee's commitment under the board's jurisdiction, rather than under the system for civil commitment, violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. And because he did not distinguish his as applied challenge from his facial challenge, the decision in the prior appeal also disposed of his as applied challenge to § 17a-593(c).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

110 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Flores


SC 18592


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 77; 17 A.3d 1025; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 188


October 18, 2010, Argued 
May 24, 2011, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Flores, 2014 Conn. App. LEXIS 37 (Conn. App. Ct., Feb. 1, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, burglary in the second degree, and conspiracy to commit burglary in the second degree, and with two counts of the crime of larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Hon. John F. Mulcahy, Jr., judge trial referee; verdict of guilty; thereafter, Hon. John F. Mulcahy, Jr., judge trial referee, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) convicted defendant, upon a jury's verdict, of first-degree kidnapping and robbery, conspiracy to commit first-degree robbery, second-degree burglary, conspiracy to commit second-degree burglary, and two counts of third-degree larceny, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-92(a)(2)(B), 53a-8(a), 53a-134(a)(4), 53a-48(a), 53a-102(a)(2), and 53a-124(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court failed to instruct the jury, in accordance with State v. Salamon, that a person could not be convicted of kidnapping unless it found beyond a reasonable doubt that the restraint or movement involved in the kidnapping was not merely incidental to the commission of another crime. Furthermore, the impropriety of the omission of the Salamon instruction was not harmless because a properly instructed jury reasonably could have concluded that the restraint of the victim was incidental to the commission of the robbery. The jury reasonably could have found that the victim was neither bound nor physically moved during the commission of the robbery, that she was restrained on her bed for no more than five minutes while defendant and his accomplices searched the room for valuables, and that the victim was released immediately after the robbery was complete. Finally, the court could not preclude the reasonable possibility that a jury could have found that the degree of force or intimidation imposed on the victim was not greater than that necessary to commit the underlying robbery. Accordingly, defendant was entitled to a new trial on the kidnapping charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to defendant's conviction on the kidnapping charge and the case was remanded for a new trial on that charge. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

 

111 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Markley v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


SC 18750


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


301 Conn. 56; 23 A.3d 668; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 190


March 23, 2011, Argued 
May 24, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to enjoin the defendants from enforcing a financing order issued by the named defendant directing certain public utility companies to retain the competitive transition assessment that it charges customers and to transfer the proceeds from such increase to the state's general fund, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Cohn, J., granted the defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and rendered judgment dismissing the action, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Markley v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3373 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 21, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ratepayer brought suit seeking to enjoin defendant department from enforcing a financing order issued by it directing certain public utility companies to retain the competitive transition assessment that it charged customers and to transfer the proceeds from such increase to the state's general fund. The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut), dismissed the action. The ratepayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the ratepayer's claims were barred by sovereign immunity. The ratepayer alleged that the department exceeded its statutory authority in issuing the financing order, because the charges were, in effect, an unauthorized tax. However, the appellate court found that the ratepayer failed to establish an equal protection claim under Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, and, accordingly, that the constitutional sovereign immunity exception did not apply. The ratepayer argued simply that: (1) the charges arbitrarily applied to the distributor's customers but not to municipal payers, and (2) the order inequitably distributed the burden between the power company and the customers. Those allegations were insufficient. Further, the legislature had a rational basis for structuring the bond program as it did, namely, to distribute broadly the burden of deficit reduction while ensuring that no payers would be forced to pay more each month than the fee they had already been paying. The antecedent question of whether to tie deficit reduction to the taxpayer's electricity purchases was a policy issue that rested with the legislature and lay beyond the purview of the court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

112 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. B.B.


SC 18481


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


300 Conn. 748; 17 A.3d 30; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 154


October 25, 2010, Argued 
May 10, 2011, Officially Released


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, was charged with possession of a weapon in a motor vehicle, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-38(a). Appellant was arraigned on the youthful offender docket. The Superior Court (Connecticut) found probable cause for his arrest, and then granted the State's motion to transfer the case from the youthful offender docket to the regular criminal docket, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-76c(b)(1). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in granting the motion to transfer because he had a liberty interest in his status as a defendant on the youthful offender docket, and due process thus entitled him to a hearing before transfer. The appellate court agreed that appellant had a liberty interest in his status as a defendant on the youthful offender docket, but the failure to hold a hearing before the transfer did not deprive him of his right to due process. Appellant's due process right was satisfied by the requirement in § 54-76c(b) of a hearing before the court on the regular criminal docket before the finalization of the transfer. Section 54-76c(b)(1) did not require notice and a hearing before a case may be transferred from the youthful offender docket to the regular criminal docket, but implicitly required a hearing on the regular criminal docket before finalization of a transfer from the youthful offender docket. Although appellant was not provided with a hearing on the youthful offender docket, the transfer had not yet been finalized. Before that occurred, appellant was entitled to a hearing on the regular criminal docket.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

113 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hong Pham v. Starkowski


SC 18582


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


300 Conn. 412; 16 A.3d 635; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 102


November 30, 2010, Argued 
April 5, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Action to enjoin the defendant from terminating certain state funded medical assistance to indigent legal aliens pursuant to recently enacted legislation, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Miller, J., granted the plaintiff's motion for class certification; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court; judgment for the plaintiff, from which the defendant appealed. Reversed; judgment directed.
Hong Pham v. Starkowski, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3470 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 18, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff legal immigrant, in a class action, sued defendant commissioner of social services (commissioner) in the trial court (Connecticut), alleging Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17b-192 and 17b-257b violated federal and state equal protection provisions by terminating certain state-funded medical assistance for class members. The trial court held the statutes violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and the commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After enacting state-funded programs giving class members medical benefits, the legislature effectively eliminated them. The supreme court held Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-192 did not violate equal protection, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Conn. Const. art. I, § 20, when applying strict scrutiny, because the members were not, due to alienage, denied benefits given to citizens, as (1) the eliminated programs only benefited aliens, so eliminating them did not discriminate between aliens and citizens, (2) citizens' eligibility for benefits under the state-federal Medicaid program did not make elimination of the state programs violate equal protection since the state did not control Medicaid eligibility, and (3) discriminating among different alien groups due to some aliens' continued eligibility was not due to suspect factors. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-257b, altering eligibility guidelines for a state medical assistance program such that the members were ineligible, did not violate equal protection because it created no classification based on alienage, as the guidelines applied equally to aliens and citizens by making those categorically eligible for Medicaid ineligible for the program.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded with direction to render judgment for the commissioner.

Keane v. Fischetti


SC 18377, SC 18379


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


300 Conn. 395; 13 A.3d 1089; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 72; 32 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 373


December 8, 2010, Argued 
March 15, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action in the first case to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' alleged negligence, and action in the second case to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged negligence of the named defendant et al., and for other relief, each brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the city of Waterbury intervened as a plaintiff in both cases; thereafter, the court, Brunetti, J., granted the defendants' motions to strike the complaint in the first case; subsequently, the cases were consolidated; thereafter, the court, Brunetti, J., granted the defendants' motions to strike the complaint in the second case; subsequently, the court, Brunetti, J., granted the motions for judgment filed by the named defendant et al. in the first and second cases and rendered judgment for the defendants in the first case, from which the plaintiff in the first case appealed, and rendered judgment for the defendants in the second case, from which the plaintiffs in the second case filed a separate appeal; thereafter, the appeals were consolidated for oral argument.
Keane v. Fischetti, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3224 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 11, 2008)
Mahony v. Fischetti, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3215 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 10, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a deceased firefighter's administratrix and an injured firefighter, sued defendants other firefighters in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) due to a motor vehicle accident in the scope of the firefighters' employment. The trial court granted motions to strike the complaints due to limits on such suits imposed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-308(b) and entered judgment for defendants. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs said the statute violated equal protection. The supreme court, assuming without deciding that firefighters were similarly situated to other municipal employees, held the statute discriminated against firefighters in favor of other municipal employees by barring firefighters eligible for workers' compensation from suing other firefighters for negligence arising from motor vehicle accidents in the scope of employment because other municipal employees could bring such suits against coworkers, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-465(a). The classification survived equal protection rational basis scrutiny because reducing municipal liability and fostering the provision of effective firefighting services were legitimate governmental objectives, and the legislature reasonably could conclude that litigation between firefighters arising from motor vehicle accidents was a greater risk to municipal liability than such litigation between other municipal employees, as (1) firefighters were more likely to operate large vehicles under emergency conditions, and (2) a threat of such litigation might deter volunteers from acting as firefighters.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed.

State v. Campbell


SC 18453


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


300 Conn. 368; 13 A.3d 661; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 43


November 30, 2010, Argued 
March 8, 2011, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree and carrying a dangerous weapon, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Devlin, J.; verdict of guilty of carrying a dangerous weapon; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for a new trial and for a judgment of acquittal, and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Gruendel, Lavine and Peters, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of carrying a dangerous weapon. The trial court denied defendant's motions for a new trial and for a judgment of acquittal, and rendered judgment in accordance with the jury verdict. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to several violence incidents on the university campus where defendant was a student, defendant regularly carried a switchblade knife. Defendant went to someone else's room to hang out and, after making a joke at the room occupant's expense, was asked to leave by the occupant. Thereafter a fight ensued and defendant stabbed the victim four times. The issue before the supreme court was whether Conn. Gen. Defendant contended that the exception was not limited to long knives. The State contended that, to the contrary, because § 53-206(b)(3) expressly referred to "the carrying of a knife, the edged portion of the blade of which is four inches or over in length," the exception plainly and unambiguously applied only to that weapon. The supreme court agreed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

Raftopol v. Ramey


SC 18482


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 681; 12 A.3d 783; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 11


March 16, 2010, Argued 
January 5, 2011, **Officially Released


** January 5, 2011, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to validate the gestational carrier agreement executed by the plaintiffs and the named defendant and for an order directing the defendant department of health to issue a replacement birth certificate naming the plaintiffs as the legal parents of the twin children born through their gestational carrier, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Hon. James G. Kenefick, Jr., judge trial referee, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment declaring that the plaintiffs were the legal parents of the children and ordering the defendant department of health to issue a birth certificate naming the plaintiffs as the legal parents, and the defendant department of health appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Department of Health, appealed from the judgment from the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) that declared plaintiff, a nongenetic, intended parent, as a legal parent of children born through a gestational carrier and ordered the Department to issue a replacement birth certificate, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-48a, naming the intended parent as the legal parent of the children.


OVERVIEW: The intended parent and his partner, who was the children's biological father, entered into a gestational agreement with the carrier. Prior to the delivery date, the intended parent filed a declaratory judgment action, seeking a determination he was a legal parent of the children and an order directing the Department to issue a replacement birth certificate. The Department argued § 7-48a did not confer parental status on a nongenetic, intended parent. The state supreme court assumed, without deciding, the gestational agreement was valid. After analyzing the text and legislative history of § 7-48a, the court concluded the legislature intended § 7-48a to confer parental status on an intended parent who was a party to a valid gestational agreement irrespective of that intended parent's genetic relationship to the children. Such intended parents did not have to adopt the children in order to become legal parents. They acquired that status by operation of law, upon an order by a court of competent jurisdiction pursuant to § 7-48a. Thus, the trial court properly ordered the Department to issue a replacement birth certificate listing the intended parent as a legal parent of the children.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Luurtsema v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 18383


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 740; 12 A.3d 817; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 12


September 21, 2010, Argued 
January 5, 2011, * Officially Released


* January 5, 2011, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Luurtsema #79814 v. Warden, State Prison, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1400 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Nazzaro, J., pursuant to the parties' stipulation, reserved two questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court concerning whether two recent decisions of the Supreme Court applied to the petitioner's habeas corpus proceedings; thereafter, the reservation was transferred to this court.
State v. Luurtsema, 262 Conn. 179, 811 A.2d 223, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 492 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner inmate's kidnapping conviction under a prior interpretation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A) was affirmed, he sought habeas corpus relief, due to a later interpretation of the statute. The trial court reserved two questions of law for the advice of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) concerning the application of two Connecticut Supreme Court decisions, and the reservation was transferred to the Connecticut Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate's conviction, the statute was reinterpreted to require proof of an intent to restrain a victim beyond that required to commit an underlying crime. The supreme court held the reinterpretation applied retroactively as a matter of state retroactivity common law because (1) the reinterpretation substantively determined the elements of kidnapping, and (2) the inmate was convicted of a crime he arguably did not commit. A per se retroactivity rule was not proper because cases existed in which denying retroactive relief might not be arbitrary or unjust. The State's reliance on the prior interpretation did not make retroactive relief improper because nothing showed the State would have charged the inmate differently under the reinterpretation. A claim that retroactivity would flood the court system with habeas petitions did not make it improper because nothing showed it would impose an unmanageable burden. It was not proper to deny relief when the passage of time barred retrying some cases because inmates would still serve sentences for underlying crimes. The reinterpretation applied retroactively to the inmate because the rationales favoring full retroactivity applied.


OUTCOME: The reserved questions were answered in the affirmative.

St. Paul Travelers Cos. v. Kuehl


SC 18387


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 800; 12 A.3d 852; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 13


October 19, 2010, Argued 
January 5, 2011*, Officially Released


* January 5, 2011, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to declare as unconstitutional a Public Act that permitted the refiling of certain claims for survivor's benefits that previously had been dismissed as untimely, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Bryant, J., granted the motion to intervene as party defendants filed by Rosalind J. Koskoff et al.; thereafter, Hon. Jerry Wagner, judge trial referee, denied the intervening defendants' motion to dismiss, granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon in favor of the plaintiff, from which the intervening defendants appealed.
St. Paul Travelers Cos. v. Kuehl, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1473 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 27, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff workers' compensation carrier filed a declaratory judgment suit seeking a ruling that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-294c(d) was unconstitutional. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) denied the motion to dismiss filed by intervening defendant law firm for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, and granted the carrier's motion for summary judgment, concluding that § 31-294c(d) violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The firm appealed. The state's highest court held that § 31-294c(a) was subject matter jurisdictional. The claimant's failure to file a notice of claim within the time limit, and the failure of the notice of claim to fall under a § 31-294c exception deprived the commissioner of subject matter jurisdiction. Section 31-294c(d) merely created an additional exception to the limitations period. The carrier's legal interest in the declaratory judgment action was in being protected from defending against a stale claim. That interest was injured by § 31-294c(d). The carrier had standing to bring the declaratory judgment action. The carrier was not required to proceed to the merits before filing the declaratory judgment suit. The only way to determine whether the carrier could obtain the relief it sought was to resolve the constitutional challenge, which the commissioner could not do. That § 31-294c(a) simultaneously protected the carrier from defending against the stale claim and was a prerequisite for the commissioner's jurisdiction rendered further proceedings before the commissioner futile. The holding that § 31-294c(d) was unconstitutional was not challenged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

119 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DiGiovanna v. St. George


SC 17624


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


300 Conn. 59; 12 A.3d 900; 2011 Conn. LEXIS 27


October 18, 2010, Argued 
January 5, 2011, *Officially Released


* January 5, 2011, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended application for the right to visitation of the defendant's minor child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Abery-Wetstone, J., issued orders specifying that a guardian ad litem was to assist the court in determining whether the plaintiff satisfied the requirements for non-parent visitation and ordering a psychological evaluation of the plaintiff and the defendant; following the court's evaluation of the information, the court determined that although the plaintiff had satisfied the requirements for visitation, it was not in the best interest of the child for the plaintiff to have visitation rights with the child and, accordingly, rendered judgment denying the plaintiff's application, and the plaintiff appealed.
DiGiovanna v. St. George Donna, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3180 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 26, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59, plaintiff, a nonparent, filed an application for visitation with defendant mother's minor child. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), denied the application; plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the parties' romantic relationship ended, the mother, learning that plaintiff intended to seek visitation with her son, cut off plaintiff's contact with him. This suit followed. Plaintiff alleged that he had functioned as the child's father; that terminating this relationship would cause the child serious, irreparable harm; and that the mother was psychologically unstable. The trial court, which had concerns about the mother's mental health, found that plaintiff met his burden of proof under Roth v. Weston to obtain visitation, but that visitation would not be in the child's best interest because the mother would react by inflicting greater psychological harm on the child than that which would result from the denial of visitation. The high court held that the best interest of the child standard could not overcome the Roth standard for ordering visitation. The trial court, in effect, sanctioned the mother's inflicting harm akin to abuse or neglect and allowed her to prevail in a case in which she had lost on the merits. It failed to consider its authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-56(i) to order her to undergo counseling to aid her in coming to terms with its decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to render judgment in favor of plaintiff and to conduct a new dispositional hearing.

 

120 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ciarlelli v. Town of Hamden


SC 18201


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 265; 8 A.3d 1093; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 462


January 9, 2009, Argued 
December 21, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the workers' compensation commissioner for the third district dismissing the plaintiff's claim for benefits as untimely, brought to the compensation review board, which affirmed the commissioner's decision, and the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The workers' compensation commissioner dismissed plaintiff police officer's claim for hypertension benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c as barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-294c(a)'s one-year limitations period. The Connecticut Workers' Compensation Review Board affirmed; plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The commission found plaintiff's claim for hypertension benefits untimely because he failed to file it within one year of learning of his elevated blood pressure readings. Plaintiff argued that his hypertension was not an accidental injury for which a claim had to be filed within one year of the injury, but a repetitive trauma injury for which a claim had to be filed within one year from the last day of his employment. The high court disagreed. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-275(16)(A), a repetitive trauma injury required proof of a causal connection to employment; as such proof was lacking, the Board properly treated his claim as one for accidental injury definitely located in time and place. However, the Board incorrectly concluded that under § 7-433c a claimant had to file a notice of claim within one year from the date that he knew or should have known that he had symptoms of hypertension. Evidence that plaintiff knew of past elevated blood pressure readings was not sufficient to trigger § 31-294c(a)'s one-year limitations period limitation period in absence of evidence he had been diagnosed with hypertension by a medical professional and had been informed of that diagnosis.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Board was reversed and the case was remanded to the Board with direction to reverse the decision of the commissioner and to remand the case to the commissioner for further proceedings.

Kaddah v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 18565


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 129; 7 A.3d 911; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 432


September 10, 2010, Argued 
November 30, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland, where the court, Nazzaro, J., rendered judgment dismissing the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed. Appeal dismissed.
Kaddah v. Comm'r of Corr., 105 Conn. App. 430, 939 A.2d 1185, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 18 (Jan. 22, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate's habeas petition in the trial court (Connecticut) sought reinstatement of a withdrawn appeal from a prior court's refusal to certify dismissal of a prior habeas petition for appeal. The trial court summarily dismissed the current petition, under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 23-29(3), and denied certification to appeal. The case was transferred from the Appellate Court (Connecticut) to the Connecticut Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's current and former habeas petitions alleged counsel at trial and on appeal of his criminal convictions provided ineffective assistance. The supreme court held the inmate's appeal had to be dismissed because the allegations of his petition were insufficient to state a claim for the relief he sought, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 23-29(2), as he simply repeated the ineffective assistance allegations of his first petition, but those claims were unrelated to the relief he sought since (1) neither his trial or appellate counsel represented him regarding his withdrawn appeal, (2) he did not allege ineffective assistance of counsel who represented him when his appeal was withdrawn, and (3) he did not allege that withdrawal resulted from any constitutional impairment, so his failure to exhaust his state court remedies did not result from any unconstitutional impairment of his right to appeal but from his own decision to withdraw the appeal from the denial of his first petition.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

State v. Garcia


SC 18465


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


299 Conn. 39; 7 A.3d 355; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 411


March 25, 2010, Argued 
November 16, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the court, Miano, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Miano, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) found defendant guilty of one count each of robbery in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(4), and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree in violation of § 53a-134(a)(4) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-48(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress a written statement given to police, as the trial court incorrectly determined that defendant was not in custody when he made his statement; that the statement was not the product of police coercion and was given knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily; and the statement was admissible even though it was given to and translated by a bilingual officer rather than a qualified interpreter. The supreme court found no error. Among other things, the trial court found that defendant was not in custody because he came to the police department on his own accord and made a knowing, intelligent, and voluntary waiver of his Miranda rights. The supreme court further noted that even if defendant were in custody, his statement was admissible because he had voluntarily waived his Miranda rights. The trial court rejected defendant's testimony that he never saw or signed the Miranda rights car, the voluntary statement form, or his statement that he had been assaulted by an officer. Finally, the supreme court found that the statement had been properly authenticated by the officer who took and translated the statement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

123 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Butts v. Bysiewicz


SC 18663


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


298 Conn. 665; 5 A.3d 932; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 383


September 15, 2010, Argued 
October 26, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to enjoin the defendant from publishing the list of candidates for the November, 2010 general election and to compel the defendant to place the plaintiff's name on the ballot as the endorsed Democratic candidate for judge of probate for the thirty-second probate district, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, and tried to the court, Prescott, J.; judgment for the defendant denying the plaintiff's request for a permanent injunction, and the plaintiff, upon certification by the Chief Justice pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a that a matter of substantial public interest is at issue, appealed to this court; thereafter, the court, Prescott, J., issued an articulation of its decision.
Butts v. Bysiewicz, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2192 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 27, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate filed suit to enjoin defendant, the Connecticut Secretary of State, from publishing the list of candidates for a general election and to compel her to place his name on the ballot as the nominee of a political party. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) denied plaintiff's request for an injunction, from which he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The party endorsed plaintiff as its candidate for judge. He was required under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-388 to deliver to defendant a certificate attesting to the party's endorsement by the 14th day following the convention. The secretary of the convention delivered the certificate to a post office clerk and paid the proper postage to send it by first class mail to defendant's office. Though the envelope bore the correct address and return address, it was not received by defendant's office nor was it returned to the sender. Learning that defendant had not received the certificate, plaintiff delivered a substitute original certificate to her office after the deadline expired. The high court held that compliance with § 9-388's deadline for delivering the certificate was mandatory and was established by actual receipt of the certificate. Defendant had no discretion to give legal effect to the substitute certificate since it was not timely delivered. Because the legislature required strict compliance with the deadline of § 9-388, the trial court could not invoke its equitable authority to compel defendant to act in direct contravention to this clear legislative mandate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lockhart


SC 17773


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


298 Conn. 537; 4 A.3d 1176; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 354; 69 A.L.R.6th 793


December 1, 2009, Argued 
October 12, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of murder, felony murder, robbery in the first degree and larceny in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex at Middletown, and tried to the jury before Holzberg, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54c, robbery in the first degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-134(a)(1) and (3), and larceny in the third degree under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-124(a)(1). The Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex at Middletown (Connecticut) sentenced him to a total effective term of 80 years incarceration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the United States Constitution and the Connecticut Constitution required law enforcement agents to record electronically, whenever feasible, custodial interrogations, Miranda warnings and any resulting statements made by a defendant; and that the State violated his right to remain silent by introducing testimony regarding his refusal to sign a Miranda rights acknowledgment card, refusal to provide a written statement, termination of an interview, and assertion of his right to remain silent. The supreme court found no errors. The supreme court held that because the text of the provisions on which defendant relied made no reference to a corroboration requirement for the admissibility of confessions and because, according to Connecticut case law, those provisions did not provide broader protections than their federal counterparts, those factors did not support defendant's claim that a recording requirement was mandated by Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 9. Defendant's right to remain silent was not violated, as his refusal to sign the Miranda rights card was not an invocation of his right to remain silent, and most significantly, defendant did not remain silent.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Jenkins


SC 18077


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


298 Conn. 209; 3 A.3d 806; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 304


October 28, 2009, Argued 
September 7, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with, inter alia, the crime of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Alexander, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Handy, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, McLachlan and Gruendel, Js., with Schaller, J., dissenting, which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to grant the defendant's motion to suppress and for further proceedings, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Jenkins, 104 Conn. App. 417, 934 A.2d 281, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 418 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, defendant pled nolo contendere to possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and was sentenced to 20 years imprisonment, executed suspended after eight years, and five years probation. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the appellate court improperly relied on an inadequate record and reached out to decide claims not properly raised before the trial court, specifically whether the officer improperly patted down defendant before obtaining consent to search the car. The supreme court agreed, concluding that defendant's failure to litigate the validity of the patdown search during the suppression hearing rendered the record inadequate for Golding review. The State also argued that the appellate court improperly concluded that, under the federal constitution, the scope or length of the traffic stop must be limited to its initial purpose. The supreme court agreed, concluding that the officer's questions, including his request for consent to search, were permissible, as they did not measurably extend the duration of the traffic stop. In addition, despite the officer's failure to inform defendant that he had the right to refuse to consent to the search, the supreme court found defendant's consent to be voluntary. The scope of defendant's consent was not limited to an invitation to check for beer on the floor by the passenger seat, but extended to the passenger compartment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed. The case was remanded to the appellate court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Cyrus


SC 18326


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 829; 1 A.3d 59; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 281


March 24, 2010, Argued 
August 17, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crime of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, operating a motor vehicle without carrying an operator's license, and operating a motor vehicle with an obstructed view, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, where the court, Robaina, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the court rendered judgment dismissing the charges, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Flynn, C. J., and Beach and Peters, Js., which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Cyrus, 111 Conn. App. 482, 959 A.2d 1054, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 548 (2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirming the trial court's dismissal of the charges against the defendant for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a (2005), operating a motor vehicle without carrying an operator's license under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-213, and operating a motor vehicle with an obstructed view under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-99f(c).


OVERVIEW: The State claimed that the appellate court improperly upheld the trial court's conclusion that the state trooper who arrested defendant lacked a reasonable and articulable suspicion to stop defendant to investigate a possible violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-99f(c), in contravention of Terry. Defendant responded that the State lacked the reasonable and articulable suspicion required by Terry for stopping him and that the appellate court properly determined, in essence, that the mere fact that defendant had a cross hanging from the rearview mirror of the car that he was driving did not give rise to a reasonable and articulable suspicion by the officer stopping the car that he was violating § 14-99f (c). The supreme court concluded that the record reflected that the State failed to establish the requisite evidentiary record in support of that standard. There was no testimony by the officer that he had in fact relief upon objectively certifiable qualities of the items hanging from rear view mirror that made them distracting or that interfered with the driver's view. The eight to ten inch chain was not large enough by any objective measure to prove it would obstruct a driver's view.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

State v. Michael A.


SC 18464


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 808; 1 A.3d 46; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 280


March 22, 2010, Argued 
August 17, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and risk of injury to a child and, in the second part, with being a persistent serious felony offender, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before Cremins, J.; verdict of guilty of the lesser included offense of sexual assault in the second degree and risk of injury to a child; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the second part of the information; judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Rogers and Pellegrino, Js., which reversed the conviction of sexual assault in the second degree and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty as to that offense only; subsequently, after a hearing, the court, Cremins, J., resentenced the defendant on the count of risk of injury to a child as enhanced by the persistent serious felony offender statute, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Michael A., 99 Conn. App. 251, 913 A.2d 1081, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 28 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of risk of injury to a child and sexual assault in the second degree. Defendant entered a plea of nolo contendere to being a persistent serious felony offender. The appellate court reversed the sexual assault conviction and remanded the case for resentencing. Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) resentencing him to 17 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the remand order explicitly was limited to reversal of the sexual assault conviction and did not authorize the trial court to fashion a new sentence. The supreme court agreed with the State, that the trial court properly resentenced defendant under the aggregate package theory, allowing the trial court to reconstruct the sentence to ensure that the punishment fit the crime and defendant, as long as the final sentence did not exceed the original sentence. Defendant also claimed that the resentencing order was improper because he did not knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waive his right to a jury trial on the issue of whether an extended period of incarceration would best serve the public interest. The supreme court concluded the defendant's original nolo contendere plea on the persistent felony offender charge necessarily and validly waived his right to a jury trial as to his guilt and the public interest determination. The trial court provided defendant with ample disclosure of the risks and identified the right to a jury trial as a right he was surrendering. The supreme court further concluded that the waiver applied to the resentencing proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Hedge


SC 18161


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 621; 1 A.3d 1051; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 275


December 2, 2008, Argued 
August 3, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Hedge v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1693 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 25, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of cocaine with intent to sell by a person who is not drug dependent, possession of opium with intent to sell by a person who is not drug dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a public housing project and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; thereafter, the court dismissed the charge of possession of opium with intent to sell by a person who is not drug dependent; subsequently, verdict of guilty of failure to appear in the first degree; thereafter, the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and declared a mistrial on the two remaining charges; subsequently, amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of unlawful transportation of cocaine and heroin with intent to sell by a person who is not drug dependent, unlawful transportation of cocaine and heroin with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a public housing project, and possession of cocaine, and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant  [***2] appealed; subsequently, the defendant filed an amended appeal.
State v. Hedge, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2380 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 22, 2007)



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) judgment convicting him of unlawfully transporting cocaine and heroin with intent to sell by a person not drug dependent, unlawfully transporting cocaine and heroin with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of a public housing project (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278a(b)), cocaine possession, and failure to appear in the first degree (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-172(a)(1)).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested while in possession of a vehicle that did not belong to him. He claimed that he did not know anything about drugs that were found secreted in the vehicle and proffered evidence that a convicted drug dealer, who previously had left drugs and money in the vehicle, had driven the vehicle shortly before him. The supreme court found that this evidence was highly relevant to defendant's theory of defense and that the trial court's exclusion of the third party culpability evidence violated defendant's Sixth Amendment right to present a defense with respect to the drug charges. The policies underlying Conn. Code Evid. R. 4-4(a) and 4-5(a) had extremely limited applicability when a defendant offered evidence of a character trait or other crimes, wrongs, or acts to prove that someone else committed the crime charged. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of failure to appear in the first degree, as the jury reasonably could have inferred that his appearance in court on January 6, 2003, was a term or condition of his bond in view of the fact that his bond was forfeited and that he was ordered rearrested after his failure to appear on that day.


OUTCOME: The convictions on the drug charges were reversed and defendant was entitled to a judgment of acquittal on the charge of unlawfully transporting cocaine and heroin with intent to sell within 1,500 feet of a public housing project and a new trial on the remaining drug charges. The trial court's judgment with respect to defendant's conviction of failure to appear in the first degree was affirmed.

Voris v. Middlesex Mut. Assur. Co.


SC 18281


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 589; 999 A.2d 741; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 269


February 23, 2010, Argued 
July 27, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a judgment declaring, inter alia, that the defendants are obligated to provide underinsured motorist coverage to the plaintiffs under an insurance contract between the parties, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Sheedy, J., granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Voris v. Middlesex Mut. Assur. Co., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2048 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 7, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds filed suit seeking a judgment declaring that defendant insurers were obligated to provide them underinsured motorist (UIM) coverage. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) granted defendants' motion for summary judgment; plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The policy, consistent with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 38a-336(g)(1), permitted a claim for UIM benefits to be brought as long as written notice of intent to bring such a claim was filed within three years of the accident. Over three years after the accident, plaintiffs provided defendants written notice of their intent to seek UIM benefits; their claim was denied as untimely. They argued that their failure to meet the time limit had to be excused unless defendants showed they were prejudiced by the late notice. To the extent Hotkowski v. Aetna Life & Casualty Co., 617 A.2d 451 (1992), left open the question whether prejudice had to be considered in determining if an insured could be excused from complying with a time limit for bringing UIM claims, the high court rejected the proposition. An unambiguous contract provision limiting the time in which an insurance claim had to be filed was enforceable. As plaintiffs failed to present any evidence as to what defendants did to mislead them, no issue of fact precluded the trial court from granting summary judgment to defendants. Section 38a-336(g)(1) did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to private insurers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Foley v. State Elections Enforcement Comm'n


SC 18646


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 764; 2 A.3d 823; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 278


July 20, 2010, Argued 
July 20, 2010 *, Officially Released


* July 20, 2010, the date that this court issued the order affirming the denial of the temporary injunction, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for declaratory and injunctive relief enjoining the named defendant from, inter alia, granting approval to the defendant Fedele 2010 to participate in the Citizens' Election Program and disbursing any funds to the defendant Fedele 2010 Joint Gubernatorial Campaign Fund, and barring that joint campaign from expending any funds previously disbursed, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Aurigemma, J., granted the motion by R. Nelson "Oz" Griebel et al. to intervene as plaintiffs; thereafter, the court denied the ex parte application for a temporary injunction filed by the named plaintiff et al., and the plaintiffs and the intervening plaintiffs, upon certification by the Chief Justice pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a that a matter of substantial public interest is at issue, appealed to this court.
Foley v. State Elections Enforcement Comm'n, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1811 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 13, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Denial of temporary injunction affirmed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a candidate and his campaign, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which denied their request for a temporary injunction (TI) to prevent defendants, the State Elections Enforcement Commission (SEEC) and state officials, from taking certain actions as to defendants, a joint committee (JC) and other campaigns, under the Citizens' Election Program, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-700 et seq.

Stat. § 9-709, and to enjoin state officials from disbursing campaign funds to the JC and to other campaigns pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 9-705 and 9-713. The trial court denied their request for a TI, and they appealed pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-265a(a). The court found that § 9-709(a) was ambiguous, but it determined that the candidates in the JC, one endorsed and one not, were permissible thereunder based on statutory construction. It also agreed with the trial court's interpretation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-704 with respect to campaign contributions. Further, the SEEC could consider contributions received or expenditures made by an opposing nonparticipating candidate before the start of the primary campaign period under § 9-713(a) through (d).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and it remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to render judgment for defendants.

State v. Wade


SC 18510


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 262; 998 A.2d 1114; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 231


March 22, 2010, Argued 
July 6, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, and with the crimes of manslaughter in the first degree and manslaughter in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; verdict of guilty of two counts each of the crimes of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, and manslaughter in the first degree; subsequently, the state entered a nolle prosequi as to the charge of manslaughter in the second degree; judgment in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Gruendel and Lavine, Js., which reversed the conviction as to manslaughter in the first degree and remanded the case with direction to modify the judgment to reflect a conviction of manslaughter in the second degree and for resentencing in accordance with that conviction; subsequently, after a hearing, the court,  [***2] D'Addabbo, J., vacated the sentences and resentenced the defendant as to all counts, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Wade, 106 Conn. App. 467, 942 A.2d 1085, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 117 (2008)



DISPOSITION:  


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of first degree manslaughter and two counts each of sale and possession of narcotics. The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed his conviction of first degree manslaughter and remanded the case to the trial court, which modified the conviction to second degree manslaughter and resentenced defendant on all counts, increasing the prison terms it had previously imposed on the drug counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim died from an overdose of drugs supplied by defendant. The intermediate appellate court held there was insufficient evidence to convict him of first degree manslaughter, but sufficient evidence to convict him of second degree manslaughter. Defendant's new aggregate sentence was two years shorter than the original one. Under the aggregate package theory, after one or more convictions were vacated, a trial court could increase sentences on the surviving counts if the total sentence was not exceeded. The high court held that as this theory applied regardless of the basis for remand, that the conviction was vacated due to insufficient evidence was immaterial. Nothing in the remand order implied the trial court was limited to reimposing a sentence only on the second degree manslaughter count. As the second sentence was less severe than the first, judicial vindictiveness was not presumed under North Carolina v. Pearce. And as defendant failed to establish the trial court acted with actual vindictiveness, his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV were not violated. Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 did not provide greater protection than the U.S. Constitution in this regard.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Stash v. Comm'r of Motor Vehicles


SC 18534, SC 18535


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 204; 999 A.2d 696; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 221


April 27, 2010, Argued 
June 29, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeals, in two cases, from the decisions of the defendant suspending the plaintiffs' motor vehicle licenses following their arrests for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, and tried to the court, Hon. George Levine, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, remanded the first case to the defendant's hearing officer for additional evidence pertaining to the approved device for measuring blood alcohol level and subsequently dismissed the appeal; thereafter, in the second case, the court, Hon. George Levine, judge trial referee, granted the plaintiff's motion to join the first case and dismissed the appeal; judgments dismissing the appeals, from which the plaintiffs filed separate appeals, which were consolidated and transferred to this court.
Pcolka v. Comm'r of Motor Vehicles, 51 Conn. Supp. 452, 1 A.3d 275, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3237 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 23, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drivers appealed judgments by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain (Connecticut) that, inter alia, upheld decisions by defendant motor vehicle commissioner and dismissed their appeals of the suspension of their motor vehicle licenses; the drivers claimed that the commissioner failed to show that they had an elevated blood alcohol content as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227b(o).


OVERVIEW: After their arrests, the commissioner notified the drivers that their licenses would be suspended for 90 days because they had failed chemical alcohol tests. The drivers argued that the commissioner improperly used a weight of alcohol to volume of breath ratio to establish that they had an elevated blood alcohol content when § 14-227b(o) required proof of a weight of alcohol to weight of blood ratio. According to the drivers, there was no evidence of any mathematical calculation or other conversion to transform the weight to volume Intoxilyzer results in their cases into weight to weight ratios. The trial court disagreed that the measurement produced by an Intoxilyzer did not comport with the requirement of § 14-227b(o)(1). The state supreme court examined the record on appeal, and the briefs and arguments of the parties, and was persuaded that the judgments of the trial court upholding the commissioner's suspension of the drivers' licenses should be affirmed. Because the trial court's memorandum of decision fully addressed the arguments raised on appeal, the trial court's well reasoned decision was adopted as a statement of the facts and the applicable law on the issues.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.


 

133 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez-Roman


SC 18348


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 66; 3 A.3d 783; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 220


October 27, 2009, Argued 
June 22, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of corrupt organizations and racketeering activity, eight counts of bribery, seven counts of bribe receiving, seven counts of conspiracy to commit bribe receiving, seven counts of forgery in the second degree and seven counts of conspiracy to commit forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Hauser, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Fairfield (Connecticut) of violations of the Connecticut Corrupt Organizations and Racketeering Activity Act (CORA), Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-394(a)(9) and (10) and 53-395(b), bribery, bribe receiving, conspiracy to commit bribe receiving, conspiracy to commit forgery, and forgery. The case was transferred to the state's highest court.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that defendant was charged with violating § 53-395(b), which made no reference to an enterprise. Section 53-395(b), as further defined in § 53-394(e), required proof of an enterprise. A partnership qualified as an enterprise under CORA. Defendant and her accomplice were not in a partnership, but were in an unchartered entity. An unchartered association in fact enterprise did not require proof of an ascertainable structure separate from that inherent in the pattern of racketeering activity with which defendant was charged. The racketeering convictions were supported. Defendant repeatedly conceded that she was involved in a criminal conspiracy with her accomplice to issue fraudulent licenses. The omission of an instruction on an enterprise was harmless error. CORA did not require proof that the enterprise existed beyond that inherent in the commission of the underlying crimes. Defendant's bribery challenge was not reviewed under Golding as defendant was not raising a constitutional claim, but was arguing that a person could not be charged with, and convicted of, both bribery and bribe receiving as part of a single conspiracy under Pinkerton.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

134 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


SC 18186


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


297 Conn. 1; 997 A.2d 461; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 226


February 22, 2010, Argued 
June 15, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, sale of a controlled substance, illegal manufacture, distribution, sale, prescription or administration of a controlled substance within 1500 feet of a school, and operation of a drug factory, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, Scarpelino, J., granted the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence and the state's motion to dismiss the charges, and rendered judgment dismissing the information, from which the state, on the granting of permission, appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop and Gruendel, Js., with Beach, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Clark, 107 Conn. App. 819, 947 A.2d 351, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 239 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9, an information charging defendant with various drug offenses was dismissed. The Connecticut Appellate Court affirmed. The State appealed, with certification.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that assuming a seizure occurred, the officers had a reasonable and articulable suspicion that defendant was involved in criminal activity based on a tip from a known confidential informant. The informant was reliable and his veracity had been demonstrated through previous contacts with the police, including one of the officers. The tip carried a greater indicia of reliability than one from an anonymous informant and required less verification. The police officers corroborated that defendant was driving a particular make and color of a car with Pennsylvania license plates in a certain area of town. It was reasonable for the officers to infer that the confidential informant's tip was reliable and that such a tip provided them with a reasonable and articulable suspicion to stop defendant's vehicle. When the police were familiar with the informant and his credibility has been established, and the police were able to corroborate several aspects of the tip by personal observation, the fact that the tip did not state the informant's basis of knowledge did not preclude the officers from having a reasonable and articulable suspicion of criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to reverse the judgment of the trial court and to remand the case to the trial court with direction to deny defendant's motion to suppress and for further proceedings according to law.

State v. Courchesne


SC 17174


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 622; 998 A.2d 1; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 227


March 19, 2008, Argued 
June 15, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of murder and capital felony, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the Court, Damiani, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss certain counts and the court, O'Keefe, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the state filed notice of the aggravating factor that it intended to prove during the penalty phase; subsequently, the guilt phase was tried to a three judge panel, West, Cofield and D'Addabbo, Js., which found the defendant guilty on all counts; thereafter, the court, D'Addabbo, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the aggravating factor and to impose a life sentence and ruled that, in order to impose the death penalty, the state must prove that both murders were committed in an aggravated manner, and the state, upon certification by the Chief Justice that a matter of substantial public interest was involved, appealed to the court, which reversed the trial court's ruling requiring the state to prove that both murders were committed in an aggravated manner and remanded the case for further proceedings; on remand, the court, D'Addabbo, J., denied, inter alia, the defendant's motion to declare the death penalty unconstitutional and motion to preclude the death penalty as an available punishment for his conviction of capital felony; subsequently, the penalty phase was tried to the jury before D'Addabbo, J.; finding that the defendant had committed the crime of murder with respect to one of the victims in an especially heinous, cruel or depraved manner and that the aggravating factor outweighed any mitigating factor or factors; thereafter, the court, D'Addabbo, J., rendered judgment imposing the sentence of death with respect to one capital felony count and the sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of release with respect to the other capital felony count, and the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Courchesne, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2428 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 4, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of his motion to suppress, a three judge panel convicted defendant of two counts of murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a(a), and one count each of capital felony under Conn. Gen. stat. § 53a-54b(8) and (9). In accordance with the jury's findings during the penalty phase, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, because the seizure by police exceeded the bounds of a Terry stop and he did not voluntarily consent to go to the police department for questioning. The supreme court found no error, concluding that the blocking of defendant's vehicle was the most efficacious way to maintain the status quo and get defendant's attention. In addition, defendant was not handcuffed or told he was could not leave. The evidence further showed that defendant voluntarily went the police department after the officers merely asked defendant if he would be willing to go. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the counts related to the death of the infant, who was in utero at the time of the crime but was delivered by cesarean section and died 6 weeks later. While the supreme court agreed with the trial court that the infant who was born alive and later died was a "person" under Connecticut homicide statues, the supreme court also agreed with defendant's contention that the trial court failed to apply the Guess principles to determine whether or not the infant was born alive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed with respect to both counts of capital felony and the count of murder relating to the child, and the case was remanded for a new trial as to those counts. The judgment was affirmed with respect to defendant's conviction for the murder of the mother.

State v. Sunrise Herbal Remedies, Inc.


SC 18371


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 556; 2 A.3d 843; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 196


March 18, 2010, Argued 
June 8, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action, in the first case, to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendants' alleged violations of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, and for other relief, and action, in the second case, for, inter alia, a judgment declaring null and void the allegedly fraudulent conveyance of certain real property from the defendant Valerie Hawk-Hoffman to the named defendant, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where, in the first case, the court, Miller, J., granted the state's ex parte application for a prejudgment attachment of certain real property owned by the defendant Valerie Hawk-Hoffman; thereafter, in the second case, the court, Wiese, J., granted the state's ex parte application for a prejudgment attachment of certain real property owned by the named defendant; subsequently, Wachovia Bank, N.A., intervened as a defendant and the court, Bentivegna, J., granted the defendants' motions to dissolve the prejudgment attachments, and the state appealed.
State v. Sunrise Herbal Remedies, Inc., 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 704 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 13, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State appealed a decision by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) that dissolved prejudgment attachments in the State's favor that had been filed against defendant owners' property; the State claimed that the trial court improperly concluded that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the applications for the attachments because they did not comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278e(a).


OVERVIEW: After the State filed an action against the owners for violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b(a) in connection with the sale of herbal products, the trial court granted its ex parte application for a prejudgment remedy pursuant to § 52-278e(a). Thereafter, the trial court concluded that the State's affidavits in support of the application were invalid because the affiant was not a competent affiant. The appellate court found, inter alia, that the trial court's conclusion was premised on an incorrect interpretation of the term "competent affiant." Although the affiant lacked personal knowledge to aver to the truth of the allegations underlying the complaints, he nonetheless was competent to represent the nature and extent of those complaints. The affiant derived personal knowledge of the existence, nature, and content of the State's prejudgment application by personally reviewing the complaints and the State's investigative file. Therefore, because he was a competent affiant, the trial court erred in finding that it lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.
