State v. Tomas D.


SC 18415


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 476; 995 A.2d 583; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 183


January 12, 2010, Argued 
June 1, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Levin, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree, and risk of injury to a child. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Waterbury, Connecticut, denied his motions for judgment of acquittal and a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Instead of taking her to school, defendant drove his 12-year-old niece to his home and raped her. He argued that as attendance records showed she was in school at the time of the crimes, and her testimony was inconsistent, the evidence was insufficient. The high court disagreed; the jury reasonably could have found that those records were the product of a data entry error and that the victim's testimony was credible. Thus, the new trial motion was properly denied. His right to compulsory process under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 was not violated when the State failed to notify him that it had released from subpoena the lead investigator, who then became temporarily unavailable to testify, as 1) there was no evidence the State did so in bad faith or with knowledge that he would then be unable to testify, 2) his testimony would have been cumulative, and 3) defendant neither issued his own subpoenas nor sought a continuance. The prosecutor did not state her personal belief about the victim's veracity, and her two improper comments about the victim's courage did not deprive defendant of a fair trial, as the verdict would not have differed absent the impropriety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

138 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bysiewicz v. Dinardo


SC 18612


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


298 Conn. 748; 6 A.3d 726; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 394


May 18, 2010, Argued 
May 18, 2010 **, Officially Released


** May 18, 2010, the date that the order reversing the judgment of the trial court was released, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a declaratory judgment to determine, inter alia, the constitutionality of the statutory requirement that an attorney possess at least ten years active practice at the bar of this state to be qualified as a candidate for the position of attorney general and to determine whether the plaintiff's fulfillment of her responsibilities as the secretary of the state constituted the active practice of law, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Sheldon, J., granted the motion to intervene as a party defendant filed by the Connecticut Republican Party; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Sheldon, J.; judgment declaring that the plaintiff satisfied the statutory requirement, from which the intervening defendant appealed.
Bysiewicz v. DiNardo, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1149 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 5, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff secretary of state sued defendants, a political party, its chair, and the office of secretary of state, seeking a declaratory judgment that she had practiced law in Connecticut for 10 years within the meaning of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3-124. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), allowed intervening defendant, another political party, to intervene, and entered judgment for plaintiff. Intervening defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, an attorney, was a candidate for attorney general. She sought a judgment declaring that in carrying out the responsibilities of her office, she had practiced law within the meaning of § 3-124. In the alternative, she sought a judgment declaring that § 3-124, which required the attorney general to have least 10 years' active practice at the Connecticut bar, was unconstitutional. The trial court held that her performance of some of her duties of her office constituted the active practice of law under § 3-124. The high court held she had standing and her claims were ripe. The phrase "attorney at law of at least 10 years' active practice" meant an attorney with at least some experience litigating cases in court. As she had no experience representing persons in court, she was not eligible to hold the office of attorney general. Performance of her official duties did not constitute the active practice of law under § 3-124. As the office of attorney general impliedly was exempt from Conn. Const. art. VI, § 10's general qualification requirements for state constitutional officers, § 3-124, although setting stricter qualifications than art. VI, § 10, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded to that court with direction to render a declaratory judgment that plaintiff failed to satisfy the requirements of § 3-124.

Gold v. Rowland


SC 17854


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 186; 994 A.2d 106; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 164


November 20, 2008, Argued 
May 11, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Class certification granted by Gold v. Rowland, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3130 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 13, 2011)
Summary judgment denied by Gold v. Rowland, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1886 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 19, 2013)
Summary judgment denied by Gold v. Rowland, 2014 Conn. Super. LEXIS 544 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 6, 2014)
Judgment entered by Gold v. Rowland, 2015 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1573 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 12, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for interpleader to determine the parties' rights to certain stock following the conversion of the defendant Anthem Insurance Companies, Inc., from a mutual insurance company to a stock insurance company, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Sheldon, J., granted in part and denied in part the motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction filed by the named defendant and the defendant state of Connecticut; thereafter, the named defendant and the defendant state of Connecticut appealed and the plaintiff and the defendants Anthem, Inc., et al., filed separate cross appeals.
Gold v. Rowland, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2837 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 26, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part; further proceedings; cross appeal of defendant insurers dismissed; cross appeal of plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed and plaintiff employee and defendant insurers cross-appealed a judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) that, inter alia, partially dismissed the employee's action to determine the parties' rights to certain stock and denied the State's motion to dismiss the employee's claim of an unconstitutional taking.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged that the State had received approximately 1.6 million shares of stock that should have been distributed to state employees pursuant to the insurers' plan of conversion. Because it concluded that the employee could prevail on his claim of an unconstitutional taking if he could establish at trial that the State had acted as his agent when it received the stock, the trial court denied the State's motion to dismiss the employee's taking claim. The state supreme court found, inter alia, that because the employee only alleged that the stock was not delivered to the State as the employees' agent in accordance with the plan of conversion, he failed to show that the State acted in excess of its statutory authority when it accepted the stock. The insurers lacked standing to bring their cross-appeal. Because nothing in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-259 set forth the manner in which the demutualization proceeds were to be distributed, the State was implicitly authorized to receive the benefits therefrom. Accordingly, the employee's claim of an unconstitutional taking and interpleader action should have been dismissed along with his constructive and resulting trust claims.


OUTCOME: The denial of the State's motion to dismiss the employee's constitutional claims and interpleader action was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings on the employee's claims against the insurers; the judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Rodriguez v. Testa


SC 18389


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 1; 993 A.2d 955; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 142


December 10, 2009, Argued 
May 4, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, personal injuries sustained as a result of the named defendant's alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, where the named defendant was defaulted for failure to appear and where the defendant Daimler Chrysler Financial Service America Trust filed a cross complaint; thereafter, the court, Brunetti, J., granted the motion of the defendant Daimler Chrysler Financial Service America Trust for permission to file a motion for summary judgment; subsequently, the court granted the motion for summary judgment filed by the defendant Daimler Chrysler Financial Service America Trust and rendered partial judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Rodriguez v. Testa, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3207 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 11, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged injured person appealed the grant of summary judgment by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) in favor of defendant car leasing company based on the Graves Amendment, 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106 preempting Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a. The injured person also claimed the Amendment was an unconstitutional under the commerce clause of the United States constitution, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8, cl. 3.


OVERVIEW: The injured person's car was struck by defendant driver, whose company had leased the car. The car was not insured by the leasing company at the time of the accident. The injured person alleged, in part, that the leasing company, as owner and lessor of the car, was liable for the driver's negligent operation of the car under the theory of vicarious liability set forth in § 14-154a. The appellate court held the savings provision of 49 U.S.C.S. § 30106(b)(1) excluded from preemption state laws that might require insurance or its equivalent as a condition of licensing or registration, or might impose such a requirement after an accident or unpaid judgment. Whereas the savings provision of § 30106(b)(2) preserved state laws that suspended the license and registration of, or otherwise penalize, a car owner who fails to meet the requirement, or who failed to pay a judgment resulting from a collision. Because § 14-154a(b)(1) did none of those things, it could not be deemed to be preserved. As the Graves Amendment preempted state law and was a valid exercise of Congressional authority under the commerce clause, the trial court properly granted the leasing company's summary judgment motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Butler


SC 18466


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 62; 993 A.2d 970; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 141


February 9, 2010, Argued 
May 4, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice Butler v. Alves, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 141799 (D. Conn., Dec. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public school, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, geographical area number twenty-three, where the court, Damiani, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Vitale, J.; after the court granted the defendant's oral motion for acquittal as to the charge of possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public school, verdict and judgment of guilty of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the trial court's judgment of conviction, following a jury trial, of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress narcotics seized from the automobile he was driving incident to a routine traffic stop because the seizure of the narcotics violated his Fourth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's car was stopped in a neighborhood known for frequent drug trafficking activity after officers saw defendant, who was driving, was not wearing a seat belt. Two officers observed defendant make a movement toward his right side, which led them to believe that he might be concealing a weapon. An officer observed defendant close the center console in the front seat. While being frisked for weapons, $ 1369 in cash and several cell phones were discovered on his person. An officer observed some plastic protruding from the center console which was removed and determined to be cocaine. Under the collective knowledge doctrine, the appellate court held it could consider the knowledge of both officers in determining whether there was reasonable suspicion sufficient to justify the protective search. The collective knowledge of the officers amply supported an inference that defendant was involved in narcotics trafficking, and, accordingly, that he was potentially armed and dangerous. Thus, there was a proper basis for effectuating the protective search of the console. The jury reasonably could have concluded he had possession of the narcotics sufficient to support the guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Boyd


SC 17719


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


295 Conn. 707; 992 A.2d 1071; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 114; 50 Comm. Reg. (P & F) 495


October 21, 2009, Argued 
April 27, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Boyd v. Connecticut, 131 S. Ct. 1474, 179 L. Ed. 2d 314, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1319 (U.S., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Boyd v. Warden, 2013 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1175 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 16, 2013)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Boyd v. Comm'r of Corr., 2015 Conn. App. LEXIS 164 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 1, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, where the court, Kavanewsky, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain evidence and to dismiss; thereafter, the court granted the state's motion in limine to admit certain prior misconduct evidence; subsequently, the matter was tried to the jury before Kavanewsky, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied. The State's motion in limine to admit certain prior misconduct evidence was granted. A jury trial in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) convicted defendant of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court concluded, inter alia, that although defendant had a legitimate expectation of privacy in his cell phone, the automobile exception applied under New York law. Because the police had probable cause to believe that defendant was selling drugs, because defendant's cell phone was visible in his car when police arrested him, and because the police had probable cause to believe that the cell phone contained evidence of drug activity, the police had probable cause to seize and search the contents of the phone under New York law, which applied to the search conducted in New York. While such a search would have been improper in Connecticut, there was no evidence Connecticut police were implicated in the seizure or the search of the phone. The supreme court next concluded the any error in the admission of testimony from defendant's girlfriend about his misconduct toward her was harmless, as the jury had before it other strong evidence of defendant's guilt. In addition, because defendant had not invoked his right to remain silent by stating he was not ready to discuss everything he knew about the murder, an officer's testimony about those statements did not violate Doyle.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

143 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conn. Coalition for Justice in Educ. Funding, Inc. v. Rell


SC 18032


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


295 Conn. 240; 990 A.2d 206; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 92


April 22, 2008, Argued 
March 30, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a judgment declaring that the plaintiff public schoolchildren have a state constitutional right to receive suitable and substantially equal educational opportunities, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Shortall, J., granted the defendants' motion to strike certain counts of the complaint from which the plaintiffs, upon certification by the Chief Justice pursuant to General Statutes § 52-265a that a matter of substantial public interest was at issue, appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Seeking, inter alia, a declaration that public school students had a right to suitable educational opportunities under Conn. Const. art. VIII, § 1, plaintiffs--students, their parents, and a citizens group--sued defendants, state officials and members of the state board of education. The Superior Court, Judicial District of Hartford, Connecticut, granted defendants' motion to strike counts one, two, and four of the complaint. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that due to the State's arbitrary and inadequate funding system and inadequate and unequal inputs, it failed to provide students suitable and substantially equal educational opportunities, including appropriate class sizes; highly qualified teachers; modern technology, libraries, and textbooks; and a rigorous curriculum. Finding no constitutional right to "suitable" educational opportunities, the trial court struck three counts of the complaint. The high court agreed with the trial court that the case was justiciable and did not present a political question, as the judicial role was limited to deciding whether existing public educational systems satisfied an articulated constitutional standard. Conn. Const. art. VIII, § 1, entitled students to an education suitable to give them the opportunity to be responsible citizens. To satisfy this standard, the State, through the local school districts, had to provide students an objectively meaningful opportunity to receive the benefits of this constitutional right. Further proceedings were required to determine whether the State in fact provided plaintiff students with constitutionally suitable educational opportunities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings according to law.

State v. Chambers


SC 18490


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


296 Conn. 397; 994 A.2d 1248; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 177


March 23, 2010, Argued 
March 23, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and tried to the jury before Hadden, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defense counsel's motion to withdraw was denied, a jury found defendant guilty of assault in the first degree, robbery in the first degree, and conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) imposed a total effective sentence of 45 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court deprived him of his rights to due process and a fair trial after trial counsel invoked Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 3.3(a), on the basis of counsel's conclusion that defendant intended to offer false testimony. Among other things, defendant argued he was improperly excluded from an in-chambers meeting that preceded the hearing at which the judge ruled on the ethical dilemma raised by defense counsel. The supreme court agreed with the State that the record was inadequate to review that claim, as the only evidence in the record consisted of two passing references by the judge that there had been such a meeting. Defendant also argued that prior accepting counsel's invocation of Rule 3.3(a)(3), the judge improperly failed to conduct an inquiry on the record to determine whether counsel's "knowledge" met the requirements of the rule. The supreme court agreed with the State that the rules require "actual knowledge" and not a "reasonable belief" by counsel that his client intended to commit perjury, and further noted that defendant's failure to contest the factual representation giving rise to the dilemma demonstrated his acquiescence to counsel's statement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

145 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winot


SC 17696


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 753; 988 A.2d 188; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 45


January 11, 2008, Argued 
February 16, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to commit kidnapping in the second degree, kidnapping in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Mullarkey, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty; thereafter, the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Schaller, Gruendel and Peters, Js., which reversed the judgment with respect to the defendant's conviction of kidnapping in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Winot, 95 Conn. App. 332, 897 A.2d 115, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 214 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second degree attempt to commit kidnapping, second degree kidnapping (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94(a)), and risk of injury to a child. He appealed. The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed in part, finding that § 53a-94(a) was unconstitutional as applied to the facts and that the evidence was insufficient to support the risk of injury conviction. The State appealed the reversal of defendant's kidnapping conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stopped his car and ordered a 12-year-old girl to get inside. He exited his car and approached her; she ran away. Four days later, this scenario was repeated; this time, he grabbed her by the arm and tried to pull her toward his car. She bit him, he released her, and she ran away again. Police found a rope noose and duct tape in the trunk of defendant's car. The high court held that § 53a-94(a), which proscribed second degree kidnapping, was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's conduct. Although his restraint of the victim was brief, when it was viewed along with the strong evidence of his specific intent to prevent her liberation, his claim that he was unaware of the criminality of his behavior, or that he was a victim of arbitrary enforcement, failed. The exclusion of the sworn statement of the victim's mother as substantive evidence under State v. Whelan did not deny defendant his right to present a defense under U.S. Const. amend. VI. Although the mother's prior inconsistent statement met the criteria of Whelan and was not itself hearsay, it nevertheless contained within it another level of hearsay for which no hearsay exception applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was reversed in part and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgment of conviction of kidnapping in the second degree. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

New Eng. Estates, LLC v. Town of Branford


SC 18132


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 817; 988 A.2d 229; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 42


May 26, 2009, Argued 
February 16, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Town of Branford v. Santa Barbara, 294 Conn. 803, 988 A.2d 221, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 43 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 1983 to recover damages from the named defendant et al. for the unconstitutional taking by eminent domain of certain real property, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Cremins, J.; verdict and judgment for the plaintiff, New England Estates, LLC, and the cited in defendants, Thomas Santa Barbara, Jr., et al., from which the named defendant appealed; subsequently, the court, Cremins, J., issued a memorandum of decision awarding attorney's fees to New England Estates, LLC, and Thomas Santa Barbara, Jr., et al., and the named defendant amended its appeal and Thomas Santa Barbara, Jr., et al. filed a cross appeal.
New Eng. Estates, L.L.C. v. Town of Branford, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2353 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 9, 2008)
Town of Branford v. Santa Barbara, 294 Conn. 785, 988 A.2d 209, 2010 Conn. LEXIS 41 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed the judgment of the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket (Connecticut) in favor of cited defendant owners in plaintiff developer's action pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. In a cross-appeal, the owners claim that the trial court improperly denied them attorney's fees and costs in connection with the valuation appeal. The § 1983 action arose from the town's taking of certain real property.


OVERVIEW: The owners were the title holders of the property at the time of the taking, and the developer had entered into an option contract with the owners to purchase the property. The property had been used for over 10 years as a landfill, and the developer had sought to obtain approval for the residential development of the property. The taking of the property was a result of the developer's various unsuccessful attempts to obtain approval of its development plans. The court held that because the developer's unexercised option to purchase the land was not considered a property interest under Connecticut state law, the developer's contractual right was not a property right protected by the federal takings clause, U.S. Const. amend. V. Since the developer lacked a property interest protected under the takings clause, the court addressed on the claims on appeal with respect to the owners. The court held that the issues litigated in the § 1983 action were not identical to the issues decided in the valuation appeal and that the owners were not awarded double damages. The court held that the owners were not precluded from recovering money damages in the § 1983 suit and the valuation action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the owners and affirmed the award of attorney's fees to the owners for work performed in the discrimination action. The court reversed the denial of attorney's fees to the owners for work performed in connection with the valuation appeal, and remanded the matter to the trial court for a determination of reasonable attorney's fees in connection with that case.

Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison


SC 18083


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 651; 986 A.2d 278; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 20


October 23, 2009, Argued 
February 2, 2010, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by, Summary judgment denied by Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison, 2011 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3152 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a judgment declaring, inter alia, that the defendant's increase in building permit fees constituted an unconstitutional taking, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the case was transferred to the judicial district of Waterbury, Complex Litigation Docket; thereafter, the plaintiff Paul Coady Construction, LLC, withdrew from the action; subsequently, the court, Cremins, J., granted the motion for class certification filed by the named plaintiff et al., and the defendant appealed; thereafter, the trial court granted in part the defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint.
Neighborhood Builders, Inc. v. Town of Madison, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2711 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town appealed from the order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted plaintiff applicants' motion for class certification. Plaintiffs brought suit alleging violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-130i and 7-148, Conn. Const. art. 10, and the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq., arising from the town's collection of building permit fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs also initially asserted a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. Plaintiffs were all building companies who had applied for a building permit. Plaintiffs asserted that the revenues derived by the town from the payment of building permit fees were significantly in excess of the cost to the town of regulating building activity, and that the town unlawfully used the fees to fund other initiatives that bore no relationship to the regulation of building activity. The trial court had dismissed all of the non-CUTPA counts of the complaint. The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion to certify and certified a class consisting of entities that directly paid to the town the allegedly excessive building permit fees during a certain time period. The court held that neither party addressed whether a CUTPA claim may be brought against a municipality, and, as a result, the trial court did not rule on that issue when it certified the class. Accordingly, in the absence of any statutory or other authority to the contrary, the court lacked jurisdiction to consider that claim in the context of the town's interlocutory appeal. The court directed the town to file a motion to decertify the class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting class certification and concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting the motion for class certification of plaintiffs' CUTPA claim.

Fennelly v. Norton


SC 18338


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 484; 985 A.2d 1026; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 5


October 19, 2009, Argued 
January 19, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Motion by the defendant to recover attorney's fees incurred in defending an appeal by the paternal grandparents of the defendant's minor children from the dismissal of their application for visitation, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Alvord, J., appointed an attorney for the minor children; thereafter, the court issued an order directing the plaintiffs to pay an apportioned percentage of the attorney's fees incurred by the defendant as well as those of the attorney for the minor children; subsequently, the court issued a clarification of its decision awarding attorney's fees, and the plaintiffs appealed.
Fennelly v. Norton, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3212 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant paternal grandparents filed an application for visitation with their grandchildren pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. The Superior Court, Judicial District of New Haven, Connecticut, denied their application and, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-62, ordered them to pay 85 percent of appellee mother's counsel fees and 90 percent of the fees of the children's court-appointed attorney. The grandparents appealed the fee awards.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the grandparents' application on grounds they failed to prove that they had a relationship with the children similar to a parent-child relationship or that dismissal would cause the children significant harm. While the grandparents' ultimately unsuccessful appeal of this order was pending, the mother filed a motion for attorney's fees; the trial court sua sponte appointed counsel to represent the children regarding the fee issue. The trial court, after noting the parties' respective financial abilities, entered the fee awards at issue. The high court held that § 46b-62 did not authorize an award of attorney's fees against third parties petitioning for visitation under § 46b-59. As the fee award did not relate to the merits of the visitation petition, and as the pending appeal continued the trial court's jurisdiction over preliminary jurisdictional matters, the trial court retained jurisdiction to appoint an attorney for the children under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-54. However, it abused its discretion by appointing an attorney for the children for a proceeding intended solely to address attorney's fees, an issue in which they lacked a direct interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with direction to deny the mother's motion for attorney's fees, to vacate the sua sponte appointment of an attorney for the minor children, and for further proceedings in which it was to consider the propriety of a refund of appointed counsel's fees, or to entertain other sources from which counsel could be compensated.

Bd. of Selectmen v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


SC 18343


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 438; 984 A.2d 748; 2010 Conn. LEXIS 1


October 26, 2009, Argued 
January 5, 2010, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a decision by the named defendant declaring null and void the resignation of the defendant Anthony Gaeta, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and transferred to the judicial district of New Britain, and tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgment dismissing the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Bd. of Selectmen v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n, 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 10 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 8, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Connecticut Freedom of Information Commission found that appellant board of selectmen violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-225(d) of the Connecticut Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq., by holding a special meeting without giving 24 hours notice to the public. The board appealed; the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Britain dismissed the appeal. The board sought further review.


OVERVIEW: After a town employee threatened to kill a selectman, the board convened an "emergency" meeting without notifying the public. The employee met with the board and was told that if he did not resign, he would be placed on leave pending an investigation. He chose to retire instead; the board voted to accept his "resignation." He filed a complaint alleging the board violated § 1-225(d), which required it to give the public 24 hours notice before convening a special meeting. The Commission agreed and declared the resignation null and void. The high court held that, in view of evidence that the selectman did not perceive the employee's threat as real, the Commission properly found that there had been no emergency under § 1-225(d) to justify the lack of notice. Any error by the trial court in finding facts outside of the record was harmless, as it did not likely affect the result. That § 1-225(d) did not define "emergency" and that the Commission failed to adopt regulations defining that term did not render § 1-225(d) void for vagueness, as the dictionary definition provided clear notice that an emergency involved a serious, unexpected situation that required immediate attention.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nathan J.


SC 17903


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


294 Conn. 243; 982 A.2d 1067; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 497


September 11, 2009, Argued 
December 1, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of risk of injury to a child, assault in the third degree, and disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield and tried to the jury before Thim, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of risk of injury to a child, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, McLachlan, Lavine and West, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Nathan J., 99 Conn. App. 713, 915 A.2d 907, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 78 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction of risk of injury to a child (Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1)). The Connecticut Appellate Court reversed and remanded the matter for a new trial, ruling that defendant had been entitled to an instruction on the defense of parental justification provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-18(1). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Learning that his 11-year-old son had pushed a teacher at school, defendant demanded that he explain his actions. The son testified that after he did so, defendant grabbed him by his shirt, and that he ducked and scraped his face against defendant's ring, resulting in a facial bruise. The trial court instructed the jury on the parental justification defense as it applied to the disorderly conduct and assault charges, but instructed the jury that the defense did not apply to the risk of injury charge. Defendant was acquitted on the former charges, but convicted of risk of injury. The high court held that the parental justification defense could apply to a risk-of-injury charge. Defendant was entitled to an instruction on that defense because the State's witnesses, including the son, injected the issue of parental justification into the trial sufficiently to raise a reasonable doubt in the mind of the jury as to whether defendant's actions were justified as parental discipline. As the trial court instructed the jury that this defense did not apply, there was a reasonable possibility that the jury was misled in reaching its verdict; thus, defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed.

Crawford v. Comm'r of Corr.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland (Connecticut), the habeas court, which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner had been convicted of robbery.

Plaintiff asserted that having reached the age of 70, the justice was ineligible to continue to deliberate or to otherwise participate in the disposition of the appeal. The court disagreed with plaintiff's claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-198(c) was unconstitutional. The court held that the justice's continued participation in the underlying appeal after reaching retirement age properly was authorized by that statute and did not affect the court's subject matter jurisdiction.

State v. Rupar


SC 18269


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


293 Conn. 489; 978 A.2d 502; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 387


April 23, 2009, Argued 
September 22, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Writ of error from the decision of the sentence review division of the Superior Court, Miano, Espinosa and Iannotti, Js., upholding the prison sentence of the plaintiff in error, brought to this court, which transferred the writ of error to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the Appellate Court denied the motion of the defendant in error to dismiss the writ of error; subsequently, the writ of error was transferred to this court.
State v. Rupar, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3669 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 22, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Writ of error dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate was convicted of fourth degree sexual assault and risk of injury to a child, and was sentenced to an effective term of 11 years, execution suspended after seven years, and 20 years' probation with special conditions. He sought review of his sentence. The Connecticut superior court, review division, affirmed. The inmate filed a writ of error; defendant State sought dismissal of the writ.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he had a liberty interest under the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, in receiving a sentence that was proportional to the sentences of similarly situated offenders. The high court held that as the review division's decision to uphold the sentence was a final judgment not otherwise appealable pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-196(d), a writ of error was authorized by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 721(a)(4). And as the inmate was not challenging the result but the adequacy of the procedures the review division employed, the high court had jurisdiction to consider the merits of the writ of error. As defendants had no substantive right to a particular sentence within the range authorized by statute, there was no Fourteenth Amendment liberty interest in receiving a sentence within the authorized range that was "proportionate" to that of similarly situated offenders. Neither Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-91a(c) nor Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 43-28 required the trial court or the review division to consider sentences imposed on other offenders; therefore, § 43-28 did not create a liberty interest in a proportionate sentence.


OUTCOME: The writ of error was dismissed.

Columbia Air Servs. v. DOT


SC 18142


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


293 Conn. 342; 977 A.2d 636; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 359


January 6, 2009, Argued 
September 8, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the alleged breach of a lease agreement, and for declaratory and injunctive relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London and referred to D. Michael Hurley, judge trial referee, who granted the defendants' motion to dismiss and who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Columbia Air Servs. v. DOT, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3025 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 8, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed the judgment by the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New London (Connecticut) which granted defendant Department of Transportation's (DOT) motion to dismiss all counts of the complaint based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The company asserted that the trial court erred in granting the motion to dismiss based on the company's claims being barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The company requested the opportunity to lease and develop land immediately abutting its existing leasehold at the airport. The DOT commissioner issued a public invitation for proposals regarding the development of the parcel. The DOT and the company engaged in negotiations. The DOT subsequently notified the company that it was terminating the proposal process. Thereafter, the company sought damages and declaratory relief. The company failed to present its claims to the claims commissioner prior to filing the action. Because exhaustion of this alternative means of relief was a prerequisite to the trial court's jurisdiction, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider any of the company's claims. Thus, the appellate court held the trial court properly granted the motion to dismiss as the breach of contract, fraud, and other claims were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The company's limited property interest in a contract with the DOT was not an entitlement to which due process protections apply. Although the company alleged that the DOT treated the competitor differently, it did not allege that the differential treatment was based on any impermissible consideration.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Bruno


SC 18251, SC 18252


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


293 Conn. 127; 975 A.2d 1253; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 279


February 19, 2009, Argued 
August 18, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part amended information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, sale of a narcotic substance by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of a narcotic substance with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, and conspiracy to violate the state dependency-producing drug laws, and, in the second part, of being a persistent drug offender, brought to the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Rodriguez, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the first part of the information was tried to the jury; verdict of guilty; subsequently, the court dismissed the second part of the information and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the jury verdict, from which the defendant appealed; thereafter, the state, on the granting of permission, filed a separate appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted by a jury of violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b), 21a-278a(b), and 53a-48, he was tried by the trial court in the Judicial District of Fairfield, Connecticut, on charges of being a persistent drug offender. The trial court found defendant not guilty of that charge. Defendant and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, in response to requests to buy heroin, used a key to open a car trunk and handled drugs in the trunk. The high court held that this evidence was sufficient to prove he had control over the drugs and knew their character. Evidence of his delivery of the heroin to a companion who, at his request, tried to learn if a buyer was a police officer was sufficient to prove defendant and his companion conspired to sell drugs. The trial court ruled that the State had improperly charged defendant with being a persistent felony offender under § 53a-40 rather than charging him with being a subsequent drug offender under § 21a-278(b). As this ruling was based on purely legal grounds, not on a finding that the State had failed to prove its case, retrial of defendant on persistent drug offender charges was not barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. As the information referred to § 21a-278(b), and as defendant understood he was charged as a subsequent offender under § 21a-278(b), not as a persistent felony offender under § 53a-40, the State was entitled to proceed to trial under § 21a-278(b) despite the information's use of "persistent" instead of "subsequent."


OUTCOME: The judgment with respect to the persistent drug offender charge was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial. The convictions on the other charges were affirmed.

State v. Connor


SC 18099, SC 18101


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


292 Conn. 483; 973 A.2d 627; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 207


April 21, 2008, Argued 
July 14, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Motion for new trial denied by State v. Connor, 2012 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1475 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 6, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut trial court entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, robbery involving an occupied motor vehicle, and larceny in the third degree. The trial court, following a hearing, found he violated the conditions of probation imposed in regard to a prior, unrelated conviction. It then sentenced him. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: As a result of an incident in which defendant abducted his former wife in her vehicle, he was charged with multiple offenses. Following a jury trial at which he was permitted to represent himself and during which there were questions about his competency, he was found guilty of kidnapping in the first degree, robbery in the third degree, robbery involving an occupied motor vehicle, and larceny in the third degree. Defendant then represented himself at a probation violation hearing, and the trial court found that he had violated conditions of probation previously imposed on him. The state supreme court found that he was entitled to a new probation violation hearing because the trial court failed to ensure that he had waived his right to counsel knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily. Regarding the criminal case, it found that the trial court did not violate his constitutional right to represent himself at trial, but that the case had to be remanded for the trial court to determine whether, even if he was competent to stand trial, he was separately competent pursuant to the Sixth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VI, and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8 to represent himself at trial.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the judgment in the probation violation case and remanded that case to the trial court for a new probation violation hearing. It remanded the criminal case to the trial court to decide whether it would have denied defendant's request to represent himself at trial, due to his mental illness or mental incapacity, even though he had been deemed to have been competent to stand trial and to waive the right to counsel.

State v. Tabone


SC 18119


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


292 Conn. 417; 973 A.2d 74; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 201


October 21, 2008, Argued 
July 7, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Tabone v. Warden, 2010 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3441 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 20, 2010)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Tabone, 301 Conn. 708, 23 A.3d 689, 2011 Conn. LEXIS 278 (2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Tabone, 279 Conn. 527, 902 A.2d 1058, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 299 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut trial court entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of sexual assault in the second degree, sexual assault in the first degree, and risk of injury to a child. It then sentenced him to a total effective sentence of 20 years incarceration, execution suspended after 10 years, followed by 10 years of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the second degree. He was originally sentenced to 10 years in prison followed by 10 years of special parole. However, his case was remanded for resentencing after the state supreme court found the sentence was illegal. The trial court then sentenced him to 20 years in prison, with execution suspended after 10 years followed by 10 years of probation. Defendant appealed that sentence. He claimed that the substitution of the probation term for the special parole term originally imposed unconstitutionally enlarged the sentence. The state supreme court found that the substitution violated his Fifth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 9 due process rights because the calculation for a probation violation as opposed to a special parole violation impermissibly enlarged the confines of his original sentence, thus requiring he be resentenced. It further found defendant's double jeopardy rights under the Fifth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 9 were not violated even though defendant's sentence was illegal, as his resentencing on two related offenses was permissible so long as the entire sentence imposed upon him had not been fully served.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

Perricone v. Perricone


SC 17683


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


292 Conn. 187; 972 A.2d 666; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 152


January 15, 2009, Argued 
June 23, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Perricone v. Perricone, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 785 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 9, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut trial court in a postdissolution proceeding to enforce a confidentiality agreement between defendant former wife and plaintiff former husband entered a judgment to enforce the agreement. Its judgment also restrained the former wife from disseminating any information pertaining to her divorce from the former husband or any derogatory or defamatory information about the parties. The former wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former husband had substantial business interests and, thus, the parties while divorcing executed a confidentiality agreement barring her from disseminating information about the divorce or from making any related disparaging remarks. Thereafter, he sought a restraining order after allegedly learning that she was going to appear on a nationally broadcast television program to discuss their divorce. The trial court following a hearing found that the confidentiality agreement was enforceable. The former wife primarily asserted on appeal that the agreement violated her federal and state constitutional rights. The state supreme court found that (1) the parties' separation agreement did not supersede and nullify the confidentiality agreement because the two agreements covered different matters; (2) the confidentiality agreement did not violate the former wife's free speech rights under U.S. Const. amend. I or Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4 and 5, as a trial court could enforce a waiver of constitutional rights, and the former wife intelligently and voluntarily waived those rights, and (3) the confidentiality agreement neither violated public policy nor was too indefinite to enforce.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Town of New Hartford v. Conn. Res. Recovery Auth.


SC 17879


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


291 Conn. 489; 970 A.2d 570; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 124


October 16, 2008, Argued 
May 19, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract and unjust enrichment, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury and transferred to the Complex Litigation Docket, where the court, Eveleigh, J., granted the named plaintiff's motion for certification of a class action; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiffs' motion for contempt, from which the named defendant appealed.
Town of New Hartford v. Conn. Res. Recovery Auth., 2008 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1383 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 30, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town brought an action to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract and unjust enrichment. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury (Connecticut) granted the town's motion for certification of a class action. Thereafter, the trial court granted the towns' motion for contempt, from which defendant state agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the course of the litigation, the towns filed a motion for relief for improper communications, alleging that the agency had misleading information suggesting that the towns had the power to bring the suit to a halt. The trial court ordered that agency desist from any further communications with the towns regarding the lawsuit except upon prior approval of the court. A court trial was held. Prior to the court rendering judgment, the agency posted statements on its website. The motion for contempt alleged that the website posting was an improper attempt to contact the towns. The agency claimed that it was denied due process of law as it was not afforded adequate notice of the motion and a meaningful opportunity to prepare a defense. The appellate court held that as the agency was given less than one day to consider a motion for contempt, which consisted of four pages of allegations, exhibits totaling in excess of a dozen pages and a request for sanctions, there was a denial of due process. While it was unclear whether a different result would have been reached had the agency been given more time, a denial of due process of law could not be justified by that uncertainty.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding the agency in contempt was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to vacate the contempt finding.

State v. Sanseverino


SC 17786, SC 17787


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


291 Conn. 574; 969 A.2d 710; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 145


October 16, 2007, Argued 
May 19, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Espinosa, J., denied the defendant's motion to sever the offenses and for separate trials; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Gruendel and Berdon, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for new separate trials, and the state and the defendant, on the granting of certification, filed separate appeals to this court; thereafter, this court reversed the judgment of the Appellate Court and remanded the case to that court with direction to reverse in part the trial court's judgment and to remand the case to the trial court to render judgment of not guilty on the charge of kidnapping in the first degree; subsequently, this court granted the state's motion for reconsideration en banc.
State v. Sanseverino, 287 Conn. 608, 949 A.2d 1156, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 250 (2008)
State v. Sanseverino, 98 Conn. App. 198, 907 A.2d 1248, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 445 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed in  [***2] part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Appellate Court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction entered after a jury found defendant guilty of, inter alia, first-degree kidnapping. After the state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and found defendant was entitled to reversal of that conviction in light of a recent state supreme court decision in another case, the state supreme court granted the State's motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: As a result of two separate alleged sexual assaults of female employees, defendant, the owner of a bakery where they worked, was charged with, inter alia, one count of first-degree kidnapping. After a jury trial, he was convicted of first-degree kidnapping in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A). While his case was on appeal, the state supreme court found in another case that a defendant could not be convicted of first-degree kidnapping unless a jury found beyond a reasonable doubt that the restraint involved in committing that crime was not merely incidental to and necessary to commit another crime against the victim. The state supreme court then found that defendant consequently was entitled to reversal of his first-degree kidnapping conviction. The state supreme court then granted the State's motion for reconsideration. It agreed with the State upon reconsideration that the State should be allowed at its election to retry defendant on that charge or, alternatively, should be allowed to obtain a judgment of conviction against defendant on the lesser included offense of unlawful restraint in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-96.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and remanded the case to it to reverse the trial court's judgment on defendant's conviction of kidnapping in the first degree, to otherwise affirm the judgment, and to remand the case to the trial court with direction either to order a new trial on the kidnapping charge or to render a judgment of conviction of unlawful restraint in the second degree, at the State's option.

Lyon v. Jones


SC 18096


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


291 Conn. 384; 968 A.2d 416; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 105; 106 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 142


November 21, 2008, Argued 
May 5, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Lyon v. Jones, 104 Conn. App. 547, 935 A.2d 201, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 433 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the Appellate Court (Connecticut)'s affirmance of a trial court's judgment of dismissal, claiming error in interpreting Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-60 and 46a-70 to bar her employment discrimination case under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. Appellees, the employer and its employees, agreed that § 46a-60 was misconstrued, claimed that § 46a-70 was properly construed, and that collateral estoppel barred the claims.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the claims under § 46a-70 were erroneously reviewed because the appellate court lacked jurisdiction; the claims had not been appealed and were moot. The § 46a-60 claim was not moot because it was raised on appeal. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100 expressly waived sovereign immunity and created a cause of action in the superior court for claims alleging a violation of § 46a-60 over which the claims commission had released jurisdiction. Although the § 46a-60 claim was not procedurally barred, the substantive claim was collaterally estopped. With respect to claims previously brought in the district court under 42 U.S.C.S. § 12111 et seq.; 29 U.S.C.S. § 621 et seq.; 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 2000e-2; § 46a-58(a); § 46a-60(a)(1) and § 46a-70(a), there was no material fact issue that the challenged acts were motivated by discriminatory intent. The employee had a full and fair opportunity to litigate the elements underlying her § 46a-60 claim at the district court and failed to make a prima facie showing of discrimination. There was no reason to depart from the doctrine of collateral estoppel to allow relitigation in the superior court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the decision pertaining to § 46-70 and remanded the case to the appellate court with directions to dismiss that part of the appeal concerning those claims; the court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

State v. Ray


SC 17905


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 602; 966 A.2d 148; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 27


September 16, 2008, Argued 
March 17, 2009 *, Officially Released


* This case was originally decided on January 6, 2009, by the same five member panel of this court. See State v. Ray, 290 Conn. 24, 961 A.2d 947 (2009). On February 25, 2009, we granted the state's motion to correct the decision. Although we conclude that this case was correctly decided, we have made several substantive changes to the prior decision in this case. Accordingly, this opinion supersedes our prior decision in all respects.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Informations charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, six counts of the crime of possession of narcotics, two counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, three counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project and one count each of the crimes of possession of drug paraphernalia and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the court, Hon. William F. Hickey, Jr., judge trial referee; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the charge of interfering with an officer; verdict and judgments of guilty of five counts of the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, six counts of the crime of possession of narcotics, two counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, three counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project and one count of the crime of possession of drug paraphernalia, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Ray, 290 Conn. 24, 961 A.2d 947, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 5 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in  [***2] part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Stamford-Norwalk Superior Court (Connecticut) entered final judgments of conviction after it found defendant guilty of five counts of the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b), as well as 12 other drugs charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant arranged to make crack cocaine sales to an undercover police officer. Thereafter, he was charged with multiple offenses, including five counts of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). He elected to be tried by the trial court. At the close of the State's case, he filed a motion for judgment of acquittal. The State responded that the burden was on defendant to prove he was drug-dependent. During his case-in-chief, he presented evidence that he was drug-dependent. At the close of his case, he renewed his motion for acquittal, which the trial court denied. The trial court concluded he had not proven by a preponderance of the evidence that he was drug dependent. The trial court then found defendant guilty on all of the drug charges against him, including those under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). The state supreme court found that the trial court correctly ruled that defendant had to prove by a preponderance of evidence that he was drug dependent. However, it then found that the trial court erred in finding he had not made such a showing since overwhelming evidence was admitted that he was drug dependent.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed defendant's convictions on five counts of the sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent. It then ordered that the case be remanded to the trial court with directions to modify those convictions to reflect convictions of the lesser-included offense of the sale of narcotics. It also directed that he be resentenced. Otherwise, the state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgments of conviction.

Hogan v. Dep't of Children & Families


SC 18009


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 545; 964 A.2d 1213; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 29


November 17, 2008, Argued 
March 10, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative appeal from the decision of the defendant to place the name of the plaintiff, a former employee of the New Haven juvenile detention center, on the child abuse and neglect registry list for injuries sustained by a juvenile detainee while under the plaintiff's supervision, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain and tried to the court, Cohn, J.; judgment sustaining the appeal in part and remanding the matter to the defendant for further proceedings, from which the plaintiff appealed and the defendant cross appealed.
Hogan v. State Dep't of Children & Families, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2125 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 3, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a former detention facility employee, and defendant, the Department of Children and Families, cross-appealed from a decision of a Connecticut trial court, which remanded plaintiff's case to defendant for a determination of whether plaintiff's name should appear on the central child abuse and neglect registry, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101k. Plaintiff had filed an administrative appeal of defendant's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had determined that plaintiff was responsible for the abuse of a juvenile and that he posed a risk to the safety and well-being of children such that his name should be placed on defendant's registry. The trial court determined that one factor cited in defendant's decision was not supported by the record and ordered the case remanded. On appeal, plaintiff raised several issues, including constitutional challenges to the registry statute. The court held that the trial court improperly determined that one of the factors relied on by defendant, namely that the case of abuse was not an isolated incident, was not supported by the evidence as the record in fact supported the hearing officer's finding that the episode with the juvenile was not an isolated incident. The court found no merit to plaintiff's constitutional challenges to the registry statute, finding that the parameters of § 17a-101k were sufficiently clear to guide defendant in light of the aim of the legislation and did not constitute an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The court further found that the registry scheme did not violate due process nor did it constitute a bill of attainder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, in part, with respect to the trial court's order remanding the case to defendant. The court remanded the case to the trial court with direction for it to affirm defendant's decision.

State v. Myers


SC 17925


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 278; 963 A.2d 11; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 15


October 21, 2008, Argued 
February 3, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Two part substitute information charging the defendant, in the first part, with the crimes of possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school and possession of narcotics, and, in the second part, with previously having been convicted of the sale of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the first part of the information was tried to the jury before J. R. Downey, J.; verdict of guilty of possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school and possession of narcotics; thereafter, the second part of the information was tried to the court, and the court rendered judgment in accordance with the verdict and enhanced the defendant's sentence for previously having been convicted of the sale of narcotics; subsequently, the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop and DiPentima, Js., with Berdon, J., dissenting in part, which reversed in part the trial court's judgment, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed  [***2] to this court.
State v. Myers, 101 Conn. App. 167, 921 A.2d 640, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 198 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court sentenced defendant as a repeat offender under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-277(a) without first obtaining a plea from defendant or conducting a trial on the issue as Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 42-2 required. An appellate court (Connecticut) found that the trial court committed plain error and vacated the sentence. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State claimed that it was not plain error to forgo a part B (repeat offender) trial under the factual and procedural circumstances of the case. The court agreed. Although the trial court's failure to comply with the § 42-2 procedures was error, the appellate court abused its discretion in vacating the sentence; the error did not result in manifest injustice. Defendant did not contest the validity of his prior conviction. His brief was bereft of a single reason why the absence of a trial or plea canvass on part B of the information was an obvious error. To the extent that some appellate court cases suggested a per se rule that all violations of the rules of practice were plain error, those cases were mistaken. Regardless of § 42-2's dictates, due process did not require a separate trial or proceeding when the fact of a prior conviction was essentially uncontested. Defendant had no constitutional right to a trial on the issue of his prior conviction. A waiver of trial on that issue was not of constitutional dimension. The self-incrimination right was not implicated. Defendant had an opportunity to confront his accusers as to the alleged fact of his prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court as to the vacation of defendant's sentence and remanded the case to that court with direction to affirm the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Carrasquillo


SC 17568


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 209; 962 A.2d 772; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 8


March 13, 2008, Argued 
January 27, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crimes of murder and carrying a pistol without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters, where the case was transferred to the regular criminal docket; thereafter, the court, Devlin, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss or to transfer the case back to the juvenile docket; subsequently, the murder charge was tried to the jury and the charge of carrying a pistol without a permit was tried to the court; verdict and finding of guilty; subsequently, the court rendered judgment of conviction, from which the defendant appealed to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-127(a), the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, Juvenile Matters (Connecticut) transferred defendant's Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a murder and weapons cases to the regular criminal docket, where his motion to dismiss or to transfer the case back to the juvenile docket was denied. He appealed his conviction on both charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant renewed his Roper claim that the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-35a(2)'s mandatory minimum sentence for murder violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII. He also claimed that his right to a fair trial was violated by the prosecutor's suggestion of a motive for murdering the victim when no motive evidence was presented at trial. The court rejected both claims. Because it was not cruel and unusual punishment to mandate a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of release in the case of a juvenile offender, it was not cruel and unusual punishment to mandate a sentence of not less than 25 years' imprisonment in defendant's case. Even if the court assumed that the prosecutor's argument was improper, any impropriety was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The suggestion that defendant and another person shared a common motive bordered on the speculative because any link between the conduct of the two men was weak at best. No direct evidence supported the argument, and it was debatable whether circumstantial evidence sufficiently warranted the inference of a common motive. Defendant was not deprived of a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Kelly v. Univ. of Conn. Health Ctr.


SC 17884


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 245; 963 A.2d 1; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 9


October 23, 2008, Argued 
January 27, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for, inter alia, the defendant's alleged negligence, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, where the court, Dubay, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Kelly v. Albertsen, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1023 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 27, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sued defendant health center, alleging medical malpractice and lack of informed consent in connection with his surgery. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Middlesex, granted the health center's motion to dismiss. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The health center was an entity operated by the State. The patient claimed that laser fibers were left in his body during a surgery performed at the health center by its employees. The trial court found that the claim was untimely presented under the one year limitation period of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148. The patient argued that, although he learned of the presence of the fibers a year earlier, actionable harm did not occur until he discovered the causal connection between the health center's negligence and the presence of the fibers. The appellate court disagreed. The one year limitation period began to run when the patient discovered the presence of the fibers. Contrary to the patient's argument, his knowledge of injury constituted actionable harm despite the absence of an expert medical opinion. The knowledge of the presence of fibers indicated professional negligence so gross as to be clear even to a lay person. 2005 Conn. Acts 05-4, § 1(a) (Spec. Sess.), which allowed the patient to resubmit his notice of claim despite his untimely filing, was an unconstitutional public emolument because it served no public purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
