State v. Ray


SC 17905


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 24; 961 A.2d 947; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 5


September 16, 2008, Argued 
January 6, 2009, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Superseded by State v. Ray, 290 Conn. 602, 966 A.2d 148, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 27 (Conn., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Informations charging the defendant with five counts of the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, six counts of the crime of possession of narcotics, two counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, three counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project and one count each of the crimes of possession of drug paraphernalia and interfering with an officer, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the court, Hon. William F. Hickey, Jr., judge trial referee; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the charge of interfering with an officer; verdict and judgments of guilty of five counts of the crime of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, six counts of the crime of possession of narcotics, two counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, three counts of the crime of sale of narcotics within 1500 feet of a public housing project and one count of the crime of possession of drug paraphernalia, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in  [***2] part; judgment, directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) acquitted defendant on a charge of interfering with an officer, but found him guilty of multiple drug offenses, including five counts of sale of narcotics by a person who is not drug-dependent, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b). The superior court denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal with as to the § 21a-278(b) charges. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that drug dependency was an affirmative defense, and not an element of the offense or an aggravating factor; therefore, it was not unconstitutional to require defendant to prove drug dependency by a preponderance of the evidence under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b) and 21a-269. In fact, defendant presented overwhelming evidence that he was drug-dependent at the time of the offenses. The trial court applied an improper evidentiary standard in determining whether defendant was drug-dependent, as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-240(18). Although a remand was ordinarily required to apply the correct standard, no reasonable fact finder could have concluded that defendant was not drug-dependent at the time of his discharge from treatment in April, 2001, or that, after years of dependence on drugs, he finally had managed to conquer his addiction at some point during the five months between that date and the date of the first offense. As a matter of law, defendant met his burden of proving that he was a drug-dependent person under § 21a-278(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to the conviction of five counts of sale of narcotics by a person who was not drug-dependent and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render a judgment of acquittal on those charges only and to resentence defendant on the remaining charges; the judgments were affirmed in all other respects.

State v. Gould


SC 18108


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


290 Conn. 70; 961 A.2d 975; 2009 Conn. LEXIS 3


September 16, 2008, Argued 
January 6, 2009, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information, in one case, charging the defendant with the crime of attempt to possess marijuana, and information, in a second case, charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of marijuana with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, possession of marijuana with intent to sell, possession of drug paraphernalia and operating a drug factory, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham, geographical area number eleven, and tried to the jury before Robaina, J.; verdict and judgment of not guilty in the first case; verdict and judgment of guilty in the second case, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession with intent to sell under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) by the Superior Court in the judicial district of Windham (Connecticut). He claimed that the requirement that he prove his drug dependency under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b) and 21a-269 violated his due process rights. He also argued that the prosecutor engaged in impropriety during closing arguments.


OVERVIEW: Postal inspectors employed by the United States Postal Service became suspicious that a package addressed to defendant's uncle at his apartment contained narcotics. After the uncle accepted the package, federal agents entered the residence. The uncle told the task force members that the package belonged to defendant and that he had accepted a package for defendant every two or three weeks. In exchange for that service, defendant gave marijuana to his uncle. Defendant arrived at the apartment and took possession of the package. The task force members then arrested him. When they searched him, they found a cellular telephone and nearly $ 1,000 in cash. Defendant testified that he never had sold any of the marijuana but used it all himself. Defendant claimed that the prosecutor's statements were improper as they were intended to mislead the jury by means of an artfully deceptive argument. The appellate court held prosecutor's reference to "ingenuity of counsel" was improper. However, that impropriety did not deprive defendant of his right to a fair trial as the statement was isolated and was not directed at a critical issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Wrotnowski v. Bysiewicz


SC 18264


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


289 Conn. 522; 958 A.2d 709; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 477


November 3, 2008, Heard 
November 3, 2008, Officially Released * 


* November 3, 2008, the date that this court's order of dismissal was released, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay denied by Wrotnowski v. Bysiewicz, 129 S. Ct. 775, 172 L. Ed. 2d 753, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 9182 (U.S., Dec. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action by the plaintiff for an order directing the defendant to verify information to determine certain qualifications of Barack Obama for the office of president of the United States on the ballot for the national election of November 4, 2008, brought, pursuant to General Statutes § 9-323, to Chase T. Rogers, Chief Justice of the Supreme Court, who conducted a hearing on the complaint and on the defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-323, plaintiff sued defendant secretary of state, alleging that defendant did not verify that the democratic nominee for the office of president of the United States for the 2008 election, was a natural born citizen of the United States as required by the U.S. Const. art. II, § 1. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: In his brief, plaintiff clarified that he sought a writ of mandamus directing defendant to acquire primary documents or certified copies from primary sources to prove that the candidate was a natural born citizen. Plaintiff had not alleged any act or conduct by defendant that interpreted a statute, regulation or other authoritative legal requirement applicable to the election process or identified any mandatory statute that defendant failed to apply or follow. Plaintiff conceded that the election statutes did not require or authorize defendant to verify the constitutional qualifications of a candidate for the office of president of the United States. Plaintiff claimed that the existing election laws governing presidential elections were not adequate to ensure compliance with U.S. Const. art. II, § 1. The court concluded that, under Scheyd, Bortner and Caruso, plaintiff had not made a colorable claim under § 9-323 that he was aggrieved by any ruling of any election official in connection with any election for presidential electors. Therefore, plaintiff lacked statutory standing to bring his complaint, and the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

Dutkiewicz v. Dutkiewicz


SC 18082


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


289 Conn. 362; 957 A.2d 821; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 431


March 18, 2008, Argued 
October 28, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Pinkus, J., denied the defendant's motion for exemption from participation in the court-ordered parenting education program, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Pinkus, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and waiving the parties' participation in the parenting education program; subsequently, the defendant's appeal was transferred to this court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dissolution action, defendant father appealed an order of the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain (Connecticut) that he attend a parenting education program, as authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-69b and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 25-5(a)(6). The father claimed that § 46b-69b was an unconstitutional infringement on his fundamental right to exercise care, control and custody over his child.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother served the father with a complaint seeking the dissolution of their marriage. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 25-5(a)(6), that filing triggered an automatic order requiring the parties to attend a parenting education program. The appellate court held that as the father's claim raised the question of whether § 46b-69b infringed on his fundamental right as a parent to raise his children free from unnecessary governmental interference, the claim raised an issue of public importance and fell under the exception to the mootness doctrine for claims that evaded review. The appellate court held that § 46b-69b did not infringe on his fundamental right to exercise care, custody and control over his child. Nothing in the statute required parents to change the way that they cared for their children. Nothing in the statute authorized the State to deprive parents of control or custody of their children. Moreover, the education program did not involve the children themselves. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-69b was rationally related to a legitimate government purpose, that is, the State's legitimate interest in promoting the welfare of children.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

172 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Kerrigan v. Comm'r of Pub. Health


SC 17716


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


289 Conn. 135; 957 A.2d 407; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 385


May 14, 2007, Argued 
October 28, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 28, 2008. As Corrected November 11, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of a certain state statute utilizing the term "marriage" for the union of couples of the opposite sex and the term "civil union" for the union of same sex couples, for an order compelling the defendants to issue to each plaintiff same sex couple a marriage license, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Pittman, J., denied the plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon in favor of the defendants, from which the plaintiffs appealed.  [***1] 
Kerrigan v. State, 49 Conn. Supp. 644, 909 A.2d 89, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2127 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, eight same-sex couples, commenced an action claiming that the state statutory prohibition against same sex marriage, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-38nn, violated their rights to substantive due process and equal protection under the state constitution. The Connecticut trial court rendered summary judgment in favor of defendants, state and local officials, and the couples appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court concluded that, in light of the history of pernicious discrimination faced by gay men and lesbians, and because the institution of marriage carried with it a status and significance that the classification of civil unions did not embody, the segregation of heterosexual and homosexual couples into separate institutions constituted a cognizable harm. Also, (1) the state scheme discriminated on the basis of sexual orientation, (2) for the same reasons that classifications predicated on gender were considered quasi-suspect for purposes of the equal protection provisions of the U.S. constitution, sexual orientation constituted a quasi-suspect classification for purposes of the equal protection provisions of the state constitution, and, therefore, state statutes discriminating against gay persons were subject to heightened or intermediate judicial scrutiny, and (3) the state failed to provide sufficient justification for excluding same sex couples from the institution of marriage. As the state's disparate treatment of same sex couples was deficient under an intermediate level of scrutiny, the couples' claims implicating a stricter standard of review were not reached.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with direction to grant the couples' motion for summary judgment and application for injunctive relief.

State v. Burroughs


SC 17894


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


288 Conn. 836; 955 A.2d 43; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 355


May 22, 2008, Argued 
September 23, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information, in the first case, charging the defendant with possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of marijuana, and failure to appear in the first degree, and information, in the second case, charging the defendant with criminal impersonation and forgery in the second degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, where the court, Hon. Martin L. Nigro, judge trial referee, denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, in the first case, on a plea of guilty of failure to appear in the first degree and on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to possession of narcotics with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and possession of marijuana, and, in the second case, on a plea of guilty of forgery in the second degree; subsequently, the court rendered judgments in accordance with the defendant's pleas, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Bishop, DiPentima and Hennessy, Js., which reversed in part the judgment in the first case and remanded for further  [***2] proceedings, and which affirmed the judgment in the second case, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. Burroughs, 99 Conn. App. 413, 914 A.2d 592, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 49 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; judgments directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, defendant entered a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charges of possession of narcotics with intent to sell and possession of marijuana. Defendant was sentenced to six years imprisonment and six years of special parole. The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed the trial court's denial of the motion to suppress. The State, on the granting of certification, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue before the appellate court was whether the appellate court properly concluded that defendant was seized within the meaning of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7 and 9, when two uniformed, armed police officers exited their patrol car and approached his vehicle. The State argued that the officer's conduct would not have caused a reasonable person in defendant's position to believe he was not free to leave. The supreme court concluded that there was an insufficient show of police authority before the officers detected the smell of marijuana to establish a seizure under the Connecticut Constitution. The officers were dispatched to investigate an anonymous report of a suspicious vehicle and, upon seeing a vehicle matching the description in the report, the officers parked behind defendant's vehicle. At no time prior to detecting the smell of marijuana did the officers activate their overhead flashing lights, shine spotlights or activate sirens, or direct any verbal commands to defendant. The officer's mere presence did not constitute the requisite show of authority sufficient to cause a reasonable person in defendant's position to believe he was not free to leave.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed only as to that court's reversal of defendant's conviction of possession of narcotics with the intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and of possession of marijuana, and the case was remanded to that court with direction to affirm the judgments of the trial court.

State v. Jenkins


SC 18018


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


288 Conn. 610; 954 A.2d 806; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 331


February 15, 2008, Argued 
September 2, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with sexual as-sault in the first degree, unlawful restraint in the second degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford, geographical area number twenty-two, where the matter was transferred to the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford; thereafter, the court, Holden, J., determined that the defendant was not competent to stand trial but was restorable to competency, and ordered the defendant to be placed for treatment at a mental health facility; subsequently, the court, Ronan, J., determined that the defendant had regained competency; thereafter, the court, Carroll, J., determined that the defendant was not competent to stand trial but was restorable to competency, and ordered the defendant to be placed for treatment at a mental health facility; subsequently, the court, B. Fischer, J., determined that the defendant had regained competency and ordered the defendant to participate in an education program to maintain his competency; thereafter, the state filed a substitute information charging the defendant with sexual assault in the first degree, kidnapping in the first degree and risk  [***2] of injury to a child; subsequently, the defendant entered a plea of not guilty and filed a motion to dismiss the substitute information; thereafter, the court, B. Fischer, J., determined that the defendant was not competent to stand trial, but restorable, and ordered the defendant to comply with an outpatient plan to restore his competency; subsequently, the court denied the defendant's motion to dismiss the information, and the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being found not competent to stand trial, defendant was confined in a mental health facility pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56d(i) for three nonconsecutive periods totaling 21 months. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Ansonia-Milford (Connecticut) rejected his claim that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56d(m) (2005) required a hearing to determine whether he should be released from treatment or civilly committed. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and initially charged with violating Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-70, 53a-96, and § 53-21. Because none of defendant's individual treatment periods restoring him to competency had exceeded 18 months, the trial court denied his request for a release from custody or a hearing pursuant to § 54-56d(m). On appeal, he claimed that the placements had to be treated cumulatively for purposes of applying the 18-month time limitation of § 54-56d(i). The court found that defendant was entitled to appeal from the interlocutory order under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-263 because his claim that the 18-month period of § 54-56d(i) had been exceeded and that he was entitled either to immediate release or to civil commitment proceedings implicated a constitutional due process right, embodied in § 54-56d, already secured to him. The court construed § 54-56d(i) to mean that after a defendant was found incompetent to stand trial but restorable to competency, the cumulative total of the placements for treatment could not exceed the period of the maximum sentence that defendant could receive or 18 months, whichever was less.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded the case for a determination of the relief to which defendant was entitled.

State v. DeJesus


SC 17710, SC 17711


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


288 Conn. 418; 953 A.2d 45; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 308


January 11, 2008, Argued 
August 19, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 16, 2008As Corrected .


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts each of the crimes of sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before Lavine, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Schaller and Peters, Js., which reversed the judgment with respect to the defendant's conviction of one count of kidnapping in the first degree, from which the defendant and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed separately to this court.
State v. DeJesus, 91 Conn. App. 47, 880 A.2d 910, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 380 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate certified appeals, the State challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), which reversed defendant's conviction for kidnapping, claiming that the court improperly concluded that the kidnapping statute was unconstitutionally void for vagueness. Defendant appealed from that part of the judgment affirming his conviction for sexual assault and kidnapping, violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-70(a)(1) and 53a-92(a)(2)(A).


OVERVIEW: The court found that the appellate court should have determined whether the facts concerning a first assault could have supported a kidnapping conviction. The court overruled its conclusion in State v. Sanseverino that there should have been a judgment of acquittal; the proper remedy was a new trial with instructions that, to find defendant guilty of the crime of kidnapping in the first degree, it had to find that he had intended to prevent the victim's liberation for a longer period of time or to a greater degree than that which was necessary to commit the underlying crime. Because defendant could have been convicted on the basis of conduct which, under Salamon, did not violate the kidnapping statute, the kidnapping conviction was properly reversed, but remanded for a new trial. The court declined to consider whether the kidnapping statute was void for vagueness. The admission of prior sexual assault act evidence was not error; the court adopted the liberal admission of prior sexual assault acts to prove that defendant had a propensity or a tendency to sexually assault young women of limited mental ability with whom he worked and over whom he had supervisory authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment that directed a judgment of not guilty of kidnapping in the first degree under count four of the information and remanded the case to that court with direction to remand the case to the trial court for a new trial on that count; the court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

Greater New Haven Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of New Haven


SC 17900


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


288 Conn. 181; 951 A.2d 551; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 295


February 7, 2008, Argued 
July 29, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to declare null and void an ordinance of the defendant city requiring the licensing and inspection of certain residential rental properties, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the plaintiff withdrew its claim for monetary damages and where the court, Pittman, J., denied the defendant's motion to dismiss; thereafter, the case was tried to the court, Silbert, J.; judgment for the defendant, from which the plaintiff appealed.
Greater New Haven Prop. Owners Ass'n v. City of New Haven, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 156 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Haven Superior Court (Connecticut) granted judgment to defendant city after plaintiff association filed an action for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief based on the city's conduct in enacting an ordinance that imposed licensing and inspection requirements upon certain residential rental properties. The association appealed and the state supreme court transferred the case to itself.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(7)(A) allowed municipalities to regulate housing. The city as a result enacted the New Haven, Conn., Code of Ordinances § 17-13.1 et seq., which imposed licensing and inspection requirements upon certain residential rental properties. The association sought relief. The trial court concluded that the city could adopt the ordinance, that the association lacked standing to challenge the city's power to obtain an administrative warrant to compel certain inspections, that the ordinance did not violate the property owners' right to procedural or substantive due process, and that it did not take property without just compensation. The state supreme court found that (1) the statute's broad grant of police power authorized adoption of the ordinance, (2) the association lacked standing to challenge the administrative warrant provision because it lacked a privacy interest in the units, (3) the ordinance did not deprive the property owners of the benefit of a certificate of occupancy and, thus, did not violate procedural or substantive due process rights, and (4) the regulatory requirements imposed did not take any alleged property interest.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Washington v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 18057


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 792; 950 A.2d 1220; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 280


February 5, 2008, Argued 
July 15, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Tolland and tried to the court, Fuger, J.; judgment denying the petition, from which the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed.
Washington v. Warden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2222 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 21, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was sentenced on 4 separate dockets. After the superior court denied the inmate's amended petition for habeas corpus relief, the inmate appealed to the Appellate Court (Connecticut), claiming that Harris, Cox and Hunter (the trilogy) should not have been applied retroactively to recalculate his release date. The court transferred the case pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-1.


OVERVIEW: Concurrent sentences were imposed on the 4 dockets. After the trilogy decisions, respondent Commissioner of Corrections applied the presentence confinement credits to the sentences imposed in dockets 1 and 2 only, rather than on all 4 dockets and established a later discharge date. The inmate claimed that retroactive application of the court's interpretation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-98d in the trilogy violated his due process rights because it acted as an ex post facto law that unconstitutionally lengthened his sentence. The court disagreed. The trilogy did not change the law, but construed the statute based on a legislative intent to change from a system that awarded multiple credit for presentence confinement. The correct application of § 18-98d had been unsettled until the trilogy, and resolution of inconsistent holdings in the trilogy was foreseeable. The Commissioner's recalculation was akin to the correction of a clerical error. In making the correction, the Commissioner did not cause the inmate to suffer harm because he remained rightfully imprisoned. The correction did not violate the inmate's due process or double jeopardy rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

State v. Sanseverino


SC 17786, SC 17787


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 608; 949 A.2d 1156; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 250


October 16, 2007, Argued 
July 1, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Superseded by, in part, Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by, On reconsideration by State v. Sanseverino, 2009 Conn. LEXIS 145 (Conn., May 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with two counts of the crime of sexual assault in the first degree and one count each of the crimes of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree and kidnapping in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, where the court, Espinosa, J., denied the defendant's motion to sever the offenses and for separate trials; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Espinosa, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, Gruendel and Berdon, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case for new separate trials, and, on the granting of certification, the state and the defendant filed separate appeals to this court.
State v. Sanseverino, 98 Conn. App. 198, 907 A.2d 1248, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 445 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; Judgment Directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Connecticut Court of Appeals reversed defendant's convictions for kidnapping in the first degree and sexual assault in the first degree involving one victim, and convictions for sexual assault in the first degree and attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree regarding a second victim. It then remanded the case for new, separate trials. After certification was granted, the State and defendant filed separate appeals.


OVERVIEW: Defendant in separate incidents allegedly sexually assaulted two female bakery workers at the bakery he owned. The two cases were joined for his jury trial. He was then convicted of kidnapping in the first degree, violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-92(a)(2)(A), and sexual assault in the first degree, violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1), for acts against one victim and of sexual assault in the first degree, violating Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(a)(1) and attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, violating Conn. Gen. §§ 53a-49(a)(2) and 53a-70(a)(1), for acts against the second victim. The appellate court held that the trial court had improperly denied his motion to sever. It rejected his vagueness claim regarding the kidnapping statute. The state supreme court found that the cases could be joined because evidence of other acts would have been cross admissible at separate trials to show a common scheme or plan by defendant, making joinder was permissible pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-57 and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-19. However, it reversed the kidnapping conviction after finding the confinement used was merely incidental to the sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment finding severance of the two victims' cases was required. It also ordered remand of the case to the appellate court to reverse to the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of kidnapping in the first degree and to remand the case to the trial court to render a not guilty judgment on that charge, as well as to otherwise affirm the trial court's judgment.

State v. Salamon


SC 17610


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 509; 949 A.2d 1092; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 251


April 17, 2007, Argued 
July 1, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of kidnapping in the second degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree and risk of injury to a child, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Stamford-Norwalk, geographical area number one, and tried to the jury before Comerford, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty by a jury in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Stamford-Norwalk (Connecticut) of one count each of kidnapping in the second degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-94, unlawful restraint in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-95, and risk of injury to a child, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1) (Rev. to 2001). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The kidnapping was based on the restraint that occurred during an assault. Defendant's argued for a reconsideration of the principle stated in the 1977 Luurtsema decision that a conviction for kidnapping could be based on restraint that was merely incidental to the commission of a separate, underlying offense against a victim. The supreme court complied, ruling first that neither stare decisis nor concepts of legislative acquiescence precluded it from doing so. On the merits, the supreme court ruled that its prior construction of § 53a-94 was incorrect and pronounced that to commit a kidnapping in conjunction with another crime, a defendant must have intended to prevent the victim's liberation for a longer period of timer or to a greater degree than that which was necessary to commit the other crime. As there was evidence that still might support defendant's conviction, a new trial by a properly instructed jury was required. While prosecutorial improprieties had occurred during defendant's trial, they did not implicate due process. Finally, while the trial court's instruction on the definition of intent was incomplete, the jury charge in its entirety was not misleading.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed only as to the conviction of kidnapping in the second degree and remanded the case for a new trial on that count. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Rural Water Co. v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


SC 17959


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 282; 947 A.2d 944; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 219


March 18, 2008, Argued 
June 10, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a variance from the town of Ridgefield's zoning regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury and tried to the court, Marano, J.; judgment dismissing the plaintiff's appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed.
Rural Water Co. v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Ridgefield, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2043 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 10, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff water company applied to defendant zoning board of appeals for a variance. The board denied the application. The water company appealed. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Danbury (Connecticut) dismissed the water company's appeal. The water company appealed and the appeal was transferred to the Supreme Court of Connecticut pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-199(c) and Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 65-1.


OVERVIEW: The water company sought a variance in order to build a single family home on a lot that was smaller than the minimum allowed and had been a well lot. A rezoning made the lot nonconforming and the prior owners failed to record the deed before the zoning change. On appeal, the water company contended that the trial court improperly concluded that the board's determination that the water company failed to show the unusual hardship necessary to grant a variance was supported by substantial evidence. The water company presented no expert testimony or evidence to show that the well had to be discontinued due to high radon levels. The water company had no answers to questions regarding whether the water company could take measures to treat the level of radon or whether residents could treat the water themselves. The supreme court also found no merit in the water company's claim that the trial court improperly concluded that the board's denial of its application was not tantamount to a taking without just compensation under the Fifth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 11, noting that the water company failed to show it had been deprived of all beneficial use of the property.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

181 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Gregan v. Koczur


SC 18058


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 145; 947 A.2d 282; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 214


March 10, 2008, Argued 
June 3, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Verified petition seeking, inter alia, custody in favor of the state department of agriculture of certain animals in the defendant's possession that allegedly were neglected and treated cruelly, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, and tried to the court, Hon. Robert J. Hale, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment awarding permanent custody of the animals to the state department of agriculture, and the defendant appealed.
State ex rel. Gregan v. Koczur, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3304 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 31, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State filed an action under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a (2005) against defendant cat owner seeking orders declaring that the cat owner had neglected or cruelly treated certain cats in her possession and vesting permanent custody of the cats with the department of agriculture. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford rendered judgment for the State. The cat owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After receiving three complaints and obtaining a search warrant, an animal control officer went to the cat owner's residence and found 46 cats in the 950 square foot residence and one dead cat in the freezer. Cat feces, vomit, and urine were spread throughout the house and there was not sufficient food for all the cats. The trial court rejected the cat owner's claim that the condition of the house was due to the fact that she had not been able to pick up as usual that morning, as the feces and urine had been there for some time and the clutter was junk or trash. The supreme court rejected the cat owner's claim that the trial court improperly determined that she neglected the cats under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a, as the failure to give proper care or provide proper food to the cats constituted neglectful conduct under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-247(a) and thus, provided a basis for a finding of neglect under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a. The supreme court also rejected the cat owner's vagueness challenge to § 22-329a, noting that a person of ordinary intelligence would have known that confining 46 cats in the conditions found constituted a failure to provide proper care for the cats.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

182 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cook


SC 17995


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


287 Conn. 237; 947 A.2d 307; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 213


January 2, 2008, Argued 
June 3, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Conn. v. Cook, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7892 (U.S., Oct. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of threatening in the second degree, carrying a dangerous weapon and disorderly conduct, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two, where the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal as to the charge of disorderly conduct; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Blawie, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of carrying a dangerous weapon, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, geographical area number two (Connecticut), found defendant guilty of carrying a dangerous weapon in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-206(a) and 53a-3(7). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly failed to instruct the jury that the State was required to prove that defendant's use or threatened use of the table leg constituted a "true threat," that is, a serious expression of an intent to commit an act of unlawful violence against another. The supreme court agreed, concluding that the trial court improperly failed to instruct the jury that it could not find defendant guilty of carrying a dangerous weapon under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53-206 and 53a-3(7) unless it found, on the basis of defendant's conduct or statements, that his alleged threat to use the table leg constituted a true threat and not simply idle talk, banter or some other form of protected expression. The error was not harmless, as a properly instructed jury could have found that a reasonable person in defendant's position would not have foreseen that his statements and actions would be interpreted as a serious expression of an intent to harm but, rather, as mere banter, jest or exaggeration. The supreme court disagreed with defendant's contention that he was entitled to a judgment of acquittal because the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

183 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Small v. Comm'r of Corr.


SC 17803


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 707; 946 A.2d 1203; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 169


October 22, 2007, Argued 
May 6, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Small v. Lantz, 555 U.S. 975, 129 S. Ct. 481, 172 L. Ed. 2d 336, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7829 (2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Appeal dismissed by Small v. Comm'r of Corr., 2013 Conn. App. LEXIS 396 (Conn. App. Ct., July 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the court, Hon. Anthony V. DeMayo, judge trial referee, who, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment denying the petition; thereafter, the court denied the petition for certification to appeal, and the petitioner appealed to the Appellate Court, McLachlan and Dupont, Js., with Harper, J., dissenting, which affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and dismissed the petitioner's appeal in part, and the petitioner, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Small v. Comm'r of Corr., 98 Conn. App. 389, 909 A.2d 533, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 480 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court (Connecticut) affirmed a trial court's denial of petitioner inmate's amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus in part and dismissed the appeal in part. The inmate appealed, claiming ineffective assistance in failing to object to, or to challenge on direct appeal, jury instructions that omitted the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-49 definition of attempt when he was charged with felony murder predicated on attempt to commit robbery.


OVERVIEW: Certification was limited to whether the appellate court properly determined that the inmate was not denied effective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal. The court overruled its decision in Bunkley v. Commissioner of Correction, 222 Conn. 444, 447 n.4, 610 A.2d 598 (1992) to the extent that its analysis of Strickland's prejudice prong was inconsistent with Smith v. Robbins, 528 U.S. 259, 285, 120 S. Ct. 746, 145 L. Ed. 2d 756 (2000). The court applied its new rule and found that there was not a reasonable probability that, if the issue had been brought before the court on direct appeal, the inmate would have prevailed. The return of a guilty verdict on the charge of conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree indicated a finding that the inmate had the requisite intent. The inmate's presence at a victim's house was a substantial step corroborative of criminal intent. Because the State could have met its burden of showing that the omitted instruction was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, there was no reasonable probability that, absent the omitted instruction, the verdict would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

184 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cote


SC 18014


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 603; 945 A.2d 412; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 133; 38 ELR 20109


January 3, 2008, Argued 
April 22, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with one count each of the crimes of storage of hazardous waste without a permit, disposal of hazardous waste without a permit and conspiracy to store and dispose of hazardous waste without a permit, and with two counts of the crime of placing another in imminent danger of death or serious bodily injury by storing and disposing of hazardous waste without a permit, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New London, where the court, Cofield, J., granted the state's motion in limine to preclude certain evidence; thereafter, the matter was tried to the jury before Cofield, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty of one count each of the crimes of storage of hazardous waste without a permit, disposal of hazardous waste without a permit and conspiracy to store and dispose of hazardous waste without a permit, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury in the Superior Court in the judicial District of New London (Connecticut), of storage of hazardous waste without a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-131a(b) (Rev. to 1999), disposal of hazardous waste without a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-131a(b), and conspiracy to store and dispose of hazardous waste without a permit under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48(a) and 22a-131a(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court improperly charged the jury as to the elements of "disposal" and "storage" by using the definitions of those terms provided in the federal Resource Conservation and Recovery Act of 1976, 42 U.S.C.S. § 6901 et seq., rather than those in Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 445, including Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-131a, governing hazardous waste. The supreme court agreed, finding that the legislature intended for the terms as defined in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-115, to apply without exception or qualification to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-131a. The supreme court further held that the error was not harmless, as there was conflicting testimony as to whether the surface on which the sandblast grit containing the hazardous material had been spread was sandy soil or an asphalt-like substance that completely covered the soil. For purposes of remand, the supreme court also addressed defendant's challenge to the exclusion of evidence that the building inspector allegedly told defendant that it was lawful for sandblast grit to be contained on site and concluded that defendant failed to satisfy the mistake of law requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-6(b)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

185 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grant


SC 18005


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 499; 944 A.2d 947; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 135


January 8, 2008, Argued 
April 22, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grant v. Connecticut, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5953 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with the crime of murder, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Blue, J., denied the defendant's motions to suppress certain evidence and for a hearing to challenge the validity and sufficiency of certain evidence contained in a search warrant; thereafter, the court denied the defendant's motion in limine to prevent the state from presenting certain expert testimony; subsequently, the case was tried to the jury before Blue, J.; verdict of guilty; thereafter, the trial court denied the defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial and rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the verdict, from which the defendant appealed to this court.
State v. Grant, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 48 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 3, 2002)
State v. Grant, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 62 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 7, 2002)
State v. Grant, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 241 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 6, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; remanded for correction of clerical errors.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven (Connecticut) convicted defendant on a jury's finding that he was guilty of murder, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. He appealed the denial of his motions to suppress evidence seized as the result of a search warrant, for a Franks hearing, and to suppress statements. He also claimed prosecutorial misconduct during closing arguments.


OVERVIEW: The court found that defendant's Fourth, Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights had not been violated. The affidavit's facts were sufficient for a reasonable mind to believe that the Type O blood at the scene that did not belong to the victim belonged to the perpetrator. The facts also were sufficient for a reasonable mind to weigh the probability of an innocent explanation for the presence of defendant's fingerprint on a tissue box in a car, and to support a belief that an innocent explanation was no more likely than defendant's presence in the car at the time of the murder. A Franks hearing was not required, as the potentially exculpatory facts omitted from the affidavit were not material. Defendant's statements were not the result of an unlawful custodial interrogation. An officer's response to defendant's implicit questions as to the basis for his arrest did not constitute interrogation under Innis. The jury would not necessarily have found that a prosecutor's comment that there was no evidence of an innocent explanation for the fingerprint or DNA evidence was a comment on defendant's failure to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and remanded the case for correction of a clerical error in the information and the judgment file.

State v. Johnson


SC 17939


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 427; 944 A.2d 297; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 129


November 26, 2007, Argued 
April 15, 2008, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Connecticut, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5538 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of attempt to sell narcotics, possession of narcotics with intent to sell, and possession of narcotics, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, geographical area number fifteen, where the court, Cronan, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain tangible evidence; thereafter, the case was tried to the jury before Vitale, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.
State v. Johnson, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1610 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction, rendered after a jury trial in the Connecticut trial court, of one count each of attempted sale of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b) and 53a-49, possession of narcotics with intent to sell in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(a), and possession of narcotics in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a). The supreme transferred the case from the Appellate Court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the police lacked probable cause to arrest him without a warrant moments after he drove into a parking lot, and that the search of his person and vehicle and the discovery of narcotics and other items of evidentiary interest incident to this arrest violated his rights under U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV. The supreme court found police had probable cause to believe that narcotics would be found either on defendant's person or in his vehicle upon his arrival at the parking lot. Accordingly, the search and seizure of defendant did not violate his constitutional rights, and defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. An informant's telephone calls to defendant in an officer's presence, in addition to the informant's choice of a location that the two had used previously, constituted "firsthand information" supporting an inference of the informant's basis of knowledge. The trial court's instructions to the jury prior to closing arguments did not unconstitutionally restrict his right to an effective closing argument. None of the cases cited by defendant supported the proposition that his claim was one of constitutional magnitude.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. T.R.D.


SC 17865


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 191; 942 A.2d 1000; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 96


September 7, 2007, Argued 
March 25, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crime of failure to comply with the sexual offender registration requirements, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four, and tried to the jury before O'Keefe, J.; verdict and judgment of guilty, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of failing to register as a sex offender in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-251 (Rev. to 2003) and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-257. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Waterbury, geographical area number four (Connecticut) sentenced defendant to three years imprisonment, execution suspended after one year, and five years probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that his waiver of counsel should not have been found knowing and intelligent because the trial court failed to inform him of the range of possible penalties he would face upon conviction. The supreme court concluded that the trial court's failure to conduct an adequate canvass to ensure that defendant's waiver of the right to counsel was made knowingly and intelligently constituted an abuse of discretion and, accordingly, required defendant be granted a new trial. The supreme court went on to address two of defendant's other arguments, as they were likely to arise upon retrial. As for defendant's contention that he was deprived of due process when he was arrested before the State took reasonable steps to contact him after he failed to return the verifications forms, the supreme court agreed with the State that defendant received full due process of law, having been formally apprised of his registration responsibilities, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-256. The supreme court also found no error in the jury instructions given as, inter alia, no instruction on mens rea was necessary since failure to register as a sex offender was a strict liability offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. Defendant was granted a new trial.

State v. Betts


SC 17994


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


286 Conn. 88; 942 A.2d 364; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 88


January 4, 2008, Argued 
March 18, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Information charging the defendant with four counts of the crime of risk of injury to a child, and with one count each of the crimes of attempt to commit sexual assault in the first degree, sexual assault in the third degree, assault in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree and interfering with an emergency call, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the jury before McMahon, J.; after the court denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence, verdict and judgment of guilty of three counts of risk of injury to a child and one count each of sexual assault in the third degree, assault in the third degree, unlawful restraint in the first degree and interfering with an emergency call, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), which convicted him of risk of injury to a child, sexual assault, assault, unlawful restraint, and interfering with an emergency call. He claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress, arguing that the victim's mother was an agent of the police for purposes of the Fourth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 7.


OVERVIEW: The mother, who was defendant's fiancee, caught defendant lying on top of the victim. She attempted to call the police, but defendant began choking and beating her. The victim gave the mother a letter that defendant wrote, expressing his sexual desire for the victim. Defendant took the letter and hid it in the bedroom he and the mother shared. When the police arrived the mother gave the letter to an officer. The supreme court held that the mother's search of the bedroom did not implicate federal or state constitutional protections because the mother was not an agent of the police when she retrieved the letter. Substantial evidence supported the conclusion that the mother was not an agent of the police. Therefore, her actions did not constitute a police search. The police did not place the mother in a position to find the incriminating letter. She received it from the victim before defendant took it. The officer learned about the letter from her conversation with the victim and then asked the mother whether she could find it. There was no evidence that the police offered the mother any kind of reward, and the mother's initial contact with the police was self-motivated.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

189 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kinney v. State


SC 18020


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 700; 941 A.2d 907; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 73


January 10, 2008, Argued 
March 4, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to recover damages for the defendant's alleged negligence in causing the death of the plaintiff's decedent as a result of work induced stress, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven, where the court, Robaina, J., granted the defendant's motion for summary judgment and rendered judgment thereon, and the plaintiff appealed.
Kinney v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2560 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 16, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix challenged an order of the Superior Court in the Judicial District of New Haven (Connecticut), which granted defendant State summary judgment in her action alleging that the State's negligence contributed to a decedent's death. The trial court found that 1994 Conn. Acts 94-13, § 1 (Spec. Sess.) could not extend the time in which her claim against the State could be presented under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a)


OVERVIEW: The decedent had been a superior court judge. Eight years after his death, the administratrix filed a claim with the State claims commissioner, seeking permission to sue the State for negligence. She had been authorized to file the otherwise untimely claim pursuant to 1994 Conn. Acts 94-13, § 1 (Spec. Sess.). The commissioner denied the administratrix permission to file an action against the State, but the legislature authorized her to sue the State. The State filed a motion for summary judgment on the ground that the special act violated Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The supreme court held that the trial court properly granted the State summary judgment. 1994 Conn. Acts 94-13, § 1 (Spec. Sess.) conferred an exclusive public emolument on the administratrix and violated Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The special act granted to the administratrix alone a personal right that was not generally available to others similarly situated. It benefited no member of the public other than the administratrix and remedied a procedural default arising from her failure to file a claim with the commissioner within three years from the date of the decedent's death pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148 (a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

190 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. John F.M.


SC 17677


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 528; 940 A.2d 755; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 51


September 20, 2007, Argued 
February 19, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Substitute information charging the defendant with the crimes of sexual assault in the second degree and sexual assault in the third degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Haven and tried to the jury before Hon. Ronald J. Fracasse, judge trial referee; thereafter, the court granted the defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal of sexual assault in the second degree; verdict and judgment of guilty of sexual assault in the third degree, from which the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, Lavery, C. J., and Schaller and Harper, Js., which reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with direction to render judgment of not guilty, and the state, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
State v. John M., 94 Conn. App. 667, 894 A.2d 376, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 144 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-72a(a)(2). The Appellate Court (Connecticut) reversed his conviction on the grounds that the evidence was insufficient to establish that defendant was the victim's stepfather and that § 53a-72a(a)(2) violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Federal Constitution. The State's petition for certification to appeal was granted.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. The jury reasonably found that defendant and the victim had a stepfather-stepdaughter relationship. The State introduced into evidence defendant's admission that at the time of the sexual assault, he was legally married to the victim's mother. The appellate court improperly relied on the Roswell decision to conclude that the State's failure to produce documentary evidence concerning the victim's parentage rendered the State's evidence legally insufficient. Roswell had been overruled sub silentio by subsequent supreme court cases. Therefore, defendant's admissions were admissible and sufficient, although not conclusive, evidence of a legal and valid familial relationship. Section 53a-72a(a)(2) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because it applied equally to sexual intercourse between persons of both the opposite sex and the same sex who were related within certain degrees of kindred. Section 53a-72a(a)(2) incorporated only the proximity of relation specified therein and did not incorporate the precise male-female unions enumerated in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-21.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the appellate court with direction to consider defendant's remaining claims.
