Cambodian Buddhist Soc'y of Conn., Inc. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


SC 17690


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 381; 941 A.2d 868; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 41


March 6, 2007, Argued 
February 12, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the defendant planning and zoning commission denying the named plaintiff's application for a special exception to construct, inter alia, a building for religious worship, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, J. R. Downey, J., granted the motion filed by Richard T. Coburn et al. to intervene as defendants; thereafter, the action was dismissed as to the plaintiff Pong Me; subsequently, the court granted in part the motion to strike filed by the defendant planning and zoning commission; thereafter, the matter was tried to the court, Frankel, J.; judgment denying the appeal, from which the plaintiffs appealed.
Cambodian Buddhist Soc'y of Ct., Inc. v. Newtown Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3158 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 18, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a religious society and its president, appealed a decision of defendant planning and zoning commission denying the society's application for a special exception to build a temple on its property. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) denied the president's appeal for lack of standing and denied the society's appeal on the merits. The society and the president appealed.


OVERVIEW: The president lacked standing to challenge the commission's decision. The society argued that the commission's decision to deny the society's application for a special exception was not supported by the record and violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-571b and the federal Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act of 2000, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc et seq. The supreme court concluded, inter alia, that the trial court correctly found that the record did not contain substantial evidence to support the commission's conclusion that the society's application should be denied because the design of the temple was not in harmony with the design of other buildings in the vicinity and the temple would create unacceptable traffic congestion and hazards. However, the record contained substantial evidence to support the commission's denial of the society's application on the grounds that the level of activity at the proposed temple would not be in harmony with the general character of the neighborhood, that the temple would substantially impair neighboring property values, and that the proposed septic wastewater and water supply systems would create a health or safety hazard.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

192 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kalphat


SC 17932


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 367; 939 A.2d 1165; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 26


October 18, 2007, Argued 
February 5, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Amended information charging the defendant with the crimes of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, possession of marijuana with intent to sell, possession of more than four ounces of marijuana, conspiracy to commit those crimes, and failure to appear in the first degree, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield, where the court, Hauser, J., denied the defendant's motion to suppress certain evidence; thereafter, the defendant was presented to the court, Fasano, J., on a conditional plea of nolo contendere to the charges of possession of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent and conspiracy, and on a plea of guilty to the charge of failure to appear in the first degree; subsequently, the court, Comerford, J., rendered judgment of guilty in accordance with the pleas, from which the defendant appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, the Superior Court in the judicial district of Fairfield (Connecticut) accepted defendant's conditional nolo contendere plea to charges of possession of one kilogram or more of marijuana with intent to sell by a person who is not drug-dependent, conspiracy to possess marijuana, and failure to appear in the first degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress certain evidence that had been obtained by the police as the result of a warrantless search in violation of his rights under the Fourth Amendment on the ground that defendant lacked standing to raise a claim under those constitutional provisions. Defendant argued that he had a reasonable expectation of privacy in packages delivered by a private freight carrier, that the carrier's employees were acting as agents of the state when they opened the box and that, even if the initial opening of the box was a private search that was not subject to the Fourth Amendment, the police officers were required to obtain a warrant before expanding the scope of the private search by opening the box completely. Although the supreme court agreed that a person may assert a reasonable expectation of privacy in packages addressed to them under an alias, defendant failed to present evidence to show that the addressee of the boxes was his alias rather than a real person. In addition, because defendant was not in possession of the boxes he was not a bailee of the boxes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

193 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Andross v. Town of W. Hartford


SC 17742


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 309; 939 A.2d 1146; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 13


September 17, 2007, Argued 
January 29, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action to enjoin the named defendant from conveying a parcel of real property to the defendant Ginsburg Development CT, LLC, and to enjoin the construction of a condominium complex on that property and the construction of a pharmacy on other property in violation of a town ordinance adopted to promote long-term development for the social and economic benefit of the residents of a certain neighborhood of the town of West Hartford, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Beach, J., granted the defendants' motions to dismiss with respect to the parcel for the pharmacy project; thereafter, Hon. Mary R. Hennessey, judge trial referee, granted the defendants' motions to dismiss with respect to the parcel for the condominium complex and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment for the defendants dismissing the plaintiffs' complaint, and the plaintiffs appealed.
Andross v. Town of W. Hartford, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 646 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 1, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town residents appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) granting the motions of defendants, a town, four town officials and three private development firms, to dismiss residents' action, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, for lack of standing and, hence, subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The residents contended that the trial court improperly applied an aggrievement analysis that had no application outside of administrative appeals, under which the trial court required them to demonstrate an injury different from that sustained by the community as a whole. Rather, they contended they only prove that they suffered an injury in fact that fell within the zone of interest of the laws claimed to have been violated. The supreme court concluded the trial court properly dismissed the residents' action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because, inter alia, the allegations that the development of the condominium and pharmacy violated the neighborhood ordinance raised claims that fell within the scope of authority of the town's plan and zoning commission. In addition, the claimed injuries arising from the conveyance of the public park land were not sufficient to constitute a cognizable basis for standing, as the complaint failed to allege any direct injury to aesthetic or recreational interests. The supreme court further declined to extend the automatic standing rule to allow any citizen to bring an action to challenge any decision implicating urban sprawl.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

194 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


R.C. Equity Group, LLC v. Zoning Comm'n


SC 17676


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 240; 939 A.2d 1122; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 9


April 9, 2007, Argued 
January 22, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from the decision of the defendant zoning commission to adopt zoning regulations, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury, where the court, Schuman, J., granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and rendered judgment thereon dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed.
R.C. Equity Group, LLC v. Zoning Comm'n of Newtown, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 321 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 31, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant zoning commission adopted zoning regulations, which plaintiff land owner appealed. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Danbury (Connecticut) dismissed the appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction in that the owner did not comply with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b) and (f)(2). On the granting of certification, the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner claimed that the failure of service was subject to the savings provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(q). The supreme court disagreed. Although the summons contained a generic citation directing a marshal to make service, the form that the owner's attorney signed and provided to the marshal for service contained no instruction directing the marshal to serve the borough clerk as § 8-8(f)(2) required. The marshal's affidavit stated that he knew that the requirements for service of process had changed from serving one copy on the clerk and one copy on the chairman, he did not think about the new requirement, and he had no excuse for not complying. However, as a matter of law, § 8-8(q) did not save the appeal. The marshal's failure to serve a borough clerk did not constitute default or neglect within the meaning of § 8-8(q). The marshal was not required to make a determination that a citation was legally insufficient when it appeared to be legal on its face. To require him to do otherwise would violate Conn. Agencies Regs. § 6-38b-6(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

195 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fish v. Fish


SC 17500


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


285 Conn. 24; 939 A.2d 1040; 2008 Conn. LEXIS 4


September 18, 2006, Argued 
January 15, 2008, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for the dissolution of a marriage, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford-New Britain at Hartford and tried to the court, Rubinow, J.; judgment dissolving the marriage and granting certain other relief; thereafter, the defendant filed a motion to modify custody; subsequently, the court, Prestley, J., granted the motions to intervene filed by Barbara Husaluk et al.; thereafter, the court issued an order modifying custody, and the defendant appealed to the Appellate Court, DiPentima, McLachlan and Foti, Js., which reversed in part the trial court's judgment, and the defendant, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Fish v. Fish, 90 Conn. App. 744, 881 A.2d 342, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 364 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a post-dissolution matter, defendant father challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court (Connecticut), affirming a trial court order modifying an original custody order by awarding joint custody to plaintiff mother and intervenor, the parties' child's aunt, and directing that the primary residence be with the aunt. The Appellate Court also found the trial court abused its discretion in ordering the allocation of tax dependency exemptions.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether a third party could satisfy the jurisdictional pleading requirements and burden of persuasion articulated in Roth v. Weston when seeking the custody of a minor child over the objection of a fit parent. The supreme court agreed with the father that third party custody decisions (which presented different issues from those in visitation proceedings) required the application of a standard more demanding than the best interests of the child. However, the burden in Roth could not be applied to the relevant third party custody statutes (Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-56(a), 46b-57, 46b-56b). The proper standard of proof was a fair preponderance of the evidence, because it comported with due process and the requirement of "fundamental fairness" described in Santosky v. Kramer. The trial court failed to apply the correct standard when it granted the aunt's motion to intervene and awarded her custody. Thereafter, the Appellate Court properly rejected the father's claim that the trial court should have awarded custody on the basis of the standard articulated in Roth but improperly affirmed the award of custody to the aunt on the ground that it was in the child's best interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the Appellate Court was affirmed insofar as it reversed the trial court's judgment as to the allocation of tax dependency exemptions; the judgment was reversed in all other respects and the case was remanded to that court with direction to reverse the trial court's judgment and to remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings according to law.

 

196 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law


SC 17892


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


284 Conn. 701; 937 A.2d 675; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 509


October 15, 2007, Argued 
December 18, 2007, Officially Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal from a decision by the defendant denying the plaintiff's application for a refund of state sales taxes it had paid to consumers when it repurchased their motor vehicles as required under the state lemon law, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of New Britain, Tax Session, where Hon. Arnold W. Aronson, judge trial referee, granted the defendant's motion to dismiss and, exercising the powers of the Superior Court, rendered judgment thereon dismissing the appeal, from which the plaintiff appealed.
DaimlerChrysler Corp. v. Law, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3191 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 25, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New Britain Superior Court, Tax Session (Connecticut), granted defendant state revenue services commissioner's motion to dismiss plaintiff car manufacturer's appeal of the commissioner's denial of its application for a state sales tax refund. The car manufacturer had paid the refund to buyers when it repurchased their vehicles, as required under the state lemon law. The car manufacturer's appeal was transferred to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: A car manufacturer refunded state sales tax to certain consumers when it accepted for return their motor vehicles pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179(d), known as the state's lemon law. That law required that the manufacturer refund the vehicle's contract price plus all collateral charges, including the sales tax paid by the consumer. The car manufacturer thereafter applied to the commissioner for a refund of the state sales tax it had paid pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179(d). The commissioner denied the application. The trial court dismissed the car manufacturer's subsequent appeal. The state supreme court found that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-422, the car manufacturer was not an aggrieved taxpayer who could file a refund claim with the commissioner. It also found that the state had not waived its sovereign immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-179(d) because the commissioner was not required to reimburse the car manufacturer under that statute. It further found that the car manufacturer had not obtained the required Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq. permission through the office of the claims commissioner to pursue its claims for money damages against the state.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

197 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


C. R. Klewin Northeast, LLC v. Fleming


SC 17779


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


284 Conn. 250; 932 A.2d 1053; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 434


September 4, 2007, Argued 
October 23, 2007, Officially Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at C.R. Klewin Northeast, LLC v. State, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 13 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Application for a writ of mandamus to compel the defendants to implement the terms of a settlement agreement negotiated by the plaintiff and the department of public works for the payment for labor and services provided by the plaintiff on a certain public works project, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford, where the court, Shortall, J., denied the defendants' motion to dismiss and their motion to strike the complaint; thereafter, the court granted the plaintiff's motion for summary judgment, denied the defendants' motion for summary judgment and rendered summary judgment in favor of the plaintiff, and the defendants appealed.
Northeast v. Fleming, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1122 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 18, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; judgment directed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor filed an action for a writ of mandamus against defendants, the state comptroller and other officials. The Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut) ordered defendants to pay $1.2 million to plaintiff under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3-7(c). Defendants appealed, arguing that the trial court improperly denied their motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction based on sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: During the course of performance of a construction contract, disputes arose over extra costs. The parties reached a settlement, but plaintiff never received payment of the settlement amount. Plaintiff argued that defendants were not entitled to sovereign immunity because § 3-7(c) required the officials to effect payment in the amount agreed upon in settlement of the claim once the governor had authorized that payment. In failing to do so, plaintiffs argued, they had acted in contravention of their authority under the statute. Reading the statute as a whole and considering its legislative history, the court held that § 3-7(c) did not create a mandatory duty to pay a claimant. It created a chain of command to obtain proper authority to resolve a dispute. When a legislative provision was designed to secure order, system, and dispatch in the proceedings, it was generally held to be discretionary. The governor's certification of the amount to be paid conferred the power to settle on an official, and then set the limits of that authorization. The legislature did not intend for this authorization to create a mandatory duty in an official to pay a settlement of a disputed claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment. It remanded the case with direction to render judgment dismissing the action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Gonzalez v. Surgeon


SC 17969


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


284 Conn. 573; 937 A.2d 24; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 493


September 19, 2007, Argued 
September 19, 2007 *, Officially Released


* September 19, 2007, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Full-text opinion released on December 11, 2007


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for a judgment declaring that certain petitions circulated for the named plaintiff so that she could be qualified as a Democratic candidate for the office of the mayor of the city of Hartford should not be invalidated, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Graham, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the named plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the appeal was transferred to this court, which granted the named plaintiff's motion for an expedited appeal.
Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 145, 931 A.2d 835, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 376 (2007)
Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2356 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the candidate and the petition circulators, sued appellees, the registrar of voters and the town clerk, in the Superior Court in the Judicial District of Hartford (Connecticut), claiming that the registrar improperly rejected, under Conn. Gen. Stat § 9-410(c), petitions to secure the candidate's name on a primary ballot. The court rendered judgment for the registrar and the clerk. The candidate and the petition circulators appealed.


OVERVIEW: The registrar of voters rejected some of the petitions submitted on the candidate's behalf for the placement of the candidate's name on a primary ballot. The registrar then determined that the candidate had not obtained enough signatures on valid petitions to qualify for the ballot. The candidate claimed that (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was void for vagueness; and that (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was an unconstitutional restriction of free speech and associational rights. On appeal, the court found that, because the meaning of the challenged portion of § 9-410(c) was clear from the statute's purpose, practical application, and legislative history, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. Moreover, because § 9-410(c) made no distinction between bona fide candidates and placeholder candidates, it necessarily referred to any candidate. Finally, the provision of § 9-410(c) that no person was to circulate petitions for more than the maximum number of candidates to be nominated by a party for the same office or position did not violate the right to free speech or association under U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gonzalez v. Surgeon


SC 17968


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


284 Conn. 554; 937 A.2d 13; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 494


September 19, 2007, Argued 
September 19, 2007 *, Officially Released


* September 19, 2007, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Full-text opinion released on December 11, 2007


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for a judgment declaring that certain petitions circulated for the named plaintiff so that she could be qualified as a Democratic candidate for the office of the mayor of the city of Hartford should not be invalidated, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Graham, J.; judgment for the defendants, from which the named plaintiff, on the granting of certification, appealed to this court.
Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 141, 931 A.2d 833, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 377 (2007)
Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2356 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate, and others, sued defendant registrar, and others, claiming, inter alia, that, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c), the registrar improperly rejected certain petitions required to secure the candidate's name on the mayoral primary ballot. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) entered judgment for the registrar, and certified questions to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Upon discovering that several persons who circulated petitions for the candidate also had circulated and submitted petitions for a challenge slate, which included a mayoral office seeker, the registrar rejected the petitions submitted by these circulators pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c). The candidate claimed that this was improper, and argued that because it was only when the circulators began circulating petitions for the challenge slate that the statute was violated, the registrar should have rejected only the petitions for the challenge slate. The appellate court disagreed. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was ambiguous, but it was reasonable to conclude that the legislature intended that the registrar would reject all of the petitions circulated by any one person as a disincentive to actions intended to siphon votes. The appellate court also rejected the candidate's claim that, because the challenge slate's mayoral office seeker was merely a placeholder, § 9-410(c) was not violated. The trial court properly held that the registrar must presume that all office seekers were bona fide and must treat all petitions filed on their behalf the same for the purposes of § 9-410(c).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gonzalez v. Surgeon


SC 17969


SUPREME COURT OF CONNECTICUT


284 Conn. 145; 931 A.2d 835; 2007 Conn. LEXIS 376


September 19, 2007, Argued 
September 19, 2007 *, Officially Released


* September 19, 2007, the date that this decision was released as a slip opinion, is the operative date for all substantive and procedural purposes.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in full at Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 284 Conn. 573, 937 A.2d 24, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 493 (Conn., Sept. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Action for a judgment declaring that certain petitions circulated for the named plaintiff so that she could be qualified as a Democratic candidate for the office of the mayor of the city of Hartford should not be invalidated, and for other relief, brought to the Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford and tried to the court, Graham, J.; thereafter, the case was tried to the court; judgment for the defendants, from which the named plaintiff appealed to the Appellate Court; subsequently, the appeal was transferred to this court, which granted the named plaintiff's motion for an expedited appeal.
Gonzalez v. Surgeon, 2007 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2356 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 29, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate brought an action alleging that defendant registrar had improperly invalidated, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c), certain petitions required to secure the candidate's name on the ballot for a primary for a mayor. The Superior Court in the judicial district of Hartford (Connecticut) entered judgment for the registrar. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The candidate claimed that the trial court improperly determined that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was not void for vagueness under the Due Process Clause of the Fifth Amendment and that § 9-410(c) did not constitute an unconstitutional restriction of free speech and associational rights under the First Amendment, the Fourteenth Amendment, and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 4, 5, 10, 14. The appellate court disagreed. The trial court properly determined that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410(c) was not unconstitutionally vague and did not violate free speech or associational rights under the federal or state constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
